Handing Deposit to Wife Despite Prohibition
Ruling on depositary handing deposit to wife despite prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a depositary violating a condition of the deposit when necessity requires, and distinguish between indispensable and avoidable situations.

Core Idea
A depositary is not liable for violating a condition if observing it makes performance impossible; otherwise, liability attaches.

This lesson examines a nuanced Hanafi ruling on deposits. The owner may impose conditions on how the deposit is handled, but not all conditions are binding. Al-Hidayah presents a scenario where the owner forbids handing the deposit to the depositary's wife, yet necessity may override the condition. The passage from al-Jami' al-Saghir refines the ruling by considering whether the depositary can fulfill his duty without involving the prohibited person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
State the ruling from al-Quduri: if the owner forbids giving the deposit to the wife, and the depositary does so, he is not liable.
This is the starting point, but it is general.
2
Note the conditional refinement
From al-Jami' al-Saghir: the ruling depends on whether the depositary can manage without the prohibited person. If indispensably needed (la budda minhu), no liability; if avoidable, liability.
The examples illustrate the condition.
3
Examine the examples
Horse deposit forbidding groom: depositary cannot care for horse alone, so condition void. Women's item forbidding wife: custom requires women's care, condition void. Otherwise liable.
The examples clarify 'indispensable'.
4
Understand the legal reasoning
A condition that makes performance impossible is void (laghw) even if beneficial; a feasible beneficial condition is binding. The benefit is to protect the deposit from untrustworthy persons.
Reasoning based on practicality and owner's interest.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
This nuanced position from al-Jami' al-Saghir is the operative ruling in the Hanafi school.
It balances necessity and owner's right to impose conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا قَالَ صَاحِبُ الْوَدِيْعَةِ الْمُوْدَعَ لَا تُسَلَّمُهَا إِلَى زَوْجَتِكَ فَسَلَّمَهَا إِلَيْهَا لَا يَضْمَنُ وَفِي الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيْرِ إِذَا نَهَاهُ أَنْ يَدْفَعَهَا إِلَى أَحَدٍ مِنْ عَمَالِهِ فَدَفَعَهَا إِلَى مَنْ لَا بُدَّ مِنْهُ لَا يَضْمَنُ كَمَا إِذَا كَانَتِ الْوَدِيْعَةُ دَابَّةٌ فَنَهَاهُ عَنِ الدَّفْعِ إِلى غُلَامِهِ وَكَمَا إِذَا كَانَتْ شَيْئًا يُحْفَظُ عَلَى يَدِ النِّسَاءِ فَنَهَاهُ عَنِ الدَّفع إلَى امْرَأتِهِ وَهُوَ مَحْمَلا لأنَّهُ لَا يُمْكِنُ إِقَامَةُ الْعَمَلِ مَعَ مُرَاعَاةِ هَذَا الشَّرْطِ وَإِنْ كَانَ مُفِيدًا فَيَلْغُوا وَإِنْ كَانَ لَهُ مِنْهُ بُدّ ضَمِنَ الشَّرْطَ مُفِيدٌ فَإِنَّ مِنَ الْعَيَالِ مَنْ لَا يُؤْتَمَنْ عَلَى الْمَالِ وَقَدْ اَمْكَنَ الْعَمَلُ بِهِ مَعَ مُرَاعَاةِ هَذَا الشَّرْطِ فَاعْتُبِرَ
And if the owner of the deposit said to the depositary: 'Do not hand it over to your wife,' and he handed it over to her, he is not liable. In al-Jami' al-Saghir: If he forbade him from handing it to any of his household, and he handed it to someone from whom there is no escape (i.e., indispensably needed), he is not liable. For example, if the deposit was a riding animal and he forbade him from handing it to his slave, and similarly if it was something that is customarily kept by women and he forbade him from handing it to his wife. This is the application because it is not possible to carry out the task while observing this condition, even if it is beneficial; so it becomes void. But if he could do without him, he is liable because the condition is beneficial. For among the household there are those who cannot be trusted with money, and it is possible to act while observing this condition, so it is considered.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where the owner of a deposit explicitly prohibits the depositary from handing the deposit to a specific person (e.g., his wife or a particular household member). The ruling distinguishes based on necessity. The primary ruling from al-Quduri (as cited in al-Hidayah) states that if the depositary hands the deposit to his wife despite the prohibition, he is not liable. However, this is a general statement. The commentary from al-Jami' al-Saghir provides the condition: if the depositary cannot fulfill his custodial duties without involving that person (e.g., a horse needs a groom, or an item customarily kept by women requires a woman's care), then the prohibition is rendered void (laghw) because observing it would make the task impossible. In such a case, the depositary is not liable. On the other hand, if the depositary could have managed without handing over (e.g., a ring he can keep on his person), then violating the prohibition makes him liable, because the condition is beneficial (mufid) and it is possible to observe it. The benefit is that some household members are untrustworthy. Thus, the ruling is conditional: liability depends on whether observance of the condition is feasible without compromising the deposit's care.

Key Terms
لا بد منه (la budda minhu): Indispensable; someone whose involvement is necessary for the proper care of the deposit.
لغو (laghw): Void or ineffective; a condition that cannot be observed without harming the purpose is rendered void.
مفيد (mufid): Beneficial; a condition that serves a legitimate purpose (e.g., protecting the deposit from untrustworthy persons).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does handing over a deposit to a forbidden person NOT result in liability?
A) When the depositary has no other choice and the person is indispensable.
B) When the forbidden person is a family member.
C) When the deposit is of low value.
D) When the owner did not explicitly forbid it.

Key Takeaway
A depositary is not liable for violating a condition if observing it makes performance impossible; otherwise, liability attaches.

Storage Location Conditions: When Does a Condition Become Binding?
Ruling on liability for violating a non-beneficial location condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of mufid (beneficial condition) to determine whether a depositary is liable for storing a deposit in a different location than specified.

Core Idea
A condition on storage location is binding only if it is beneficial—the alternative location is less secure.

In wadi'ah (deposit contracts), the depositor may impose conditions to protect the deposit, but not every condition is enforceable. The Hanafi school evaluates whether the condition is mufid—that is, does it actually affect the security (hirz) of the deposit? This passage from al-Hidayah illustrates the rule with examples of rooms and houses, showing that liability for deviation depends on the relative security of the chosen location.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and the deviation
What exactly did the owner require? Where did the depositary actually store the deposit? For example, the owner says 'keep it in this room' and the depositary puts it in another room or a different house.
2
Assess the security (hirz) difference between locations
Compare the two locations: are they equally secure or is one clearly more vulnerable? Two rooms in the same house are generally equal; two houses may differ. If the difference is obvious (e.g., a room with a broken wall), even two rooms can differ.
Hirz is relative and determined by custom.
3
Determine if the condition is mufid (beneficial) or ghayr mufid
If the two locations are equally secure, the condition is not beneficial; it is ghayr mufid. If the location specified by the owner is significantly more secure, the condition is mufid.
4
Conclude on liability (daman)
If the condition is ghayr mufid, the depositary is not liable for storing elsewhere. If the condition is mufid, the depositary is liable for violating it.
The contract itself remains valid; only liability is affected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ قَالَ اِحْفَظْهَا فِي هَذَا الْبَيْتِ فَحَفِظَهَا فِي بَيْتِ آخَرَ مِنَ الدَّارِ لَمْ يَضْمَنُ لِاَنَّ الشَّرْطَ غَيْرُ مُفِيدٍ فَإِنَّ الْبَيْتَيْنِ فِي دَارٍ وَاحِدَةٍ لَا يَتَفَاوَتَانِ فِي الْحِرْزِ وَإِنْ حَفِظَهَا فِي دَارٍ أُخْرَى ضَمِنَ لأَنَّ الدَّارَيْنِ تَتَفَاوَتَانِ فِي الْحِرْزِ فَكَانَ مُفيدًا فَيَصِحُ التَّقْسِيدُ وَلَوْ كَانَ التَّفَاوَتُ بَيْنَ الْبَيْتَيْنِ ظَاهِرًا بِأَنْ كَانَتِ الدَّارُ الَّتِي فِيْهَا الْبَيْتَانِ عَظِيمَةً وَالْبَيْتُ الَّذِي نَهَاهُ عَنِ الْحِفْظِ فِيهِ عَوْرَةً ظَاهِرَةً صَحَ الشَّرْطُ
And if he said: 'Keep it in this room,' and he kept it in another room of the same house, he is not liable, because the condition is not beneficial; for two rooms in one house do not differ in security. And if he kept it in another house, he is liable, because two houses differ in security, so the condition is beneficial, and the restriction is valid. And if the difference between the two rooms is apparent, such that the house containing the two rooms is large and the room he forbade keeping it in has an obvious vulnerable point, then the condition is valid.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage deals with the validity of a condition imposed by the depositor regarding the specific location where the deposit must be kept. The general principle is that the depositary must follow the owner's instructions regarding storage location, but if the condition is not beneficial (ghayr mufid), violating it does not create liability. The passage gives concrete examples: if the owner says 'keep it in this room' and the depositary puts it in another room of the same house, he is not liable because both rooms are within the same house and offer essentially the same level of security (hirz). Therefore, the condition is not beneficial and becomes void. However, if the depositary moves the deposit to a different house entirely, he becomes liable because houses can differ significantly in security, so the condition is beneficial and must be observed. An exception arises when the two rooms are in a very large house and the forbidden room has a clear vulnerability (e.g., a broken wall or weak door). In that case, even within the same house, the condition is beneficial because the security differs, so the condition is valid, and violation makes the depositary liable. This ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) rather than qiyas, because strict analogy would hold that any deviation from the owner's instructions creates liability. The underlying rationale is that the owner's condition is only binding if it serves a real purpose in protecting the deposit.

Key Terms
الحرز (al-hirz): A secure place for safekeeping; the level of protection against theft or damage.
مفيد (mufid): Beneficial; a condition that has a meaningful impact on the safety or preservation of the deposit.
قيد (qayd): A restriction or condition imposed by the owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A depositor asks the depositary to keep a valuable necklace in a specific room. The depositary puts it in another room in the same house. Both rooms are equally secure. Is the depositary liable?
A) Yes, because he disobeyed the owner's instruction.
B) Yes, but only if the necklace is stolen.
C) No, because both rooms in the same house have equal security; the condition is not beneficial.
D) No, because the depositary always has discretion over storage.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a storage condition in wadi'ah is enforceable only if it provides a real security benefit; otherwise the depositary is not liable for deviating.

Liability for Sub-Deposit: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-madhhab dispute on liability for sub-deposit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on sub-deposit liability and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between the views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Liability for sub-deposit arises from parting, not handing over – Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on the liability chain when a depositary sub-deposits without permission. Understanding who bears the loss – and why – sharpens your ability to trace liability in trust-based transactions. We will examine both positions, their proofs, and the practical consequences for the owner.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Identify the key facts: the owner deposited with the first depositary, who then deposited with a second without the owner's permission, and the item was lost.
The loss is not due to negligence of the second, but the dispute is about who bears the loss.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the owner can only claim from the first depositary, not the second. The first becomes liable only when he parts with the item, and the second remains a trustee.
Note the emphasis on the timing of liability.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the owner can claim from either party. The first becomes liable immediately upon handing over, and the second becomes liable by receiving from a liable person.
They argue that both are transgressors because the owner did not consent to the second's trust.
4
Compare their proofs
Analyze the qiyas used by each side. The Sahibayn analogize the second depositary to the depositary of a usurper. Abu Hanifa analogizes the second to one who receives a garment blown by wind – no act of his, so no liability.
Pay attention to the underlying principle: when does transgression (ta'addi) occur?
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is that under Abu Hanifa the owner has only one target for compensation; under the Sahibayn the owner can choose the more solvent party, but if the second pays, he can recourse against the first.
This can affect litigation strategy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَنْ أَوْدَعَ رَجُلًا وَدِيْعَةً فَاَوْدَعَهَا آخَرَ فَهَلَكَتْ فَلَهُ أنْ يُضَمِنَ الأوَّلَ وَلَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يُضَمِّنَ الْآخَرَ وَهَذَا عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةً وَقَالَا لَهُ أَنْ يُضَمِّنَ أَيَّهُمَا شَاءَ فَإِنْ ضَمَّنَ الْأَوَّلَ لَا يَرْجِعُ عَلَى الْآخَرِ وَإِنْ ضَمَّنَ الْآخَرَ رَجَعَ عَلَى الْأَوَّلِ لَهُمَا أَنَّهُ قَبَضَ الْمَالَ مِنْ يَدِ ضَمِيْنِ فَيَضْمَنُهُ كَمُودَعِ الْغَاصِبِ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّ الْمَالِكَ لَمْ يَرْضَ بِأَمَانَةِ غَيْرِهِ فَيَكُونُ الْأَوَّلُ مُتَعَدِّيَا بِالتَّسْلِيم وَالثَّانِي بِالْقَبْضِ فَيُخَيَّرُ بَيْنَهُمَا غَيْرَ أَنَّهُ إِنْ ضَمَّنَ الْأَوَّلَ لَمْ يَرْجِعُ عَلَى الثَّانِي لأَنَّهُ مَلَكَهُ بِالضَّمَانِ فَظَهَرَ انَّهُ اَوْدَعَ مِلْكَ نَفْسِهِ وَإِنْ ضَمَّنَ الثَّانِي رَجَعَ عَلَى الْأَوَّلِ لِأَنَّهُ عَامِلٌ لَهُ فَرْجِعُ عَلَيْهِ بِمَا لَحِقَهُ مِنَ الْعُهْدَةِ وَلَهُ إِنَّهُ قَبْضَ الْمَالَ مِنْ يَدِ آمِيْنِ لِأَنَّهُ بِالدَّفْعِ لَا يَضْمَنُ مَالَمْ يُفَارِقْهُ لِحُضُورِ رَابِهِ فَلَا تَعَدِى مِنْهُمَا فَإِذَا فَارَقَهُ فَقَدْ تَرَكَ الْحِفَظَ الْمُلْتَزَمَ فَيَضْمَنُهُ بِذَالِكَ وَأَمَّا الثَّانِي فَمُسْتَمِرُّ عَلَى الْحَالَةِ الأولى وَلَمْ يُوجَدُ مِنْهُ صَنْعَ فَلَا يَضْمَنُهُ كَالرِيحِ إِذَا الْقَتْ فِي حِجْرِهِ ثَوْبَ غَيْرِهِ۔ ترجمہ ایک شخص نے کسی کے پاس ودیعت رکھی اس نے کسی اور کے پاس رکھ دی اور وہ تلف ہو گئی تو مالک موذع اول سے نادان لے سکتا ہے مورع ثانی سے نہیں لے سکتا یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ ان میں سے جس سے چاہے تاوان لے سکتا ہے پس اگر اول سے تاوان لیا تو وہ ثانی پر رجوع نہیں کر سکتا اور اگر ثانی سے لیا تو وہ اول پر رجوع کرے گا۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ثانی نے مال ضمین کے ہاتھ سے لیا ہے تو وہ بھی ضامن ہوگا۔ جیسے غاصب کا مورع ضامن ہوتا ہے اور یہ اس لئے ہے کہ مالک دوسرے کی امانت سے راضی نہیں ہوا۔ پس مودع اول دینے سے متعدی ہوا اور مودع ثانی قبضہ کرنے سے پس مالک کو دونوں کے درمیان اختیار ہو گا۔ صرف اتنی بات ہے کہ اگر اس نے اول سے تاوان لیا تو وہ ثانی پر رجوع نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ موقع اول تاوان دے کر اس کا ملک ہو گیا۔ پس یہ بات ظاہر ہوگئی کہ اس نے اپنی ذاتی ملک ودیعت رکھی ہے اور اگر ثانی سے تاوان ایسا تو وہ اول پر رجوع کرے گا۔ کیونکہ نانی اول کے لئے عامل ہے تو اس کو جو منمان لاحق ہوا ہے وہ اول سے لے گا۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ثانی نے مال امین کے ہاتھ سے لیا ہے۔ کیونکہ اول صرف دینے سے ضامن نہیں ہو جاتا جب تک کہ اس سے جدا نہ ہو جائے اس کی رائے موجود ہونے کی وجہ سے پس دونوں میں سے کسی کی طرف سے تعدی نہیں ہے۔ ہاں جب وہ اس سے جدا ہو گیا۔ تو اس نے التزام کی ہوئی حفاظت کو چھوڑ دیا تو اس کی وجہ سے ضامن ہو جائے گا۔ رہا مورع ثانی وہ برابر اپنی حالت پر باقی ہے۔ اور اس کی طرف سے کوئی حرکت نہیں پائی گئی لہذا وہ ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ جیسے ہوا کسی کی گود میں کپڑا اڑا کر ڈال دے۔
He said: And whoever deposits a trust with a man, and he deposits it with another, and it is destroyed, then he (the owner) may hold the first liable, and he may not hold the other liable. This is according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He may hold either of them liable as he wishes. If he holds the first liable, he (the first) does not recourse against the other. If he holds the other liable, he recourses against the first. Their proof: He (the second) received the property from the hand of a liable person, so he is liable for it, like the depositary of a usurper. This is because the owner did not consent to the trust of another. Thus the first is transgressor by handing over, and the second by taking possession. So he (the owner) is given choice between them. However, if he holds the first liable, he does not recourse against the second because he (the first) owned it by the guarantee; thus it appears that he deposited his own property. And if he holds the second liable, he recourses against the first because he (the second) is his agent, so he recourses against him for the liability that befell him. And his (Abu Hanifa's) proof: He (the second) received the property from the hand of a trustee. Because the first does not become liable by handing over as long as he does not part from it, due to the presence of his (the owner's) property. So there is no transgression from either. When he parts from it, he has abandoned the committed preservation, so he becomes liable for it by that. As for the second, he continues in the first state, and no action from him is found, so he is not liable, like the wind when it throws another's garment into his lap.
Translation: A person placed a deposit with someone, who then deposited it with another, and it was lost. The owner can demand compensation from the first depositary, not the second, according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The two disciples say he can demand from whichever he wishes. If he demands from the first, the first cannot recourse against the second. If he demands from the second, the second recourses against the first. The disciples' proof: The second received the property from a liable person, so he is liable, like the depositary of a usurper. This is because the owner did not consent to another's trust. So the first is transgressor by handing over, and the second by taking possession. So the owner has choice. However, if he takes from the first, the first acquires ownership by the guarantee, so it appears he deposited his own property. If he takes from the second, the second recourses against the first because the second is acting for the first. Abu Hanifa's proof: The second received the property from a trustee. Because the first does not become liable by handing over until he parts from it, due to the presence of the owner's right. So there is no transgression from either. When he parts, he abandons the required preservation, so he becomes liable. As for the second, he remains in his original state, and no act from him is found, so he is not liable, like the wind that throws someone's garment into his lap.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability when a depositary (mustawda') sub-deposits the entrusted item without permission and it is subsequently lost. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the owner can only claim compensation from the first depositary (the one who originally received the deposit), not from the second. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) hold that the owner may choose to claim from either, but with specific recourse consequences: if he claims from the first, the first cannot claim from the second; if he claims from the second, the second can claim from the first. The reasoning of the Sahibayn: The first depositary becomes a transgressor (mut'addi) by handing over without permission, and the second becomes a transgressor by taking possession from a liable person (since the first is now liable). Thus the owner has the option. If he claims from the first, the first's ownership of the item by guarantee is established, so his sub-deposit is of his own property. If he claims from the second, the second can recourse against the first because the second acted as the first's agent in that scenario. Imam Abu Hanifa's reasoning: The first depositary does not become liable merely by handing over; liability only arises when he actually separates from the item (i.e., relinquishes control). Until that point, he is still a trustee. Therefore, the second receives from a trustee, not a liable person, so the second is also a trustee. The second is like someone who receives a garment blown by wind. The first becomes liable only after separation, but the second remains without liability. The commentary clarifies that the Sahibayn's view is based on the owner's lack of consent to the second's trustworthiness.

Key Terms
تعدي (ta'addī): Transgression; acting beyond the limits of trust, e.g., handing over the deposit without permission.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability or guarantee; the obligation to compensate for loss or damage.
امين (amīn): A trustee; one who is entrusted with property and not liable for loss unless negligent or transgressing.
ضامن (ḍāmin): A person subject to liability; must compensate for the value of the lost item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, from whom can the owner claim compensation if the depositary sub-deposits without permission and the item is lost?
A) Only from the first depositary.
B) From either the first or second depositary.
C) Only from the second depositary.
D) From neither, as it is a loss from an act of God.

Key Takeaway
The answer to who is liable in a sub-deposit depends on whether the first depositary is considered to have transgressed at the moment of handing over (Sahibayn) or only upon parting (Abu Hanifa).

Sub-Deposit and Liability: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sub-deposit liability with qiyas analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on liability when a depositary sub-deposits without permission and explain the reasoning and practical consequences of each position.

Core Idea
Without permission, sub-depositing triggers liability; Abu Hanifa limits it to the first depositary, the Sahibayn extend it to both.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about a common deposit scenario: the depositary (first) sub-deposits the entrusted item with a third party (second) without the owner's permission, and the item is lost. The core question is whom the owner may sue. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), offer different answers based on their analysis of trust (amanah) and transgression (ta'addi). By studying this dispute, you will see how Hanafi imams reason from principles to reach divergent rulings, and how these differences affect practical outcomes for litigants.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the matn ruling
Identify the basic ruling in the text: the owner may hold the first depositary liable, not the second. This is Abu Hanifa's position.
The matn gives Abu Hanifa's view as the default.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's position
The Sahibayn hold that the owner may choose to hold either the first or the second depositary liable, but if he chooses the first, the first cannot seek recourse from the second; if he chooses the second, the second can seek recourse from the first.
This is a genuine ikhtilaf within the school.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof (qiyas)
The Sahibayn analogize the second depositary to the depositary of a usurper (mudi' al-ghasib): just as someone who receives property from a usurper's hand becomes liable because the hand is not trustworthy, so the second depositary here receives from a hand that had no right to transfer, making him liable.
The analogy hinges on the status of the hand from which property is received.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof (direct reasoning)
Abu Hanifa argues that the second depositary took the property from a trustworthy hand (amin), because the first depositary does not become liable by merely handing over as long as he has not separated from the item. Only when the first abandons his obligated custody does he become liable. The second, having performed no transgressive act, remains an amin and is not liable, like a person into whose lap the wind blows a garment.
Abu Hanifa focuses on the act of taking and the continuity of trust.
5
Examine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, the owner must pursue the first depositary only. Under the Sahibayn, the owner can choose the more solvent party, and the recourse between depositaries creates inner dynamics.
This difference affects litigation strategy and risk allocation.

Source Text

قَالَ وَمَنْ أَوْدَعَ رَجُلًا وَدِيْعَةً فَاَوْدَعَهَا آخَرَ فَهَلَكَتْ فَلَهُ أنْ يُضَمِنَ الأوَّلَ وَلَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يُضَمِّنَ الْآخَرَ وَهَذَا عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةً وَقَالَا لَهُ أَنْ يُضَمِّنَ أَيَّهُمَا شَاءَ فَإِنْ ضَمَّنَ الْأَوَّلَ لَا يَرْجِعُ عَلَى الْآخَرِ وَإِنْ ضَمَّنَ الْآخَرَ رَجَعَ عَلَى الْأَوَّلِ لَهُمَا أَنَّهُ قَبَضَ الْمَالَ مِنْ يَدِ ضَمِيْنِ فَيَضْمَنُهُ كَمُودَعِ الْغَاصِبِ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّ الْمَالِكَ لَمْ يَرْضَ بِأَمَانَةِ غَيْرِهِ فَيَكُونُ الْأَوَّلُ مُتَعَدِّيَا بِالتَّسْلِيم وَالثَّانِي بِالْقَبْضِ فَيُخَيَّرُ بَيْنَهُمَا غَيْرَ أَنَّهُ إِنْ ضَمَّنَ الْأَوَّلَ لَمْ يَرْجِعُ عَلَى الثَّانِي لأَنَّهُ مَلَكَهُ بِالضَّمَانِ فَظَهَرَ انَّهُ اَوْدَعَ مِلْكَ نَفْسِهِ وَإِنْ ضَمَّنَ الثَّانِي رَجَعَ عَلَى الْأَوَّلِ لِأَنَّهُ عَامِلٌ لَهُ فَرْجِعُ عَلَيْهِ بِمَا لَحِقَهُ مِنَ الْعُهْدَةِ وَلَهُ إِنَّهُ قَبْضَ الْمَالَ مِنْ يَدِ آمِيْنِ لِأَنَّهُ بِالدَّفْعِ لَا يَضْمَنُ مَالَمْ يُفَارِقْهُ لِحُضُورِ رَابِهِ فَلَا تَعَدِى مِنْهُمَا فَإِذَا فَارَقَهُ فَقَدْ تَرَكَ الْحِفَظَ الْمُلْتَزَمَ فَيَضْمَنُهُ بِذَالِكَ وَأَمَّا الثَّانِي فَمُسْتَمِرُّ عَلَى الْحَالَةِ الأولى وَلَمْ يُوجَدُ مِنْهُ صَنْعَ فَلَا يَضْمَنُهُ كَالرِيحِ إِذَا الْقَتْ فِي حِجْرِهِ ثَوْبَ غَيْرِهِ

ترجمہ ایک شخص نے کسی کے پاس ودیعت رکھی اس نے کسی اور کے پاس رکھ دی اور وہ تلف ہو گئی تو مالک مودع اول سے تاوان لے سکتا ہے مودع ثانی سے نہیں لے سکتا یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ ان میں سے جس سے چاہے تاوان لے سکتا ہے پس اگر اول سے تاوان لیا تو وہ ثانی پر رجوع نہیں کر سکتا اور اگر ثانی سے لیا تو وہ اول پر رجوع کرے گا۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ثانی نے مال ضمین کے ہاتھ سے لیا ہے تو وہ بھی ضامن ہوگا۔ جیسے غاصب کا مودع ضامن ہوتا ہے اور یہ اس لئے ہے کہ مالک دوسرے کی امانت سے راضی نہیں ہوا۔ پس مودع اول دینے سے متعدی ہوا اور مودع ثانی قبضہ کرنے سے پس مالک کو دونوں کے درمیان اختیار ہو گا۔ صرف اتنی بات ہے کہ اگر اس نے اول سے تاوان لیا تو وہ ثانی پر رجوع نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ مودع اول تاوان دے کر اس کا ملک ہو گیا۔ پس یہ بات ظاہر ہوگئی کہ اس نے اپنی ذاتی ملک ودیعت رکھی ہے اور اگر ثانی سے تاوان لیا تو وہ اول پر رجوع کرے گا۔ کیونکہ مودع ثانی اول کے لئے عامل ہے تو اس کو جو ضمان لاحق ہوا ہے وہ اول سے لے گا۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ثانی نے مال امین کے ہاتھ سے لیا ہے۔ کیونکہ اول صرف دینے سے ضامن نہیں ہو جاتا جب تک کہ اس سے جدا نہ ہو جائے اس کی رائے موجود ہونے کی وجہ سے پس دونوں میں سے کسی کی طرف سے تعدی نہیں ہے۔ ہاں جب وہ اس سے جدا ہو گیا۔ تو اس نے التزام کی ہوئی حفاظت کو چھوڑ دیا تو اس کی وجہ سے ضامن ہو جائے گا۔ رہا مودع ثانی وہ برابر اپنی حالت پر باقی ہے۔ اور اس کی طرف سے کوئی حرکت نہیں پائی گئی لہذا وہ ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ جیسے ہوا کسی کی گود میں کپڑا اڑا کر ڈال دے۔

قوله ولهـمـا انــه قبض .... صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مودع المودع نے مال ودیعت پر ضمین کے ہاتھ سے قبضہ کیا ہے تو جیسے مودع الغاصب ضامن ہوتا ہے ایسے ہی یہ بھی ضامن ہو گا مثلاً ایک شخص نے کوئی چیز غصب کر کے کسی کے پاس ودیعت رکھ دی اور وہ ضائع ہو گئی تو مودع الغاصب ضامن ہوتا ہے اور یہ جو ہم نے کہا کہ اس نے ضمین کے ہاتھ سے قبضہ کیا ہے یہ اس لئے کہ زید خالد کے علاوہ دوسرے کی امانت داری سے راضی نہیں تو خالد کی طرف سے تو تعدی یہ ہوئی کہ اس نے محمود کے پاس ودیعت رکھی اور محمود کی طرف سے یہ تعدی ہوئی کہ اس نے اس پر قبضہ کیا لہذازید ان دونوں میں سے جس سے چاہے تاوان لے لے۔

قوله غیرانه ضمن صاحبین کی دلیل ہی سے متعلق ہے یعنی صرف اتنی بات ہے کہ اگر اس نے مودع اوّل سے ضمان لیا تو وہ دوسرے مودع سے واپس نہیں لے سکتا اس لئے کہ مودع اول تو ادا کیے گئے ضمان سے اس کا مالک ہو گیا۔ پس یہ بات ظاہر ہو گئی کہ اس نے اپنے ذاتی مال کو اپنے مودع کے پاس ودیعت رکھا ہے۔ لہذا وہ اپنے مودع سے تاوان نہیں لے سکتا۔ اور اگر مالک ودیعت نے مودع دوم سے تاوان لیا تو وہ مودع اول سے واپس لے لے گا۔ کیونکہ مودع دوم نے مودع اول کے لئے کام کیا ہے تو جو ضمان اس پر پڑا ہے وہ مودع اول سے لے گا۔

قوله وله انه قبض ... امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مودع المودع نے ضمین کے ہاتھ سے قبضہ نہیں کیا بلکہ امین کے ہاتھ سے قبضہ کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ مودع اول صرف ودیعت حوالہ کرنے سے ضامن نہیں ہو جاتا جب تک کہ وہ اس سے جدا نہ ہو تو قبل از مفارقت نہ مودع کی طرف سے تعدی ہے نہ مودع المودع کی طرف سے۔ ہاں جب وہ جدا ہو جائے گا تب اس کی طرف سے تعدی پائی جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ اس نے حفظ ملتزم کو ترک کر دیا تو مالک اس سے ترک حفظ کے سبب سے ضمان لے گا۔ بخلاف مودع المودع کے کہ اس کی جانب سے کوئی موجب ضمان فعل نہیں پایا گیا لہذا وہ ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ جیسے ہوا اگر کسی کی گود میں دوسرے کا کپڑا اڑا کر ڈال دے اور وہ تلف ہو جائے تو وہ ضامن نہیں ہو جاتا۔
He said: And whoever deposits a deposit with a man, and he deposits it with another, and it perishes, then he may hold the first liable, and he may not hold the other liable. This is according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He may hold liable whichever of them he wishes. If he holds the first liable, he does not have recourse against the other; and if he holds the other liable, he has recourse against the first. Their proof: that he (the second) took the property from the hand of a guarantor, so he is liable, like the depositary of a usurper. And this is because the owner was not pleased with the trustworthiness of another, so the first is transgressing by handing over, and the second by taking, so he is given choice between them. Except that if he holds the first liable, he does not have recourse against the second, because he (the first) became owner of it by the guarantee, so it appears that he deposited his own property. And if he holds the second liable, he has recourse against the first, because he (the second) is his agent, so he has recourse for the liability that befell him. And his (Abu Hanifa's) proof: that he took the property from the hand of a trustworthy person, because by handing over he is not liable as long as he does not separate from it due to the presence of his opinion, so no transgression from either. When he separates from it, he has abandoned the obligated custody, so he becomes liable by that. As for the second, he continues in the first state, and no action was found from him, so he is not liable, like the wind when it throws another's garment into his lap.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability when a depositary (al-mudi') sub-deposits the entrusted item with a third party without the owner's permission, and the item is subsequently lost. The ruling is stated in the matn: the owner can only claim damages from the first depositary (al-mudi' al-awwal), not from the second (al-mudi' al-thani). This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differ, granting the owner the option to claim from either depositary, with specific consequences regarding recourse. The passage then provides the proofs for each opinion. The Sahibayn's proof is based on qiyas (analogy) with the case of a depositary of a usurper (mudi' al-ghasib): just as a person who receives property from a usurper's hand becomes liable because the property came from a non-trustworthy hand, similarly, the second depositary here received the property from the first depositary who had no right to sub-deposit, thus the second depositary is also a guarantor. They argue that the first depositary transgressed by handing over without permission, and the second transgressed by taking possession without the owner's consent, so the owner may choose whom to sue. However, if the owner sues the first, the first becomes owner of the item by paying compensation, so he cannot then sue the second. If the owner sues the second, the second can seek recourse from the first because the second acted as an agent for the first in taking possession. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the second depositary took the property from a trustworthy hand (amin), because the first depositary does not become liable merely by handing over as long as he has not separated from the property while maintaining his oversight. Thus, there is no transgression from either at the moment of transfer. Only when the first depositary separates from the item and abandons his obligation of custody does he become liable. The second depositary, however, remains in the same state as before and committed no act that would make him liable, analogous to a person into whose lap the wind blows another's garment: he is not liable. This disagreement is a classic example of how Hanafi imams apply principles of trust and transgression in deposit law.

Key Terms
ودیعة (wadīʿah): A deposit; property entrusted to another for safekeeping without compensation.
مودع (mūdiʿ (depositor) / mūdaʿ (depositary)): In this text, mūdaʿ (with fatha) refers to the person who receives the deposit (the depositary). The depositor is called al-mūdiʿ (with kasra) or al-mālik.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability to compensate for loss or damage; guarantee.
تعدي (taʿaddī): Transgression; an act beyond what is permitted, making one liable for loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a depositary (first) sub-deposits an item with another person (second) without the owner's permission, and the item is lost, whom can the owner sue?
A) Only the first depositary
B) Only the second depositary
C) Either the first or the second
D) Neither, because the owner must bear the loss

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, unauthorized sub-deposit creates liability for the first depositary, but the Sahibayn also hold the second depositary liable, with recourse between them; the practical difference lies in the owner's options and the risk allocation.

Sub-deposit Without Permission: Liability of Depositary and Sub-depositary
Ruling on liability when depositary sub-deposits without permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on liability when a depositary sub-deposits without permission and explain the basis of disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The sub-depositary's liability depends on whether he took from a guarantor or a trustee — a dispute over the effective cause.

This passage from Kitab al-Wadi'ah presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on the liability of a sub-depositary. The issue arises when the original depositary, without permission, entrusts the item to another, and it is lost. The question: can the owner claim from the sub-depositary? Two positions emerge from the school, each with a distinct legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
Identify the two positions: Abu Hanifa's that owner can only claim from first depositary, and Sahibayn's that owner has option between first and second.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
Understand the qiyas to the depositary of a usurper. See how they argue that the sub-depositary took possession from a guarantor.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's rebuttal
Abu Hanifa distinguishes: the first depositary is a trustee, not a guarantor, until separation. The sub-depositary took from a trustee, so he is not liable.
Key: the effective cause ('illa) difference.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Abu Hanifa limits recourse to first depositary; Sahibayn gives option. Also, subsequent indemnity between depositary and sub-depositary differs.

Source Text

كتاب الوديعة. تشریح رجلا- ودیعت رکھی اور اس نے وہ چیز کسی دوسرے کے پاس ودیعت دی۔ مثلا پاس ودیعت رکھی محمود کے حالانکہ مالک نے اس کو [بیا؟] اجازت نہیں دی تھی اور نہ محمود اس کی ایسی میں ہے جس کو دیے بغیر کوئی چارہ نہ ہو ) پھر ودیعت مذکور محمود کے پاس تلف ہو گئی تو مالک ودیعت (زید) صرف مودَع اول ( خالد سے تاوان لے سکتا ہے نہ کہ مودع ثانی (محمود) سے یہ حکم امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور ایک روایت میں امام احمد بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک زید کو اختیار ہے چاہے مودع یعنی خالد سے ضمان لے اور چاہے موزع المودع یعنی محمود سے لے۔ امام شافعی، امام مالک اور دوسری روایت میں امام احمد بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں اب اگر اس نے مودع اول (خالد) سے تاوان لیا تو خالد یہ تاوان موزع المودع ( محمود ) سے نہیں لے سکتا اور اگر اس نے مودع المودع (محمود) سے تاوان لیا تو وہ یہ تاوان مودع اول ( خالد ) سے لے گا۔

قوله ولهما انه قبض .... صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ موزع المودع نے مال ودیعت پر ضمین کے ہاتھ سے قبضہ کیا ہے تو جیسے مودع الغاصب ضامن ہوتا ہے ایسے ہی یہ بھی ضامن ہو گا مثلاً ایک شخص نے کوئی چیز غصب کر کے کسی کے پاس ودیعت رکھ دی اور وہ ضائع ہو گئی تو مودع الغاصب ضامن ہوتا ہے اور یہ جو ہم نے کہا کہ اس نے ضمین کے ہاتھ سے قبضہ کیا ہے یہ اس لئے کہ زید خالد کے علاوہ دوسرے کی امانت داری سے راضی نہیں تو خالد کی طرف سے تو تعدی یہ ہوئی کہ اس نے محمود کے پاس ودیعت رکھی اور محمود کی طرف سے یہ تعدی ہوئی کہ اس نے اس پر قبضہ کیا لہذا زید ان دونوں میں سے جس سے چاہے تاوان لے لے۔

قوله غیرانه ضمن صاحبین کی دلیل ہی سے متعلق ہے یعنی صرف اتنی بات ہے کہ اگر اس نے مودع اوّل سے ضمان لیا تو وہ دوسرے موزع سے واپس نہیں لے سکتا اس لئے کہ مودع اول تو ادا کرنے سے اس کا مالک ہو گیا۔ پس یہ بات ظاہر ہو گئی کہ اس نے اپنے ذاتی مال کو اپنے مودع کے پاس ودیعت رکھا ہے۔ لہذا وہ اپنے موزع سے تاوان نہیں لے سکتا۔ اور اگر مالک ودیعت نے موزع دوم سے تاوان لیا تو وہ موزع اول سے واپس لے لے گا۔ کیونکہ موزع دوم نے موزع اول کے لئے کام کیا ہے تو جو ضمان اس پر پڑا ہے وہ موزع اول سے لے گا۔

قوله وله انه قبض ... امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ موزع المودع نے ضمین کے ہاتھ سے قبضہ نہیں کیا بلکہ امین کے ہاتھ سے قبضہ کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ مودع اول صرف ودیعت حوالہ کرنے سے ضامن نہیں ہو جاتا جب تک کہ وہ اس سے جدا نہ ہو تو قبل از مفارقت نہ مودع کی طرف سے تعدی ہے نہ مودع المودع کی طرف سے۔ ہاں جب وہ جدا ہو جائے گا تب اس کی طرف سے تعدی پائی جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ اس نے حفظ ملتزم کو ترک کر دیا تو مالک اس سے ترک حفظ کے سبب سے ضمان لے گا۔ بخلاف مودع المودع کے کہ اس کی جانب سے کوئی موجب ضمان فعل نہیں پایا گیا لہذا وہ ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ جیسے ہوا اگر کسی کی گود میں دوسرے کا کپڑا اڑا کر ڈال دے اور وہ تلف ہو جائے تو وہ ضامن نہیں ہو جاتا۔
Book of Deposit. Explanation: A man deposited something and he gave that thing to someone else as a deposit. For example, he deposited it with Mahmud while the owner had not given him permission, and Mahmud was not in a situation where giving it was unavoidable. Then that deposit was destroyed with Mahmud. So the owner (Zaid) can only take compensation from the first depositary (Khalid), not from the second depositary (Mahmud). This is the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and in one narration Imam Ahmad also holds this view. According to the Sahibayn, Zaid has the option: if he wishes, he may take guarantee from the depositary (Khalid), or if he wishes, from the sub-depositary (Mahmud). Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and in another narration Imam Ahmad also hold this view. Now if he takes compensation from the first depositary (Khalid), Khalid cannot take this compensation from the sub-depositary (Mahmud). And if he takes compensation from the sub-depositary (Mahmud), then he (the sub-depositary) will take this compensation from the first depositary (Khalid).

His saying: 'And for them both, because he took possession...' The proof of the Sahibayn is that the sub-depositary took possession of the deposited property from the hand of a guarantor. So just as the depositary of a usurper becomes a guarantor, similarly this one also becomes a guarantor. For example, a person usurped something and deposited it with someone, and it was lost; then the depositary of the usurper becomes a guarantor. And what we said that he took possession from the hand of a guarantor is because Zaid was not satisfied with the trustworthiness of anyone other than Khalid. So on Khalid's part, there was transgression (ta'addi) in that he deposited it with Mahmud, and on Mahmud's part, there was transgression in that he took possession of it. Therefore, Zaid may take compensation from whichever of the two he wishes.

His saying: 'Except that he guaranteed...' This is related to the proof of the Sahibayn, i.e., only this much: that if he takes guarantee from the first depositary, he cannot recover it from the second depositary, because the first depositary became the owner of it by payment. So it becomes apparent that he deposited his own personal property with his depositary. Hence, he cannot take compensation from his depositary. And if the owner of the deposit took compensation from the second depositary, then he will recover it from the first depositary, because the second depositary acted for the first depositary, so any guarantee that falls on him will be taken from the first depositary.

His saying: 'And for him, because he took possession...' The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that the sub-depositary did not take possession from the hand of a guarantor, but from the hand of a trustee. Because the first depositary does not become a guarantor merely by handing over the deposit until he separates from it. So before separation, there is neither transgression on the part of the depositary nor on the part of the sub-depositary. Yes, when he separates, then transgression will be found on his part, because he abandoned the obligation of preservation. So the owner will take guarantee from him due to abandonment of preservation. Unlike the sub-depositary, on whose side no act causing guarantee is found; therefore, he will not be a guarantor. Just as if someone's cloth is blown into another's lap and it is destroyed, that person does not become a guarantor.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Wadi'ah (Book of Deposit) presents an inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability when a depositary (muda') deposits the entrusted property with a third party without the owner's permission and it is subsequently lost. The author follows the structure: first stating the ruling, then presenting different positions, followed by proofs. The core issue is whether the owner can claim compensation from the original depositary only (Imam Abu Hanifa's view), or from either the original depositary or the sub-depositary at his option (Sahibayn and other imams). The text then examines the consequences: if the owner recovers from the original depositary, the original depositary cannot recover from the sub-depositary; if he recovers from the sub-depositary, the sub-depositary can recover from the original depositary. The Sahibayn's proof is based on qiyas: just as a depositary of a usurper (muda' al-ghasib) is a guarantor because he took possession from a usurper's hand, here the sub-depositary took possession from a guarantor (the original depositary who breached trust), so he is also a guarantor. The transgression (ta'addi) is on both: the original depositary by sub-depositing, and the sub-depositary by accepting possession. Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes: the sub-depositary took possession from a trustee (amin), not a guarantor, because the original depositary does not become a guarantor merely by handing over; only upon separation does he become liable due to abandoning preservation. The sub-depositary's act of possession is not a cause of guarantee; analogously, if a cloth blows into someone's lap and is destroyed, that person is not liable. This is a classic Hanafi application of istihsan over qiyas, prioritizing the trust-based nature of deposit.

Key Terms
مودع (mūdi‘): The person who deposits something (the depositor). In this passage, Zaid is the mūdi‘ (owner/depositor).
مودع المودع (mūda‘ al-mūda‘): The sub-depositary (the second person to receive the deposit from the first depositary).
تعدي (ta‘addī): Transgression or breach of trust, such as improperly handling the deposit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a depositary sub-deposits without permission and the item is lost, who is liable to the owner?
A) Only the first depositary
B) Only the sub-depositary
C) Either the first depositary or the sub-depositary at the owner's option
D) Both equally

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that the owner may claim from either the original depositary or the sub-depositary when the item is lost after unauthorized sub-deposit.

10 min
Dispute on Oath and Liability in Wadi'ah with Two Claimants
Intra-Hanafi dispute on oath and depositor's liability after judge's ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the positions of Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf on depositor liability and oath administration after a judge's ruling based on nukul.

Core Idea
Nukul (refusal to swear) is treated as dalalah iqrar, but whether it creates liability for the depositor is disputed between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

When a depositor refuses to take an oath in response to a claimant, the judge may rule for the claimant, treating the refusal as an indirect confession. But if a second claimant later emerges, a question arises: does the depositor become liable to the second claimant, and should an oath regarding value be administered? This lesson explores the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf on this issue, as reported by al-Khassaf in his commentary on Al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
Two claimants each claim a slave as their deposit. The depositor refuses to take an oath for the first claimant, and the judge rules for the first claimant. What happens regarding the second claimant's claim for value?
The dispute is about the second claimant's right to an oath and the depositor's liability for the value.
2
State the intra-Hanafi positions
Imam Muhammad holds that the depositor is liable for the value to the second claimant, and therefore an oath regarding value should be administered. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the depositor is not liable, so administering such an oath is futile.
Both positions are based on different causal analyses.
3
Trace the underlying causal principle
Muhammad argues that the depositor's nukul (as confession) is the cause of the judge's ruling, so the depositor bears responsibility. Abu Yusuf argues that the loss is caused by the judge's order, not the confession, so the depositor is not liable.
This difference in causality leads to different rulings on liability and oath.
4
Apply to the branch case of oath with value
Since nukul is analogous to confession (dalalah iqrar), if the underlying rule makes the depositor liable upon confession, then nukul also triggers liability, necessitating an oath with value. If confession does not create liability, nukul also does not.
Thus the dispute on the branch case mirrors the dispute on the principal case.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Muhammad's view, the second claimant can demand an oath regarding value and potentially receive compensation. Under Abu Yusuf's view, no oath is administered and no compensation is due from the depositor.
The text does not specify the mufta bihi; later Hanafi texts may prefer Muhammad's view on liability.

وَذَكَرَ الْخَصَّافُ أَنَّهُ نَفَذَ قَضَاؤُهُ لِلْأَوَّلِ وَوَضَعَ الْمَسْأَلَةَ فِي الْعَبْدِ وَإِنَّمَا نَفَذَ لِمُصَادَفَتِهِ مَحَلَّ الْإِجْتِهَادِ لِأَنَّ مِنَ الْعُلَمَاءِ مَنْ قَالَ يَقْضِي لِلْأَوَّلِ وَلَا يَنْتَظِرُ لِكَوْنِهِ إِقْرَارًا دَلَالَةً ثُمَّ لَا يَحْلِفُ لِلثَّانِي مَا هَذَا الْعَبْدُ لِي لِأَنَّ نُكُولَهُ لَا يُفِيدُ بَعْدَمَا صَارَ لِلْأَوَّلِ وَهَلْ يُحَلِّفُهُ بِاللَّهِ مَا لِهَذَا عَلَيْكَ هَذَا الْعَبْدُ وَلَا قِيمَتَهُ وَهُوَ كَذَا وَكَذَا وَلَا أَقَلُّ مِنْهُ قَالَ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُحَلَّفَهُ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ خِلَافًا لِأَبِي يُوسُفَ بِنَاءً عَلَى أَنَّ الْمُودِعَ إِذَا أَقَرَّ بِالْوَدِيعَةِ وَدُفِعَ بِالْقَضَا إِلَى غَيْرِهِ يَضْمَنُهُ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ خِلَافًا لَهُ وَهَذِهِ فَرَيْعَةُ تِلْكَ الْمَسْأَلَةِ وَقَدْ وَقَعَ فِيهَا بَعْضُ الْإِطْنَابِ وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ

تَرْجَمَةٌ: وَإمَامُ خَصَّافٍ قَالَ أَنَّ القَاضِيَ يَحْكُمُ لِلْأَوَّلِ وَيَنْفُذُ حُكْمُهُ. وَضَعَ المَسْأَلَةَ فِي العَبْدِ. وَنَفَذَ الحُكْمُ لِأَنَّهُ فِي مَحَلِّ الِاجْتِهَادِ، إِذْ بَعْضُ العُلَمَاءِ قَالُوا يَقْضِي لِلْأَوَّلِ وَلَا يَنْتَظِرُ، لِأَنَّ امْتِنَاعَ المَدْعِيِّ عَلَيْهِ عَنِ اليَمِينِ دَلِيلُ الإِقْرَارِ. ثُمَّ لَا يَحْلِفُ لِلثَّانِي بِأَنَّ هَذَا العَبْدَ لَيْسَ لَهُ، لِأَنَّ نُكُولَهُ لَا يُفِيدُ بَعْدَ مَا صَارَ لِلْأَوَّلِ. وَهَلْ يُحَلِّفُهُ بِاللَّهِ مَا لِهَذَا عَلَيْكَ هَذَا العَبْدُ وَلَا قِيمَتَهُ وَهُوَ كَذَا وَكَذَا وَلَا أَقَلَّ مِنْهُ؟ قَالَ الخَصَّافُ: يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُحَلَّفَ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ خِلَافًا لِأَبِي يُوسُفَ، بِنَاءً عَلَى أَنَّ المُودِعَ إِذَا أَقَرَّ بِالوَدِيعَةِ وَدُفِعَ بِالقَضَاءِ إِلَى غَيْرِهِ يَضْمَنُ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ خِلَافًا لِأَبِي يُوسُفَ. وَهَذِهِ فَرْعِيَّةٌ مِنْ تِلْكَ المَسْأَلَةِ. وَقَدْ وَقَعَ فِيهَا بَعْضُ الإِطْنَابِ. وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

تشريح: قوله وذكر الخصاف... صورت میں امام خصاف نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ مدعی اول کے حق کا حکم نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ پس موجودہ پورے ہزار درہم مدعی ثانی کی شرکت کے بغیر اسی کو ملیں گے لیکن امام خصاف نے مسئلہ کو وضع دراہم کے بجائے غلام میں رکھی ہے یعنی دونوں مدعیوں نے ایک ہی غلام اپنا مملوک ہونے اور ودیعت رکھنے کا دعوی کیا اور مدعی علیہ نے ایک مدعی کے لئے قسم کھانے سے انکار کیا یہ پس قاضی نے اس مدعی کے لئے غلام کا حکم دے دیا تو قاضی کا حکم نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ اور دوسرے مدعی کے لئے قسم لینے تک انتظار نہیں کرے گا۔ کیونکہ مدعی اول کے لئے مدعی علیہ کا قسم سے انکار کرنا دلالہ اقرار ہے۔ گویا اس نے اس بات کا اقرار کر لیا کہ غلام مذکور اسی مدعی کی ودیعت ہے۔ حکم قاضی کے نافذ ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ قضا د کور مجتہد فیہ مسئلہ میں واقع ہوئی ہے چنانچہ بعض علماء اس کے قائل ہیں کہ قاضی مدعی اول کے لئے حکم کر دے اور مدعی ثانی کے لئے قسم لینے تک انتظار نہ کرے۔ لان امتناعه عن اليمين يدل على الاقرار۔

قوله ثم لا يحلف للثاني.... جب قاضی نے مدعی اول کے لئے حکم دے دیا تو پھر دوسرے مدعی کیلئے مدعی علیہ سے یوں قسم نہیں لے گا کہ یہ غلام اس مدعی کا نہیں ہے یعنی قسم میں صرف اتنا ہی کہنا کہ یہ غلام اس مدعی کا نہیں ہے۔ محض بے فائدہ ہے اس لئے کہ اگر وہ قسم کھانے سے انکار کرے تو غلام مدعی دوم کو نہیں مل سکتا۔ کیونکہ وہ تو مدعی اول کے لئے ہو چکا لہذا تم میں قیمت کو بھی ملانا چاہئے۔

قوله وهل يحلفه بالله.. عبارت میں ”قَالَ ينبغي“ هل يحلفہ“ کا جواب ہے اور بناء قال کا مفعول لہ ہے یا اس کے فائل سے حال ہے۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ عبد کے ساتھ قیمت ملا کر اس سے اس طرح قسم لی جائے گی یا نہیں؟ بالله ما لهذا عليك هذا العبد و لا قيمته وهو كذا و كذا و لا اقل منه و امام خصاف نے کہا ہے کہ امام محمد کے نزدیک مذکور قسم لینی چاہیئے برخلاف قول ابو یوسف کے یہ اختلاف ذیل کے اختلافی مسئلہ پر مبنی ہے۔ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ موقع نے زید کے لئے ودیعت کا اقرار کیا اس کے بعد کہنے لگا کہ مجھ سے غلطی ہوئی بلکہ یہ ودیعت تو فلاں کی ہے تو موقع پر وہ

ودیعت اول کو دینا واجب ہے کیونکہ ان دونوں کے لئے اس کا اقرار کرنا صحیح اور بل ہی لفلان کہہ کر رجوع کرنا باطل ہے۔ اب اگر وہ قضاء قاضی دیتا ہے تو امام محمد کے نزدیک اس صورت میں بھی قیمت کا ضامن ہوگا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ دوسرے مقرلہ کا جو حق فوت ہوا ہے وہ صرف مودع کے اقرار کی وجہ سے نہیں ہوا بلکہ اول کو ودیعت دینے کی وجہ سے ہوا ہے اور اول کو ودیعت دینا قضاء قاضی کے ذریعہ سے ہوا ہے لہذا مودع ضامن نہ ہوگا۔

امام محمد یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ تو تسلیم ہے کہ ودیعت دینا قاضی کے حکم سے ہوا ہے۔ لیکن قاضی کو اس فیصلہ پر تو اسی نے مسلط کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کے اقرار کی وجہ سے قاضی کو یہ فیصلہ کرنا پڑا۔ (ادھر وہ ثانی کے لئے بھی ودیعت ہونے کا اقرار کر چکا) اور موزع جب ودیعت پر کسی غیر کو مسلط کر دے تو وہ ضامن ہو جاتا ہے۔

جب یہ مسئلہ سامنے آگیا تو اب مسئلہ تکلیف کا اس مسئلہ پر مبنی ہونا اس لئے ہے کہ قسم سے انکار کرنا دلالہ اقرار ہے۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک دوسرے کے لئے ودیعت کا اقرار کرنا وجوب ضمان کے حق میں مفید ہے تو ایسے ہی قسم سے انکار کرنا بھی مفید ہو گا۔ لہذا مدعی علیہ سے مدعی ثانی کے لئے قسم لی جائے گی اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اقرار سے ضامن نہیں ہوتا تو ایسے ہی نکول سے بھی ضامن نہ ہو گا۔ فلا فائدة في التحليف۔

قوله وهذه قريعة..... هذه كا مشار الیہ مسئلہ تکلیف قاضی ہے جو وهل يحلفه بالله اله عبارت میں مذکور ہے اور قد وقع فيه “ کے بجائے فیها کہنا چاہیے کیونکہ لفظ مسئلہ مونث ہے اب یہ تو مذکور کی تاویل میں ہے یا بنی پر تسامح ہے۔ فان الفقهاء يتسامحون في العبارات اور لفظ فريعة بصورت تصغیر لانے میں اس طرف اشارہ ہے کہ ہم نے یہ مسئلہ مختصر اذکر کیا ہے نیز مسئلہ مذکورہ کی جس میں امام ابو یوسف و امام محمد نے اختلاف کیا ہے بہت سی فروع ہیں جن میں سے کئی ایک علامہ عینی نے بنایہ میں ذکر کی ہیں۔ من شاء فليراجع اليه.
And al-Khassaf mentioned that his (the judge's) ruling takes effect for the first (claimant), and he placed the case concerning the slave. It takes effect because it coincides with a matter of ijtihad, for among the scholars are those who say: he rules for the first and does not wait, because it (the refusal to swear) is an indication of confession. Then he does not administer an oath to the second (claimant): 'This slave is not mine,' because his nukul (refusal to swear) is of no benefit after it has become for the first. And he (the judge) administers an oath to him by Allah: 'This slave is not owed to this (claimant) by you, nor its value which is such and such, nor anything less than it.' He said: it is appropriate to administer an oath to him according to Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf, based on the fact that when the depositor confesses to the deposit and it is given by judicial decree to someone else, he is liable for it according to Muhammad, contrary to him (Abu Yusuf). And this is a branch of that case, and there has occurred in it some elaboration. And Allah knows best.

[Urdu translation and commentary follow: explaining that al-Khassaf stated the judge's ruling for the first claimant is executed. He placed the case regarding a slave. The ruling is executed because it is in a sphere of ijtihad. Some scholars say the judge rules for the first and does not wait for the second, because refusal to swear indicates confession. Then he does not swear the second claimant simply stating the slave is not his, because nukul is useless after the slave has become for the first. As for whether the judge should swear the defendant with the value included, al-Khassaf said it should be administered according to Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf, based on the underlying dispute: when the depositor confesses to one and then the judge gives it to another, the depositor is liable according to Muhammad, not Abu Yusuf. Abu Yusuf says the loss is due to the judge's order, not the confession. Muhammad says the depositor empowered the judge through his confession. Since the depositor also confessed to the second, his confession triggers liability. Similarly, nukul (refusal to swear) is like confession. Hence the judge should swear the defendant for the second claimant according to Muhammad, while Abu Yusuf sees no benefit. The word 'furai'ah' (diminutive) indicates this is a brief mention; many branches exist as mentioned by 'Ayni in al-Binayah.]
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on a ruling from al-Hidayah regarding a dispute over a deposit (wadi'ah) where two claimants each claim a slave as their deposit. The depositor (mudi') refuses to take an oath for the first claimant. The judge rules in favor of the first claimant based on the principle that refusal to swear (nukul) is tantamount to confession (dalalah iqrar) according to some scholars. The judge does not wait to administer an oath for the second claimant because the slave is already awarded. However, a question arises: should the judge administer an oath to the defendant for the second claimant regarding the value of the slave? Imam al-Khassaf reports that according to Imam Muhammad, such an oath should be administered, including the value, on the grounds that nukul functions like a confession, and in the underlying case, when a depositor confesses to one person and then the judge gives the deposit to another, the depositor becomes liable (damman) according to Muhammad because his confession caused the judge's decision. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees: he holds that liability arises only from the judge's order, not from the confession itself, so the depositor is not liable. Consequently, for the second claimant, administering an oath regarding value is futile because even if the defendant refuses, it cannot transfer ownership already established. This passage demonstrates the deeper usul principle that the effect of nukul mirrors the effect of express confession (iqrar). The text concludes by acknowledging that this is a brief treatment of a branch issue with many ramifications, and refers to al-'Ayni's Al-Binayah for further details.

Key Terms
نكول (nukūl): Refusal of the defendant to take the required oath after it is demanded by the judge.
إقرار دلالة (iqrār dalālah): An indirect confession inferred from conduct, such as nukul (refusal to swear).
مودع (mūdiʿ): The person who deposits an item (depositor). In the context, he is also the defendant (mudda'a 'alayh).
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability or compensation; in this context, the depositor's obligation to pay the value of the deposit to the second claimant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, why should the judge administer an oath to the defendant regarding the value of the slave for the second claimant?
A) Because the defendant explicitly confessed to the second claimant
B) Because nukul (refusal to swear) is treated as dalalah iqrar, and in the underlying case, the depositor's confession triggers liability
C) Because the judge must always administer an oath for any leftover claims
D) Because Abu Yusuf also agreed to administer the oath

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, nukul is treated as an indirect confession (dalalah iqrar), but its effect on the depositor's liability to a second claimant is disputed between Imam Muhammad (liable) and Imam Abu Yusuf (not liable) due to differing views on the causal role of the judge's order.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Depositary's Liability After Court-Ordered Delivery and Analogy to Nukul
Intra-Hanafi dispute on causation in depositary liability and analogy to nukul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the reasoning of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding a depositary's liability when delivering a deposit by court order, and evaluate the analogy to nukul as implied confession.

Core Idea
The depositary is liable if his own confession caused the court order, even though the order itself was the direct cause.

In Hanafi fiqh, a depositary (mudi') is generally a trustee (amin) not liable for loss. But what happens when he confesses that the deposit belongs to two claimants, then delivers it to one based on a judge's order? Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad differ on whether he becomes liable. Their disagreement hinges on the concept of legal causation. Moreover, their reasoning extends to a related issue: if a defendant refuses to take an oath (nukul), does that function as an implied confession? This lesson breaks down the dispute and its implications.

Guided Path
1
1. State the scenario
A depositary confesses that a deposit belongs to two persons (A and B). Later, A brings a claim and the judge orders delivery to A. The depositary complies. B's right is lost. Determine who is liable for B's loss.
The depositary's confession for both is valid and retraction is invalid.
2
2. Identify the positions
Imam Abu Yusuf holds the depositary is not liable. Imam Muhammad holds he is liable for the value.
These are the two core views within the Hanafi school.
3
3. Analyze Imam Abu Yusuf's reasoning
He argues the direct cause of the loss is the court order (qada' qadi), not the depositary's confession. The depositary did not voluntarily cause the loss; he merely complied with the judge's ruling.
Abu Yusuf focuses on the immediate operative cause.
4
4. Analyze Imam Muhammad's reasoning
He concedes the delivery was by court order, but argues that the depositary's confession caused the judge to rule that way. Moreover, by confessing and then delivering, the depositary empowered a third party (the judge) over the deposit, which makes him liable.
Muhammad looks at the indirect but effective cause (sabab).
5
5. Extend to nukul
Imam Muhammad analogizes: if confession creates liability, then refusal to swear (nukul), being evidence of confession (dalalah iqrar), should also create liability. Abu Yusuf rejects the analogy because he denies that confession itself creates liability in the original case.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Muhammad would administer the oath to the defendant; Abu Yusuf sees no benefit.

Source Text

الوديعة
ودیعت اول کو دینا واجب ہے کیونکہ ان دونوں کے لئے اس کا اقرار کرنا صحیح اور بل ہی لفلان کہہ کر رجوع کرنا باطل ہے
اب اگر وہ
قضاء قاضی دیتا ہے تو امام محمد کے نزدیک اس صورت میں بھی قیمت کا ضامن ہوگا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ دوسرے مقرلہ کا جو حق فوت ہوا ہے وہ صرف مودع کے اقرار کی وجہ سے نہیں ہوا بلکہ اول کو ودیعت دینے کی وجہ سے ہوا ہے اور اول کو ودیعت دینا قضاء قاضی کے ذریعہ سے ہوا ہے لہذا مودع ضامن نہ ہوگا۔
امام محمد یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ تو تسلیم ہے کہ ودیعت دینا قاضی کے حکم سے ہوا ہے۔ لیکن قاضی کو اس فیصلہ پر تو اسی نے مسلط کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کے اقرار کی وجہ سے قاضی کو یہ فیصلہ کرنا پڑا۔ (ادھر وہ ثانی کے لئے بھی ودیعت ہونے کا اقرار کر چکا) اور موزع جب ودیعت پر کسی غیر کو مسلط کر دے تو وہ ضامن ہو جاتا ہے۔
جب یہ مسئلہ سامنے آگیا تو اب مسئلہ تکلیف کا اس مسئلہ پر مبنی ہونا اس لئے ہے کہ قسم سے انکار کرنا دلالہ اقرار ہے۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک دوسرے کے لئے ودیعت کا اقرار کرنا وجوب ضمان کے حق میں مفید ہے تو ایسے ہی قسم سے انکار کرنا بھی مفید ہو گا۔ لہذا مدعی علیہ سے مدعی ثانی کے لئے قسم لی جائے گی اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اقرار سے ضامن نہیں ہوتا تو ایسے ہی نکول سے بھی ضامن نہ ہو گا۔ فلا فائدة في التحليف
قوله وهذه قريعة ..... هذه كا مشار الیہ مسئلہ تکلیف قاضی ہے جو وهل يحلفه بالله اله عبارت میں مذکور ہے اور قد وقع فيه “ کے بجائے فیها کہنا چاہیے کیونکہ لفظ مسئلہ مونث ہے اب یہ تو مذکور کی تاویل میں ہے یا بنی پر تسامح ہے۔ فان الفقهاء يتسامحون في العبارات اور لفظ فريعة بصورت تصغیر لانے میں اس طرف اشارہ ہے کہ ہم نے یہ مسئلہ مختصر اذکر کیا ہے نیز مسئلہ مذکورہ کی جس میں امام ابو یوسف و امام محمد نے اختلاف کیا ہے بہت سی فروع ہیں جن میں سے کئی ایک علامہ عینی نے بنایہ میں ذکر کی ہیں۔ من شاء فليراجع اليه.
The deposit: Giving it to the first [claimant] is obligatory because his confession for both of them is valid, and saying 'Rather it is for so-and-so' and retracting is invalid. Now if he gives it by court order, then according to Imam Muhammad in this case also he becomes guarantor of the value. And according to Imam Abu Yusuf he does not become guarantor. Imam Abu Yusuf says: the right lost by the second confessee did not happen solely due to the depositary's confession, rather it happened due to giving the deposit to the first [claimant], and giving the deposit to the first happened through the court order, so the depositary is not liable. Imam Muhammad says: It is conceded that giving the deposit was by the judge's order, but he [the depositary] is the one who empowered the judge to make that decision, because due to his confession the judge had to make that ruling (and he had already confessed for the second as well). And when the depositary empowers a third party over the deposit, he becomes liable. When this issue is clarified, then the issue of oath [refusal] is based on this because refusal to swear indicates confession (dalalat iqrar). And according to Imam Muhammad, confessing the deposit for the second is effective for establishing liability, similarly refusal to swear is also effective. Therefore the defendant will be made to swear for the second claimant. And according to Imam Abu Yusuf, confession does not make liable, so similarly nukul [refusal] also does not make liable. So there is no benefit in administering the oath. His saying: 'And this is a small gem...' The referent of 'this' is the issue of the judge's oath that is mentioned in the expression 'and whether he should make him swear by Allah'. And instead of 'qa' w f' fhi' it should be 'fiha' because the word 'mas'alah' is feminine. Either this is interpreting the masculine or it is carelessness in expression, for the jurists are lenient in expressions. The word 'fari'ah' in the diminutive form indicates that we have mentioned this issue briefly. Also, the mentioned issue in which Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad differed has many branches, some of which Allamah Ayni mentioned in al-Binayah. Whoever wishes should refer to it.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the liability of a depositary (mudi') who delivers a deposited item to one claimant based on a court order (qada' qadi), when another claimant also claims it. The core issue is causation: what legally caused the loss of the second claimant's right? Imam Abu Yusuf argues that the direct cause is the court order, not the depositary's confession, so no liability. Imam Muhammad argues that the depositary's confession caused the judge to rule, making the depositary the indirect cause (sabab), and once he empowers a third party over the deposit, he becomes liable. The text then analogizes this to the issue of nukul (refusal to take an oath) in a similar dispute: if a defendant refuses to swear, does that function as an implied confession making him liable? Imam Muhammad says yes, because refusal is evidence of confession (dalalah iqrar), just as explicit confession makes liable. Abu Yusuf says no, because refusal is like the confession that he already argued does not create liability in the previous case. The passage concludes with a note on the commentator's use of 'fari'ah' (diminutive) to indicate a brief treatment, and refers to al-Binayah for further branches.

Key Terms
مودع (mudi'): The person who deposits an item with another for safekeeping; here also used for the depositary (the one receiving the deposit).
مقر له (muqarr lahu): The person in whose favor a confession (iqrar) is made.
قضاء قاضي (qada' qadi): A judicial decree or order issued by a judge.
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee to compensate for loss or damage.
نكول (nukul): Refusal of a defendant to take an oath when required by the court.
دلالة اقرار (dalalah iqrar): An indication or evidence of confession; here, refusal to swear is treated as dalalah iqrar by Imam Muhammad.
فريعة (fari'ah): Diminutive form of فريعة, meaning a small gem or precious thing; used here to denote a brief but important legal point.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the dispute about the depositary's liability, what is the key difference in causal reasoning between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad?
A) Abu Yusuf focuses on the court order as direct cause; Muhammad focuses on the confession as indirect cause.
B) Abu Yusuf says the depositary empowered the judge; Muhammad denies.
C) They agree on the cause but differ on the amount.
D) Muhammad uses qiyas; Abu Yusuf uses istihsan.

Key Takeaway
The depositary's liability after a court order depends on whether his own confession was the legal cause of the order; this same causation determines whether nukul is treated as implied confession.

The Ruling and Linguistic Origin of 'Ariyah (Loan)
Opening ruling and linguistic analysis of 'ariyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of 'ariyah, identify its proof, and explain the preferred linguistic derivation preferred by Hanafi scholars.

Core Idea
'Ariyah is a recommended act of kindness, proven by the Prophet's borrowing and supported by consensus.

This lesson opens the book of 'ariyah (gratuitous loan for use) from Ashraf al-Hidayah. We will first identify the ruling—permissible and recommended—then examine the proof: the Prophet himself borrowed armor from Safwan. We also explore the linguistic origin of the term 'ariyah, as different derivations affect the legal nuance. Finally, we reflect on the virtue of this transaction and its connection to divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the hukm of 'ariyah as mentioned: ja'iz (permissible) and mustahabb (recommended). In Hanafi terminology, mustahabb equals sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah.
The text uses 'ja'izah' but commentary elevates it to recommended due to ihsan.
2
Locate the Proof
Find the dalil: the Prophet borrowed armor (durū') from Safwan bin Umayyah on the day of Hunain. This action proves permissibility, and the act of ihsan makes it recommended. Also, consensus (ijma') is cited by Shaykh Muwaffaq.
The hadith is ahad, but its meaning is qat'i for permissibility.
3
Trace the Linguistic Debate
Examine the different derivations: some derive from 'ariyah (gift), others from 'ar (shame) or 'ara (nakedness). The preferred opinion, from al-Mughrib, is from i'arah (lending), refuting the shame theory because the Prophet would not shame himself.
The concept of tanaawub (alternation) also appears, linking to the revocability of 'ariyah.
4
Understand the Virtue
The commentator notes that giving 'ariyah is like responding to the distressed (al-mudtarr), making the lender Allah's deputy. The hadith 'takhallaqu bi akhlaq Allah' is invoked.
This elevates the act from merely permissible to spiritually rewarding.
5
Connect to the Legal Definition
The passage sets the foundation: 'ariyah is a non-binding contract where the owner allows use without consumption, revocable at will. The upcoming sections will expand on rules.
The key difference from qard (loan for consumption) is highlighted linguistically.

Source Text

كتـــاب الـــعـــاريـــه
عاریت کی شرعی حیثیت
قَالَ الْعَارِيَةُ جَائِزَةٌ لِأَنَّهُ نَوْعُ إِحْسَانِ وَقَدْ اسْتَعَارَ النَّبِيُّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ دُرُوعًا مِنْ صَفْوَانَ
ترجمہ عاریت جائز ہے کیونکہ یہ ایک طرح کا احسان ہے اور خود آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت صفوان سے لی تھیں۔ تشریح قوله کتاب الخ اس کی وجہ مناسبت تو ہم کتاب الود یعہ کے آغاز میں ذکر کر چکے کہ ان میں ہر ایک امانت ہے۔ رہی لفظ عاریت کی لفظی و شرعی تحقیق سولفظ عاریت یاء مشرق کے ساتھ اصح ہے۔ اور تخفیف بھی جائز ہے۔ جیسا کہ قاموس میں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے اس کو عربیہ بمعنی عطیہ سے مانا ہے۔ جس میں علامہ بدرالدین عینی وغیرہ نے مناقشہ کیا ہے جو آگے صفحات پر آ رہا ہے۔ جوہری اور ابن الاثیر وغیرہ نے کہا ہے کہ یہ عاریہ کی طرف منسوب ہے کیونکہ دوسرے سے عاریہ چیز مانگنا باعث عیب ہے ( مصباح و شرح نقایہ ) صاحب مغرب نے عارہ کی طرف منسوب مانا ہے جو اعارہ کا اسم ہے اور عار معنی عیب کی طرف منسوب ہونے کی تردید کی ہے۔ چنانچہ مغرب میں ہے:
العارية اصلها عورية فعلية منسوبة الى العارة اسم من الاعارة كالغارة من الاغارة واخذها من العار العيب او العرى خطاء اھ
وجه تردید یہ ہے کہ عاریہ عاریہ ہے اور عاریتہ وادی ہے۔ ائمہ لغت نے اس کی تصریح کی ہے۔ صاحب نہا یہ کہتے ہیں کہ مغرب میں جو مذکورہ ہے اس پر اعتماد ہے اس واسطے کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کا عاریت طلب کرنا حدیث سے ثابت ہے اگر یہ چیز باعث عار ہوتی تو آپ ہرگز طلب نہ فرماتے۔ مبسوط میں ہے کہ تعاور بمعنی تناوب سے ہے گو یا مالک اپنی ملک سے غیر کے لئے نفع اٹھانے کی باری کرتا ہے اس شرط پر کہ وہ جب چاہے عاریت واپس لے کر اپنی نوبت لوٹا لے گا ( وقاله البطلیو سی ایضاً ) اسی لئے اعادہ کمیل و موزون میں قرض ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ ان میں سے انتفاع استهلاک عین کے بغیر نہیں ہوسکتا اور استبلاک مین کے بعد بعینہ میل و موزون میں باری نہیں لوٹ سکتی یہاں تک کہ وہ حقیقہ عاربیت ہو بلکہ باری اس کے مثل میں لوٹے گی ازہری نے اس کو عار الشئی سے مانا ہے بمعنی آنا جانا اس سے بطال یعنی آوارہ گر دکوعیار کہتے ہیں کیونکہ وہ اپنی لغویات میں گھومتا پھرتا ہے۔ والعرب تقول اعاره و عاره مثل اطاعه و طاعہ شرعی تعریف آگے آ رہی ہے۔ فائدہ ... عاریت دینے کے محاسن میں سے ایک عمدہ خوبی یہ بھی ہے کہ مستعیر اپنی حاجت وضرورت کی وجہ سے مضطر اور بے قرار ہوتا ہے اور حق تعالی کا ارشاد ہے:
" أمَّن يُجِيبُ الْمُضْطَرَّ إِذَا دَعَاهُ
آیا کوئی سنتا ہے بے قرار کی جب وہ اس کو پکارے۔
پس معیر مستعیر کو عاریت دے کر اس کی فریادرسی اور حاجت روائی میں گویا اللہ کا نائب اور بحکم حدیث "" تخلقوا باخلاق الله متخلق باخلاق ربانی ہوا۔ قـولـه العارية جائزة الخ . عاریت کا شرعی حکم یہ ہے کہ یہ جائز ہے ( دینے میں ثواب ہے اور لینے میں بھی کوئی عیب نہیں ہے ) شیخ موفق نے المغنی میں کہا ہے کہ عاریت کے جواز اور اس کے استحباب پر مسلمانوں کا اجماع ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ ایک طرح کا احسان ہے.. وماعلی احسنین من سبیل ۔ خود آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کا حضرت صفوان بن امیہ سے حنین کے دن تھیں (۳۰) زر ہیں اور ایک روایت کے مطابق سو (۱۰۰) زر ہیں عاریت لینا اور
Kitab al-Ariyah. The legal status of 'ariyah. He said: 'Ariyah is permissible because it is a type of kindness, and the Prophet, peace be upon him, borrowed armor from Safwan.' Translation: 'Ariyah is permissible because it is a type of kindness, and the Prophet himself borrowed from Hadrat Safwan. Commentary: 'His saying: Kitab al-Ariyah etc.' The reason for the connection [to previous book] we mentioned at the beginning of Kitab al-Wadi'ah: that each is a trust (amanah). As for the lexical and legal investigation of the word 'ariyah: the word 'ariyah with a fat ha on the ya is more correct, and tashdid is also permissible as in Qamus. The author of al-Hidayah derived it from 'ariyah meaning 'gift', which Allamah Badr al-Din al-Ayni and others have criticized, which will come later. Jawhari and Ibn al-Athir etc. said that it is attributed to 'ariyah (borrowing) because asking someone for something borrowed is a cause of shame (ayb). (Misbah and Sharh al-Niqayah). The author of al-Mughrib considered it attributed to 'arah which is the noun of i'arah (lending), and refuted the attribution to 'ar meaning shame. Accordingly, in al-Mughrib: 'The original of 'ariyah is 'awriyyah, a relative adjective from al-arah, a noun from al-i'arah, like al-gharah from al-igharah. Taking it from al-ar (shame) or al-ara (nakedness) is an error.' The refutation is that 'ariyah is a borrowed thing, and the linguists have clarified this. The author of al-Nihayah says that what is mentioned in al-Mughrib is reliable because the Prophet's requesting 'ariyah is proven by hadith; if it were a cause of shame, he would never have requested it. In al-Mabsut, it is said that ta'aawur means tanaawub (alternating), as if the owner alternates with the other in benefit from his property on condition that whenever he wishes he can take back the 'ariyah and return his turn. This is also said by al-Batlayusi. Therefore, in homogeneous things (mithl, mawzun), it is a loan (qard) because benefit cannot be had without consuming the substance, and after consumption the identical thing cannot return in mithli and mawzun for turn; rather the turn returns in its equivalent. Azhari considered it from 'ara ash-shay' meaning to come and go; from that a vagabond is called 'ayyar because he roams around in his frivolities. The Arabs say a'arah and 'aarah like ata'ahu and ta'ahu. The legal definition will come later. Benefit: Among the benefits of giving 'ariyah is that the borrower (musta'ir) is distressed and restless due to his need, and Allah says: 'Who answers the distressed when he calls Him?' So the lender (mu'ir) by giving 'ariyah becomes like Allah's deputy in relieving distress, and according to the hadith 'Assume the characteristics of Allah's attributes', he becomes characterized with the attributes of the Lord. His saying: 'al-ariyah ja'izah etc.' The legal ruling of 'ariyah is that it is permissible (giving has reward, and receiving has no fault). Shaykh Muwaffaq said in al-Mughni that there is consensus of the Muslims on the permissibility and recommendation of 'ariyah because it is a type of kindness. 'And there is no way against the doers of good.' The Prophet himself borrowed from Safwan bin Umayyah on the day of Hunain thirty coats of mail, and according to another narration a hundred, so taking 'ariyah and...
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage opens the book of 'ariyah (gratuitous loan for use) in Ashraf al-Hidayah. It first states the ruling: 'ariyah is ja'iz (permissible). The proof: the Prophet borrowed armor from Safwan, which was a voluntary transaction, establishing its legitimacy. Then the commentator delves into the etymology of the word 'ariyah, addressing different scholarly opinions. Some derive it from 'ariyah (gift), others from 'ar (shame) because borrowing may cause shame to the borrower. But the preferred view is from i'arah (lending), as in al-Mughrib, because the Prophet's borrowing contradicts the shame theory. The meaning of alternating benefit (tanaawub) is also given, linking to the concept of qard. Then a benefit (fa'idah) is given: the virtue of granting 'ariyah is likened to Allah's response to the distressed, and the hadith 'takhallaqu bi akhlaq Allah' (adopt the attributes of Allah). Finally, the commentator returns to the ruling, citing consensus on its permissibility and recommendation. The passage sets the foundation for the legal definition and rules of 'ariyah.

Key Terms
عارية ('ariyah): A gratuitous loan of a non-consumable item for use, where the owner allows another to benefit from the item without compensation, with the item to be returned later.
مستعير (musta'ir): The borrower who receives the item for use.
معير (mu'ir): The lender who gives the item as 'ariyah.
إحسان (ihsan): Kindness or goodness; the basis for the recommendation of 'ariyah.
تناوب (tanaawub): Alternation; the idea that the owner alternates benefit with the borrower, as in the concept of 'ariyah being a turn-taking in benefit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary proof for the permissibility of 'ariyah?
A) A verse from the Quran about kindness.
B) The consensus of the Muslims as narrated by Shaykh Muwaffaq.
C) The Prophet's borrowing of armor from Safwan.
D) The linguistic derivation from i'arah.

Key Takeaway
'Ariyah is a permissible and recommended act of kindness, linguistically derived from i'arah (lending), and its practice reflects the divine attribute of answering the distressed.
