intermediate
8 min
The Ruling of Aariyah: Permissibility and Proofs
Establishes aariyah as permissible via Quran, hadith, and ijma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on aariyah and identify the Quranic, hadith, and ijma proofs for its permissibility.

Core Idea
Aariyah is a commendable act of kindness, proven by the Prophet's own practice.

In this lesson, we examine the legal status of aariyah—lending an item for free use. The Hanafi school holds it to be permissible (ja'iz) and recommended (mustahabb). The author cites multiple proofs: the Quranic verse criticizing those who withhold small items (al-Ma'un), the Prophet's borrowing of coats of mail from Safwan and a horse from Abu Talha, and the consensus of the scholars. We will walk through each proof and understand why aariyah is not a shameful act but a form of ihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is aariyah? What is its hukm level? In the Hanafi school, it is ja'iz (permissible) and mustahabb (recommended).
The passage opens with 'al-ʿāriyatu jā'izah'.
2
Understand the linguistic discussion
Why does the author discuss the etymology? To refute the misconception that 'aariyah' is derived from 'ar' (disgrace). The author shows it is from 'ta'awur' (alternating benefit).
The Prophet's borrowing disproves any connection to shame.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
The verse 'and they withhold al-ma'un' (small kindnesses) implies praise for lending such items, making aariyah a good deed.
Al-ma'un includes items like buckets and axes commonly lent.
4
Analyze the hadith proofs
Two hadiths are cited: the Prophet borrowed coats of mail from Safwan at Hunayn, and a horse from Abu Talha during a panic. Both show the permissibility and commendability of borrowing and lending.
The hadith of Safwan also indicates that aariyah is a trust (maḍmūnah) to be returned.
5
Note the ijma
The text states there is consensus (ijma') among Muslims on the permissibility and recommended nature of aariyah.
Referenced from al-Mughni by Ibn Qudamah.

كتاب العارية
عاریت کی شرعی حیثیت
قَالَ الْعَارِيَةُ جَائِزَةٌ لِأَنَّهُ نَوْعُ إِحْسَانِ وَقَدْ اسْتَعَارَ النَّبِيُّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ دُرُوعًا مِنْ صَفْوَانَ
ترجمہ: عاریت جائز ہے کیونکہ یہ ایک طرح کا احسان ہے اور خود آنحضرت صلی الله علیہ وسلم نے حضرت صفوان بن امیہ سے لی تھیں۔
تشریح: قوله کتاب الخ اس کی وجہ مناسبت تو ہم کتاب الوديعة کے آغاز میں ذکر کر چکے کہ ان میں ہر ایک امانت ہے۔ رہی لفظ عاریت کی لفظی و شرعی تحقیق: لفظ عاریت یاء مشرق کے ساتھ أصح ہے۔ اور تخفیف بھی جائز ہے جیسا کہ قاموس میں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے اس کو عربیہ بمعنی عطیہ سے مانا ہے جس میں علامہ بدرالدین عینی وغیرہ نے مناقشہ کیا ہے جو آگے صفحات پر آ رہا ہے۔ جوہری اور ابن الاثیر وغیرہ نے کہا ہے کہ یہ عاریہ کی طرف منسوب ہے کیونکہ دوسرے سے عاریہ چیز مانگنا باعث عیب ہے (مصباح و شرح نقایہ) صاحب مغرب نے عارہ کی طرف منسوب مانا ہے جو اعارہ کا اسم ہے اور عار معنی عیب کی طرف منسوب ہونے کی تردید کی ہے۔ چنانچہ مغرب میں ہے:
العارية اصلها عورية فعلية منسوبة الى العارة اسم من الاعارة كالغارة من الاغارة واخذها من العار العيب او العرى خطاء اھ
وجه تردید یہ ہے کہ عاریائی ہے اور عاریتہ وادی ہے۔ ائمہ لغت نے اس کی تصریح کی ہے۔ صاحب نہایہ کہتے ہیں کہ مغرب میں جو مذکورہ ہے اس پر اعتماد ہے اس واسطے کہ آنحضرت صلی الله علیہ وسلم کا عاریت طلب کرنا حدیث سے ثابت ہے اگر یہ چیز باعث عار ہوتی تو آپ ہرگز طلب نہ فرماتے۔ مبسوط میں ہے کہ تعاور بمعنی تناوب سے ہے گویا مالک اپنی ملک سے غیر کے لئے نفع اٹھانے کی باری کرتا ہے اس شرط پر کہ وہ جب چاہے عاریت واپس لے کر اپنی نوبت لوٹا لے گا (وقاله البطلیوسی ایضاً) اسی لئے اعادہ کمیل و موزون میں قرض ہوتا ہے کیونکہ ان میں سے انتفاع استهلاک عین کے بغیر نہیں ہوسکتا اور استهلاک عین کے بعد بعینہ میل و موزون میں باری نہیں لوٹ سکتی یہاں تک کہ وہ حقیقة عاریت ہو بلکہ باری اس کے مثل میں لوٹے گی ازہری نے اس کو عار الشئی سے مانا ہے بمعنی آنا جانا اس سے بطال یعنی آوارہ گرد کو عیار کہتے ہیں کیونکہ وہ اپنی لغویات میں گھومتا پھرتا ہے۔ والعرب تقول اعاره و عاره مثل اطاعه و طاعہ۔ شرعی تعریف آگے آ رہی ہے۔ فائدہ: عاریت دینے کے محاسن میں سے ایک عمدہ خوبی یہ بھی ہے کہ مستعیر اپنی حاجت و ضرورت کی وجہ سے مضطر اور بے قرار ہوتا ہے اور حق تعالی کا ارشاد ہے:
"أَمَّنْ يُجِيبُ الْمُضْطَرَّ إِذَا دَعَاهُ"
ترجمہ: آیا کوئی سنتا ہے بے قرار کی جب وہ اس کو پکارے۔
پس معیر مستعیر کو عاریت دے کر اس کی فریادرسی اور حاجت روائی میں گویا اللہ کا نائب اور بحکم حدیث "تخلقوا بأخلاق الله" متخلق بأخلاق ربانی ہوا۔ قوله العارية جائزة الخ: عاریت کا شرعی حکم یہ ہے کہ یہ جائز ہے (دینے میں ثواب ہے اور لینے میں بھی کوئی عیب نہیں ہے) شیخ موفق نے المغنی میں کہا ہے کہ عاریت کے جواز اور اس کے استحباب پر مسلمانوں کا اجماع ہے کیونکہ یہ ایک طرح کا احسان ہے.. وما على المحسنين من سبيل۔ خود آنحضرت صلی الله علیہ وسلم کا حضرت صفوان بن امیہ سے حنین کے دن تیس (30) زِرْهیں اور ایک روایت کے مطابق سو (100) زِرْهیں عاریت لینا اور حضرت ابوطلحہ سے ان کا مندوب نامی گھوڑا بطور عاریت لینا احادیث سے ثابت ہے۔ چنانچہ امام ابوداؤد، نسائی، احمد اور حضرت صفوان بن امیہ سے حاکم اور دار قطنی نے حضرت ابن عباس سے حاکم نے حضرت جابر بن عبداللہ سے بالفاظ مختلفہ روایت کیا ہے۔
إِنَّ النَّبي صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ استعار منه دروعًا يوم حنين فقال: أغصباً؟ يا محمد! قال: بل عاريته مضمونة.
نبی کریم صلی الله علیہ وسلم نے جنگ حنین کے دن ان سے (یعنی حضرت صفوان سے) کئی زرہیں عاریہ کی ہیں انہوں نے کہا: اے محمد کیا یہ غصب لے رہے ہو؟ آپ نے فرمایا: بلکہ عاریتہ لے رہا ہوں جو واپس کر دی جائیں گی۔
نیز شیخین نے حضرت انس سے روایت کیا ہے: قال: كان فزع بالمدينة فاستعار النبي فرسا من ابي طلحة يقال له المندوب فركب فلما رجع قال: ما رأينا من شيء وإن وجدنا لبحراً. (حضرت انس نے فرمایا کہ ایک دن مدینہ میں گھبراہٹ پیدا ہوئی تو آنحضرت صلی الله علیہ وسلم نے حضرت ابوطلحہ کا مندوب نامی گھوڑا عاریۃً لیا اور اس پر سوار ہو کر نکلے پھر جب واپس تشریف لائے تو فرمایا کہ میں نے گھبراہٹ کی کوئی چیز نہیں دیکھی۔ نیز میں نے اس گھوڑے کو نہیں پایا مگر کشادہ قدم اور تیز رفتار)
قرآن پاک میں حق تعالی کا ارشاد ہے:
"وَيَمْنَعُونَ الْمَاعُونَ"
ترجمہ: اور وہ مانگے نہیں دیتے برتنے کی چیز۔
ماعون اس معمولی چیز کو کہتے ہیں جس کو عاریۃً دے دینے کا عام رواج ہو جیسے دول، رس، ہانڈی، ہوئی، کلہاڑی وغیرہ آیت میں معمولی چیز مانگے نہ دینے والوں کی مذمت کی گئی ہے تو عاریت دینا محمود ٹھہرا۔
The Book of Aariyah. The legal status of aariyah. He said: Aariyah is permissible because it is a type of kindness, and the Prophet, peace be upon him, borrowed coats of mail from Safwan. Translation: Aariyah is permissible because it is a type of kindness, and the Prophet himself borrowed from Safwan bin Umayyah. Commentary: ... (continues with detailed linguistic and legal analysis).
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It opens by stating that aariyah (lending an item for free use) is permissible (ja'iz), not obligatory. The Hanafi position is that it is a recommended act of kindness (ihsan). The proof includes the Prophet's own practice: he borrowed coats of mail from Safwan bin Umayyah at the Battle of Hunayn, and a horse from Abu Talha during a panic in Madinah. These hadiths are cited from authentic collections. Additionally, the Quranic verse 'and they withhold small kindnesses' (al-Ma'un) implies praise for giving such items on loan. The passage also includes a lengthy linguistic discussion on the etymology of 'aariyah', concluding it is not from 'ar' (disgrace) but rather from 'ta'awur' (alternating benefit). The core ruling is that aariyah is a commendable act, not sinful to request or grant.

Key Terms
العارية (al-ʿāriyah): A contract whereby the owner permits another to use an item without compensation, with the obligation to return the specific item.
إحسان (iḥsān): Beneficence; doing good to others. Here it is the reason given for the permissibility of aariyah.
الماعون (al-māʿūn): Small household items commonly lent, such as a bucket, rope, pot, axe, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence from the Prophet's life for the permissibility of aariyah?
A) He borrowed a sword from Ali at Uhud.
B) He borrowed coats of mail from Safwan at Hunayn.
C) He borrowed a camel from Abu Bakr during the Hijra.
D) He borrowed a house from Umm Hani on the Conquest of Makkah.

Key Takeaway
Aariyah is permissible and recommended in the Hanafi school, supported by the Prophet's actions, Quranic implication, and scholarly consensus.

The Obligation of Aariyah: Hanafi vs Zahiri
Refutes the claim that aariyah is fard using hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on aariyah, explain the evidence for both sides, and evaluate why the Hanafi tarjih is the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
No right in wealth besides zakat — aariyah is recommended, not obligatory.

This lesson presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute: does a lender have an obligation to lend an item to a needy person? Ibn Hazm and the Zahiri school argue it is fard based on a hadith about the rights of camels. The Hanafi school, however, maintains that aariyah is only recommended (mustahabb), relying on explicit hadiths that limit compulsory financial obligations to zakat alone. Understanding this dispute clarifies how Hanafi usul prioritises explicit texts (nass) over general indications.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that giving aariyah (lending an item) is recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory. Refusal does not incur sin.
2
Identify the opposing school and their proof
Ibn Hazm and the Zahiris consider aariyah fard (obligatory) when the borrower is needy and trustworthy, citing a hadith: the Prophet listed lending vessels, stud animal, and milk as rights of camels.
The hadith is from Abu Huraira; it is a hadith ahad.
3
Follow the opponent's dalil
The Zahiri school argues that the word 'right' (haqq) implies obligation, and the camel hadith specifies aariyah as part of the due of wealth.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds with two explicit hadiths: 'If you have paid zakat, you have fulfilled what is required' and 'No right in wealth besides zakat.' These nass override any general indication in the camel hadith.
The Hanafi response also notes that the camel hadith is interpreted as recommendation, not obligation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: according to Ibn Hazm, refusing to lend to a needy person is sinful; according to Hanafis, it is not sinful but one misses reward. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعض حضرات کی رائے یہ ہے کہ عاریت دینا واجب ہے۔ چنانچہ ابن حزم نے محلی میں کہا ہے:
"و من سألها محتاجًا ففرض عليه إعارته إياها إذا وثق بوفائه"
جب کوئی بحالت احتیاج کوئی چیز مانگے تو عاریت فرض ہے جب کہ اس کی واپسی کا اعتماد ہو۔
کیونکہ حضرت ابوہریرہ سے حدیث ہے ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: "ما من صاحب إبل لا يؤدي حقها" قيل: يا رسول الله (صلى الله عليه وسلم) وما حقها؟ قال: "إعارة دبوبها وإطراق فحلها ومنحة لبنها يوم وردها."
جواب یہ ہے کہ ابن ماجہ اور المنذر نے باسناد حسن حضرت ابوہریرہ سے آپ کا ارشاد روایت کیا ہے: "إذا أديت زكاة مالك فقد قضيت ما عليك" نیز ابن ماجہ نے باسناد حسن فاطمہ بنت قیس سے مرفوعا روایت کیا ہے: "ليس في المال حق سوى الزكوة"
Some people are of the opinion that giving aariyah is obligatory. Thus Ibn Hazm said in al-Muhalla: 'And whoever asks for it while in need, it is obligatory upon the owner to lend it to him if he has confidence in its return.' Because there is a hadith from Abu Huraira that the Prophet said: 'There is no owner of camels who does not give their due.' It was said: O Messenger of Allah, what is their due? He said: 'Lending their milking vessels, letting their stud be used, and giving their milk on the day of watering.' The answer is that Ibn Majah and al-Mundhiri narrated with a hasan chain from Abu Huraira that he said: 'If you have paid the zakat of your wealth, you have fulfilled what is required of you.' Also Ibn Majah narrated with a hasan chain from Fatimah bint Qays as a marfu' hadith: 'There is no right in wealth besides zakat.'
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. It presents the view of some scholars (e.g., Ibn Hazm) who argue that aariyah is obligatory when the borrower is in need and trustworthy, citing a hadith about the rights of camels. The Hanafi position, however, refutes this. The refutation relies on two hadiths: one stating that paying zakat fulfills all obligations on wealth, and another explicitly stating that there is no right in wealth besides zakat. Thus, aariyah remains a recommended act, not an obligatory one. The Hanafi school holds that making aariyah obligatory would contradict the explicit text that only zakat is compulsory in wealth. This is a clear example of tarjih (preference) based on stronger evidence.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): Obligatory; an act that must be performed and omission is sinful.
زكاة (zakāh): The compulsory alms on wealth, which is the only obligatory financial right in the Hanafi view.
إعارة (iʿārah): The act of lending an item for use without charge; synonym for aariyah.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended; performing it brings reward, omitting it is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which hadith does the Hanafi school use to argue that aariyah is not obligatory?
A) The hadith about rights of camels.
B) 'If you have paid zakat, you have fulfilled what is required.'
C) 'Help your brother, whether he is an oppressor or oppressed.'
D) 'The best charity is that given when you are healthy and need.'

Key Takeaway
Aariyah is not obligatory because the only compulsory right in wealth is zakat, as established by explicit prophetic traditions.

The Definition of 'Ariyah: Tamlik vs Ibaha
Defines 'ariyah and presents the tamlik vs ibaha dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two definitions of 'ariyah (tamlik and ibaha) and explain the Hanafi tarjih in favor of tamlik with its supporting arguments.

Core Idea
'Ariyah is ownership of usufruct without compensation—the borrower owns the right to use, not just permission.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya opens the chapter on 'Ariyah (loan). It presents the definitional dispute at the heart of the contract: is 'ariyah a transfer of ownership of usufruct (tamlik) or mere permission to benefit (ibaha)? The author champions the tamlik view, rebutting the arguments of Imam al-Karkhi and the Shafi'i school. Understanding this dispute shapes the legal consequences of the loan—the borrower's rights and the lender's ability to revoke.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Locate the Hanafi majority definition (tamlik al-manafi') and al-Karkhi's alternative (ibahat al-intifa').
Tamlik = ownership; ibaha = permission.
2
Analyze al-Karkhi's evidence
List his four arguments: concluded with words of ibaha, no term required, prohibition terminates it, borrower cannot sublease.
Each argument challenges the tamlik view.
3
Evaluate the Hanafi response
How does the author rebut each? Note the linguistic derivation from 'ariyyah (gift) and the analogy with physical objects.
The author argues that usufruct can be owned like physical objects.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What practical difference does the definition make? For example, can the lender revoke after use? Can the borrower sublease?
Tamlik gives stronger rights, but still revocable before use.
5
State the mufta bihi
Confirm the relied-upon Hanafi position: tamlik, as supported by the majority and the author.
Al-Karkhi's view is a minority position within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب العارية.
وَهِيَ تَمْلِيْكُ الْمَنَافِعِ بِغَيْرِ عِوَضِ وَكَانَ الْكَرْخِي يَقُولُ هِيَ إِبَاحَةُ الْإِنْتِفَاعِ بِمِلْكِ الْغَيْرِ لِأَنَّهَا تَنْعَقِدُ بِلَفْظَةِ الْإِبَاحَةِ وَلَا يُشْتَرَطُ فِيهِ ضَرْبُ الْمُدَّةِ وَمَعَ الْجِهَالَةِ لَا يَصِحُ التَّمْلِكُ وَكَذَالِكَ يَعْمَلُ فِيهِ النَّهى وَلَا يَـ الْإِجَارَةُ مِنْ غَيْرِهِ وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ إِنَّهُ يُنْبِيءُ عَنِ التَّمْلِيْكِ فَإِنَّ الْعَارِيَةَ مِنَ الْعَرِيَّةِ وَهِيَ الْعَطِيَّةُ وَلِهَذَا يَنْعَقِدُ بِلَفْظَةِ السَّمْلِيْكِ وَالْمُنَافِعِ قَابِلَةٌ لِلْمِلْكِ كَالْاعْيَانِ وَالتَّمْلِيْكُ نَوْعَانِ بِعَوَضٍ وَبِغَيْرِ عِوَضٍ ثُمَّ الْأَعْيَانِ تَقْبَلُ النَّوْعَيْنِ فَكَذَا الْمَنَافِعُ وَالْجَامِعُ بَيْنَهُمَا دَفْعُ الْحَاجَةِ
It is the ownership of usufruct without compensation. Al-Karkhi used to say: it is the permission to benefit from the property of another, because it is concluded with the word of permission, and stipulation of a term is not required in it, and with ignorance (of duration) ownership is not valid, and similarly prohibition is effective in it, and the borrower cannot lease it to another. And we say: it indicates ownership, because 'ariyah is derived from 'ariyyah which is a gift, and therefore it is concluded with the word of ownership. And usufructs are capable of being owned like physical objects. And ownership is of two types: with compensation and without compensation. Then physical objects accept both types, so also do usufructs. And the common factor between them is the fulfillment of need.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya opens the chapter on 'Ariyah (loan). It defines 'ariyah as 'tamlik al-manafi' bi ghayr 'iwad' – ownership of usufruct without compensation. This is the position of the majority of Hanafi scholars, as adopted by the author. It then presents the view of Imam al-Karkhi, a prominent Hanafi jurist, who defined it as 'ibahat al-intifa' bi milk al-ghayr' – permission to benefit from the property of another. Al-Karkhi gave four arguments: (1) it is concluded with the word of ibaha (permission), (2) no fixed term is required, whereas tamlik with ignorance of duration is invalid, (3) the lender's prohibition is effective in terminating it, unlike a completed ownership, (4) the borrower cannot lease it to another, unlike if he owned the usufruct. The author refutes these by asserting that 'ariyah linguistically derives from 'ariyyah (gift), implying transfer of ownership, and analogically usufruct can be owned like physical objects. He reduces the four objections by showing that ownership can also be restricted; the prohibition works because it is a revocable gift. The author's view aligns with the relied-upon Hanafi position. The passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of defining legal terms through linguistic derivation and qiyas.

Key Terms
عَارِيَة ('āriyah): A contract whereby the owner (mu'ir) gives the usufruct of his property to another (musta'ir) without compensation.
تَمْلِيْكُ الْمَنَافِعِ (tamlik al-manāfi'): Transfer of ownership of the usufruct (the right to use) from the owner to the borrower.
إِبَاحَةُ الْإِنْتِفَاعِ (ibāḥat al-intifā'): Permission to benefit; the borrower is allowed to use the item but does not own the usufruct as property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi definition in this passage, what is 'ariyah?
A) Permission to benefit from the property of another
B) Ownership of the usufruct without compensation
C) A revocable gift of the physical object
D) A rental contract with no term

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines 'ariyah as ownership of usufruct without compensation, rejecting the permission-based definition due to linguistic and analogical evidence.

12 min
Definition of 'Ariyah: Tamlik vs Ibaha Dispute
Dispute between Hanafi majority and Imam al-Karkhi on definition of 'Ariyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two definitions of 'Ariyah (tamlik al-manfa'ah vs ibahat al-intifa') and explain the Hanafi response to al-Karkhi's four proofs.

Core Idea
'Ariyah is ownership of usufruct without compensation, not mere permission.

The correct legal definition of 'Ariyah (loan for use) is contested within the Hanafi school. While the majority of Hanafi scholars define it as a transfer of ownership of the usufruct without compensation (tamlik al-manfa'ah bi-ghayr 'iwad), Imam al-Karkhi and others argue it is merely a permission to benefit (ibahat al-intifa'). This lesson examines the four proofs for the ibaha view and the authoritative Hanafi response that upholds the tamlik definition.

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi definition of 'Ariyah
Begin with the definition given in the text: 'al-ariyah tamlik al-manfa'ah bi-ghayr 'iwad' — ownership of the usufruct without compensation. Identify the key terms: tamlik (ownership transfer), manfa'ah (usufruct), and bi-ghayr 'iwad (without consideration).
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position of the Hanafi school.
2
Identify Imam al-Karkhi's alternative definition
State al-Karkhi's view: 'Ariyah is ibahat al-intifa' — permission to benefit from another's property. Note that this view is shared by Imams al-Shafi'i and Ahmad.
Al-Karkhi's definition denies any ownership transfer; it is a mere permission.
3
List al-Karkhi's four proofs
The text mentions four pieces of evidence: (1) 'Ariyah can be concluded with words of ibaha (e.g., 'abtu'ka'), (2) duration need not be specified, (3) the mu'ir can revoke the loan by prohibition, and (4) the musta'ir cannot sublease the item. Write each down and consider why each is seen as inconsistent with tamlik.
These are the strongest objections from the ibaha school.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to each proof
For each proof, note the Hanafi counter-argument: (1) 'Ariyah derives from 'Ariyyah (gift), implying tamlik; it can be concluded with tamlik wording. (2) Duration is not required in all tamlik contracts (e.g., hiba). (3) Revocability is a feature of non-binding gifts, not a denial of ownership transfer. (4) The musta'ir's inability to sublease is because he lacks full ownership, similar to a donee before possession.
The Hanafi response shows that the four proofs do not actually disprove tamlik.
5
Examine the qiyas (analogy) used by the Hanafis
The Hanafis argue that usufructs (manafi') are capable of ownership like physical objects (a'yan) because both can be transferred with or without compensation. The common cause (jami') is 'daf' al-hajah' (fulfillment of need). Complete the qiyas: asl = physical objects, far' = usufructs, illa = ability to be owned and the need.
This analogy is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) and is central to the Hanafi proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْإِبَاحَةِ وَلَا يُشْتَرَطُ فِيهِ ضَرْبُ الْمُدَّةِ وَمَعَ الْجِهَالَةِ لَا يَصِحُ التَّمْلِكُ وَكَذَالِكَ يَعْمَلُ فِيهِ النَّهى وَلَا يَـ الْإِجَارَةُ مِنْ غَيْرِهِ وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ إِنَّهُ يُنْبِيءُ عَنِ التَّمْلِيْكِ فَإِنَّ الْعَارِيَةَ مِنَ الْعَرِيَّةِ وَهِيَ الْعَطِيَّةُ وَلِهَذَا يَنْعَقِدُ بِلَفْظَةِ السَّمْلِيْكِ وَالْمُنَافِعِ قَابِلَةٌ لِلْمِلْكِ كَالْاعْيَانِ وَالتَّمْلِيْكُ نَوْعَانِ بِعَوَضٍ وَبِغَيْرِ عِوَضٍ ثُمَّ الْأَعْيَانِ تَقْبَلُ النَّوْعَيْنِ فَكَذَا الْمَنَافِعُ وَالْجَامِعُ بَيْنَهُمَا دَفْعُ الْحَاجَةِ
ترجمہ اور عاریت منافع کا مالک بنانا ہے بلاعوض اور امام کرخی فرماتے تھے کہ عاریت ملک غیر سے انتفاع کی اباحت ہے کیونکہ عاریت اباحت کے لفظ سے منعقد ہو جاتی ہے۔ اور اس میں بیان مدت شرط نہیں ہے۔ حالانکہ مجہول ہونے کے ساتھ تملیک صحیح نہیں ہوتی۔ اسی طرح اس میں نہی کارگر ہوتی ہے۔ اور مستغیر کسی دوسرے کو اجارہ پر دینے کا مالک نہیں ہوتا اور ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ لفظ عاریت تملیک سے باخبر کرتا ہے۔ کیونکہ عاریہ بمعنی عطیہ سے ہے اس لئے عاریت تملیک کے لفظ سے منعقد ہو جاتی ہے اور منافع قابل ملک ہوتے ہیں اعیان کی طرح اور تملیک دو طرح پر ہوتی ہے ایک بعوض دوم بلاعوض ۔ پھر اعیان دونوں قسموں کے قابل ہیں تو ایسے ہی منافع بھی ہوں گے اور امر جامع ان دونوں میں دفع حاجت ہے۔ تشریح قوله وهى تمليك اصطلاح شرع میں عام علماء کے نزدیک بلاعوض تملیک منافع کو عاریت کہتے ہیں جو شخص مالک منائے اس کو معیر اور جس کو مالک بنایا جائے اس کو مستغیر اور جس چیز کی منفعت کا مالک بنایا جائے اس کو عاریت اور مستعار کہتے ہیں۔ افواہ اودی کا شعر ہے انمانـعـمـتـه قـوم متعة وحياة المرء ثوب مستعار
تعریف میں بلا عوض کی قید سے اجارہ نکل گیا کہ اس میں گو منافع کی تملیک ہوتی ہے مگر بلا عوض نہیں ہوتی، فائدہ عاریت دنیا ایک طرح کا تبرع اور احسان ہے اور عقد تبرع صرف ایجاب پر موقوف ہوتا ہے اسی لئے فتاوی عالمگیری میں کہا ہے کہ عاریت کا رکن صرف معیر کی جانب سے ایجاب کا ہونا ہے رہا مستغیر کی جانب سے قبول کرنا سو ہمارے اصحاب ثلثہ کے نزدیک از روئے استحسان شرط نہیں ہے ۔ پھر ایجاب کا قولی ہونا ضروری ہے ۔ چنانچہ خانیہ میں ہے کہ اگر کسی نے عاریت مانگی اور معیر خاموش رہا تو یہ عاریت نہ ہوگی۔ البتہ قبول کا قولی ہونا کوئی ضروری نہیں فعلی بھی ہو سکتا ہے۔ مثلاً معیر نے کہا کہ یہ کپڑا عاریت کے طور پر لے لے مستعبیر نے اپنا ہاتھ پھیلایا اور کپڑا لے لیا۔
قوله و كان الكرخی کتاب میں جو عاریت کو تملیک کہا گیا ہے۔ یہ قول شیخ ابو بکر رازی کے اختیار پر ہے۔ شیخ ابوالحسن کرخی فرماتے تھے کہ غیر کی ملک سے انتفاع مباع ہونے کو عاریت کہتے ہیں۔ امام شافعی اور امام احمد کا قول بھی یہی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے اس قول کی چارو جہیں
ذکر کی ہیں۔ اول ..... یہ کہ عاریت اباحت کے لفظ سے منعقد ہو جاتی ہے۔ چنانچہ مغیر اگر یہ کہے بہت لک هزا الثواب تو یہ عاریت ہوتی ہے۔ حالانکہ تملیک اباحت کے لفظ سے منعقد نہیں ہوتی۔
دوم یہ کہ عاریت میں بیان شرط نہیں ہے۔ یعنی بیان مدت کے ساتھ منفعت کی مقدار سے باخبر کرناضروری نہیں ۔ حالانکہ مدت مجہول ہونے کے ساتھ منافع کی تملیک صحیح نہیں ہوتی جیسے اجارہ میں ہے۔
سوم ..... یہ کہ عاریت میں مغیر کا منع کر دینا مؤثر ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی معیر اگر کہہ دے کہ آئندہ عاریت سے کام نہ لینا تو منع مفید ہوتا ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اس سے عاریت ٹوٹ جاتی ہے۔ اگر عاریت تملیک ہوتی تو میر کو منع کرنے کا اختیار نہ ہوتا جیسے ہبہ اور اجارہ میں اختیار نہیں ہوتا۔ چہارم یہ کہ مستعمیر کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہے کہ وہ کسی دوسرے کو عاریت کی چیز اجارہ پر دے اگر عاریت تملیک ہوتی تو اجارہ پر دینا جائز ہوتا۔ کیونکہ
قوله ونحن نقول ... امام کرخی کے جواب میں ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ لفظ عاریت سے تملیک کے معنی نکلتے ہیں کیونکہ یہ عربیہ معنی عطیہ سے مشتق ہے اسی لئے عاریت تملیک کے لفظ سے منعقد ہو جاتی ہے بان يقول ملكتك منفعة دارى هذه شهراً (ذكره في المسبوط ) ممکن ہے اس پر کوئی یہ کہے کہ منافع تو اعراض ہیں۔ جو باقی نہیں رہتے ۔ پس یہ قابل تملیک نہ ھوں گے۔ صاحب ہدایہ اپنے قول والمنافع قابلة للملك كا الاعیان سے اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ ایعیان کی طرح منافع بھی قابل تملیک ہیں اس لیئے کہ تملیک دو طرح سے ہوتی ہے،
ایک بالعوض دوم بلاعوض
پھر اعیان ان دونوں قسموں کے قابل ہے ( تملیک عین بالعوض جیسے ہیں اور صدقہ ) تو منافع بھی ان دونوں کے قابل ہوں گے (پس تملیک منافع بالعوض جیسے اجارہ اور تملیک منافع بلا عوض جیسے عاریت) کیونکہ امر جامع یعنی دفع حاجت دونوں میں موجود قال الزيلعي كل ما جا زفيه التمليك ببدل جازفيه التمليك بغير بدل الا النكاح
...and it is not a condition in it to stipulate a duration, and with ignorance tamlik is not valid. similarly, prohibition is effective in it, and he cannot give ijara to another. And we say: it (the word ariyah) indicates tamlik, because ariyah is from ariyyah which means gift, therefore it is concluded with the word tamlik. And usufructs are capable of ownership like physical objects. And tamlik is of two types: with compensation and without compensation. Then physical objects accept both types, so also usufructs. And the common cause between them is fulfillment of need. Translation: And ariyah is making possession of usufruct without compensation. And Imam al-Karkhi used to say: ariyah is permission to benefit from the property of another, because ariyah is concluded with the word ibaha. And stipulation of duration is not a condition in it. Whereas with ignorance tamlik is not valid. Similarly, prohibition is effective in it. And the musta'ir does not have the right to give another ijara. And we say: the word ariyah indicates tamlik, because ariyah is from ariyyah meaning gift, therefore ariyah is concluded with the word tamlik. And usufructs are capable of ownership like physical objects. And tamlik is of two types: with compensation and without compensation. Then physical objects accept both types, so also usufructs. And the common cause between them is fulfillment of need. Elaboration: His saying 'and it is tamlik': In the terminology of Shara', according to the majority of scholars, ariyah is tamlik of usufruct without compensation. The person who makes the owner is called mu'ir, the one made owner is called musta'ir, and the thing whose usufruct is owned is called ariyah and musta'ar. The verse of Aws ibn Aws [poetry unclear] ... In the definition, the condition 'without compensation' excludes ijara, because in ijara there is tamlik of usufruct but with compensation. Benefit: Ariyah is a kind of beneficence and favor, and a contract of beneficence depends only on offer. For this reason it is stated in Fatawa Alamgiri that the pillar of ariyah is only the offer from the mu'ir; as for acceptance from the musta'ir, according to our three imams it is not a condition by istihsan. Then the offer must be verbal. Accordingly, in al-Khaniyyah it is stated that if someone requests ariyah and the mu'ir remains silent, it is not ariyah. However, acceptance need not be verbal; it can be physical. For example, the mu'ir says 'take this cloth as ariyah', the musta'ir stretches out his hand and takes the cloth. His saying 'and al-Karkhi': In the book, what is called ariyah is tamlik. This is a choice of Shaykh Abu Bakr al-Razi. Shaykh Abul Hasan al-Karkhi used to say: Ariyah is called permission to benefit from the property of another. Imam al-Shafi'I and Imam Ahmad also held this view. The author of al-Hidayah mentioned four proofs for this view: First: Ariyah is concluded with the word ibaha. For example, if the mu'ir says 'I allow you to benefit from this garment' (bittuka hadha al-thawb [?]), that is ariyah, whereas tamlik is not concluded with the word ibaha. Second: In ariyah, stipulation of duration is not a condition, i.e., it is not necessary to inform of the quantity of usufruct by specifying duration. Whereas with unknown duration, tamlik of usufruct is not valid, as in ijara. Third: In ariyah, the mu'ir's prohibition is effective. That is, if the mu'ir says 'do not use the ariyah from now', the prohibition is effective, even to the point that the ariyah is terminated. If ariyah were tamlik, the mu'ir would not have the right to prohibit, just as in hiba and ijara he has no such right. Fourth: The musta'ir does not have the right to give the ariyah item to another on ijara; if ariyah were tamlik, it would be permissible to give it on ijara, because whoever owns something without compensation can make another owner with compensation, like the donee (mawhub lahu). His saying 'and we say...' In response to Imam al-Karkhi, we say that the word ariyah conveys the meaning of tamlik, because it is derived from ariyyah meaning gift, therefore ariyah is concluded with the word tamlik, such that the mu'ir says 'I grant you ownership of the usufruct of this house for one month' (mentioned in al-Mabsut). It may be objected that usufructs are accidents that do not endure, so they cannot be owned. The author of al-Hidayah responds with his statement 'and usufructs are capable of ownership like physical objects': just as physical objects can be owned, so too usufructs, because tamlik is of two types: with compensation and without compensation. Then physical objects are capable of both types (tamlik of the object with compensation like sale, and without compensation like gift and charity), so likewise usufructs are capable of both (tamlik of usufruct with compensation like ijara, and without compensation like ariyah) because the common cause, i.e., fulfillment of need, is present in both. Al-Zayla'i said: Everything in which tamlik with compensation is permissible, tamlik without compensation is also permissible except for marriage.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed dispute over the definition of 'Ariyah (loan for use). The majority of Hanafi scholars define it as 'tamlik al-manfa'ah bi-ghayr 'iwad' — a transfer of ownership of the usufruct without compensation. Imam al-Karkhi, however, defines it as 'ibahat al-intifa'' — mere permission to benefit, not ownership. Al-Karkhi's view is shared by Imams al-Shafi'i and Ahmad. The author then lists four proofs for the ibaha view: (1) 'Ariyah can be concluded with words of permission (ibaha) like 'Abtu'ka', whereas tamlik cannot; (2) duration need not be specified, but tamlik of usufruct with unknown duration is invalid; (3) the mu'ir can revoke the 'Ariyah by prohibition, which is inconsistent with tamlik; (4) the borrower cannot sublease, but an owner could. The Hanafi response counters each: linguistically, 'Ariyah derives from 'Ariyyah (gift), implying tamlik, and it can be concluded with explicit tamlik wording. Usufructs (manafi') are property and can be owned like physical objects (a'yan), as tamlik applies to both with and without compensation. The common cause (jami') is the fulfillment of need (daf' al-hajah). Al-Zayla'i's principle is cited: anything that can be owned with compensation can also be owned without, except marriage. The Hanafi position is that 'Ariyah is a type of tamlik, not mere ibaha.

Key Terms
عاریة (ʿāriyah): A contract of loaning a specific item for use without charge, with the usufruct owned without compensation.
تملیک المنفعة (tamlīk al-manfaʿah): Transfer of ownership of the usufruct (benefit) of an object to another person.
اباحة الانتفاع (ibāḥat al-intifāʿ): Mere permission to benefit without any ownership transfer.
معیر (muʿīr): The owner who lends the item; the lender in ariyah.
مستعیر (mustaʿīr): The person who receives the loan for use; the borrower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence the Hanafi majority uses to argue that 'Ariyah is tamlik al-manfa'ah?
A) The fact that the borrower can sublease the item.
B) The linguistic derivation of 'Ariyah from 'Ariyyah (gift) and its ability to be concluded with tamlik wording.
C) The requirement to specify a duration.
D) The fact that the lender cannot revoke the loan.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines 'Ariyah as tamlik al-manfa'ah bi-ghayr 'iwad, a transfer of ownership of the usufruct without compensation, based on linguistic derivation and analogy to physical objects.

Objections on Qiyas in the Definition of 'Ariyah and Their Hanafi Responses
Critical refinement on qiyas for 'Ariyah definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three objections raised against the qiyas used by al-Hidayah in defining 'ariyah and state the Hanafi responses using usul al-fiqh principles.

Core Idea
Qiyas on definitions targets the subsidiary legal ruling, not the definition itself.

This lesson examines a critical refinement by the author of al-`Inayah on the qiyas used in al-Hidayah to prove that usufructs (manafi') are ownable like physical objects (a'yan). The discussion clarifies the nature of definitions, the domain of qiyas, and the requirement of parallelism in qiyas. Understanding these objections sharpens your ability to handle usul al-fiqh critiques in Hanafi legal methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three objections
List each objection raised by the author of al-`Inayah: (1) definitions are tasawwurat and cannot be proven by istidlal, (2) qiyas is being applied to mawdu'at (linguistic usage) not legal rulings, and (3) usufructs are not parallel to physical objects as required for qiyas.
These objections represent a refined understanding of usul al-fiqh principles.
2
Analyze the Hanafi response to each objection
For each objection, trace the author's rebuttal: (1) the inference is on the subsidiary claim of correctness, not the definition itself; (2) the qiyas targets the legal capacity for ownership, not linguistic setting; (3) qiyas only requires sharing the 'illah, not total identity.
The responses clarify the precise domain of qiyas in Hanafi thought.
3
Extract the usul principles invoked
Identify the key usul rules: the distinction between tasawwurat and tasdiqat, the prohibition of qiyas in mawdu'at (but allowance in ahkam), and the condition of 'illah rather than full parallelism.
These principles are foundational for understanding when qiyas is valid.
4
Apply the resolved qiyas
Understand the outcome: by analogy to physical objects (which can be owned with or without compensation based on texts on sale and gift), usufructs are also capable of both types of tamlik because the 'illah (daf' al-hajah) is present in both.
This qiyas validates the permissibility of 'ariyah and other contracts involving usufructs.

Source Text

تنبیہ صاحب عنایہ نے اس مقام پر تین وجوہ سے بحث کی ہے۔
بحث اول کہ صاحب ہدایہ کا کلام مذکور تعریفات میں استدلال ہے حالانکہ تعریفات استدلال کو قبول نہیں کرتیں اس لئے کہ تعریفات از قبیل تصورات ہیں اور استدلال تصدیقات میں ہوتا ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ یہاں استدلال نفس تعریف پر نہیں ہے ( جواز قبیل تصورات ہے) بلکہ اس ضمنی حکم پر ہے۔ جس کا قصد معرف کیا کرتا ہے۔ بان يقول هذا التعريف هو الصحيح هذا التعرف هوا الحق هذا التعريف صحيح جامع مانع وغیرہ ۔ جیسا کہ یہ امر اپنی جگہ پر مصرح ہے کہ منع ونقص اور معارضہ وغیرہ کے جو اعتراضات تعریفات پر وارد کئے جاتے ہیں وہ احکام ضمینہ پر ہوتے ہیں نہ کہ نفس تعریفات پر۔
بحث دوم یہ کہ قیاس مذکور والمنافع قابلة للملك كالاعيان موضوعات میں ہے جو صیح نہیں۔ کیونکہ قیاس کے لئے یہ شرط ہے کہ جو شرعی حکم ثابت بالنص ہو وہ بعینہ اس فرع کی جانب متعدی ہو جو اس کی نظیر ہے اور یہاں کوئی نص موجود نہیں ۔ نیز موضوعات شرعی حکم بھی نہیں ہیں۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ صاحب ہدایہ کا مقصد عرف شرع میں بلاعوض تملیک منافع کے لئے لفظ عاریت کے موضوع ہونے کو بذریعہ قیاس ثابت کرنا نہیں ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ موضوعات میں قیاس ہونے کا اعتراض وارد ہو بلکہ اعیان جو تملیک کی دونوں قسموں کے قابل ہیں ان کے قیاس سے ۔ ثابت کرنا ہے کہ منافع بھی ان دونوں کے قابل ہیں اور اس اثبات سے معترض کا صرف یہ وہم دور کرنا ہے کہ اعراض چونکہ باقی نہیں رہتے اس ۔ یہ قابل تملیک نہیں ہو سکتے۔ اور یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ اعیان کا تملیک کی دونوں قسموں کو قبول کرنا ایک شرعی حکم ہے جو اس نص سے ثابت ہے۔ جو ج بیع و ہبہ پر دال ہے۔ فیصح تعديته الى قبول المنافع للهما ايضاً
بحث سوم یہ کہ قیاس کے لئے یہ بھی شرط ہے کہ حکم شرعی اس فرغ کی طرف متعدی ہو جو اس کی نظیر ہے اور یہاں منافع اعیان کی نظیر نہیں ؟ جواب یہ ہے کہ اگر نظیر نہ ہونے سے مراد یہ ہے کہ من کل الوجود نظیر نہیں ہے تو یہ تسلیم ہے مگر اس سے معترض کو کوئی فائدہ نہیں اس لئے کہ قیاس کے لئے فرع کا اصل کے ساتھ جمیع جہات میں اشتراک شرط نہیں ہے بلکہ ان دونوں کا صرف علت حکم میں شریک ہونا کافی ہے۔ اصول فقہ سے معلوم ہے اور اگر نظیر نہ ہونے سے مراد یہ ہے کہ علت حکم میں بھی نظیر نہیں ہے تو ی نا قابل تسلیم ہے اس لئے کہ یہاں تملیک ہو حکم ہے اس کی علت دفع حاجت ہے اور اس علت میں اعیان اور منافع دونوں مشترک ہیں۔ (نتائج)
Caution: The author of al-`Inayah has discussed three objections in this place. First objection: The speech of the author of al-Hidayah is an istidlal (inference) in definitions, whereas definitions do not accept istidlal because definitions belong to tasawwurat (concepts) and istidlal occurs in tasdiqat (propositions/assent). Answer: The istidlal here is not on the definition itself (which belongs to tasawwurat), but on the subsidiary ruling (hukm ḍimnī) that the definer intends, such as saying 'this definition is correct', 'this definition is the true one', 'this definition is sound, comprehensive, and exclusive', etc. As is explicitly stated elsewhere, the objections of opposition, deficiency, contradiction, etc., that are raised against definitions are actually on these subsidiary rulings, not on the definitions themselves. Second objection: The qiyas mentioned 'and usufructs are capable of ownership like physical objects' occurs in matters of linguistic usage (mawḍūʻāt), which is not correct, because for qiyas it is a condition that a legal ruling established by text be transferred exactly to the branch that is its parallel, and here there is no text. Moreover, matters of linguistic usage are not legal rulings. Answer: The intent of the author of al-Hidayah is not to prove by qiyas that the word 'āriyah is semantically set (mawḍūʻ) for tamlīk al-manfaʻah in the custom of Sharīʻah, such that the objection of qiyas in mawḍūʻāt would apply. Rather, by analogy to physical objects which are capable of both types of tamlīk, he intends to prove that usufructs are also capable of both, and by this proof he merely dispels the opponent's misconception that since usufructs are accidents which do not endure, they cannot be owned. And it is evident that physical objects' acceptance of both types of tamlīk is a legal ruling established by text (the texts indicating sale and gift). Therefore, it is valid to transfer it to usufruct's acceptance of both types as well. Third objection: For qiyas it is also a condition that the legal ruling be transferred to a branch that is its parallel (naẓīr); here, are not usufructs parallel to physical objects? Answer: If by 'not parallel' is meant that they are not completely identical in all respects, this is conceded, but it does not benefit the objector because qiyas does not require the branch to share with the original in all aspects; rather, it suffices that they share in the effective cause (ʻillah) of the ruling, as is known from uṣūl al-fiqh. If by 'not parallel' is meant that they do not share even in the effective cause, this is not conceded, because here tamlīk is the ruling, and its effective cause is the fulfillment of need (dafʻ al-ḥājah), and in this cause physical objects and usufructs are both common.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by the author of al-`Inayah (a super-commentary on al-Hidayah) addressing three objections to the qiyas used by the author of al-Hidayah to prove that usufructs (manafi') are ownable like physical objects (a'yan). The first objection is that definitions are mere concepts (tasawwurat) and cannot be proven by inference (istidlal). The response clarifies that the inference is not about the definition itself but about the subsidiary claim that the definition is correct, comprehensive, etc. The second objection is that qiyas is being applied to linguistic usage (mawdu'at), which is not a legal ruling. The response explains that the qiyas is not proving the linguistic setting of the word but rather the legal capacity of usufructs to be owned, which is a legal ruling. The capacity of physical objects is proven by texts on sale and gift, and this ruling is extended analogically to usufructs. The third objection is that usufructs are not parallel (nazir) to physical objects. The response distinguishes: if 'not parallel' means not identical in every aspect, that is fine because qiyas only requires commonality in the effective cause ('illah). The 'illah here is daf' al-hajah (fulfillment of need), which is present in both. This is a sophisticated discussion of usul al-fiqh principles applied to a specific fiqh issue.

Key Terms
تعریف (taʿrīf): A definition that clarifies the essence of a thing (concept), belonging to tasawwur.
استدلال (istidlāl): Inference based on evidence to establish a proposition (tasdiq).
حکم ضمنی (ḥukm ḍimnī): A subsidiary ruling that accompanies the definition, e.g., that the definition is correct.
موضوعات (mawḍūʿāt): Matters of linguistic usage, i.e., what words are set to mean in language or custom.
دفع حاجت (dafʿ al-ḥājah): Fulfillment of need; the effective cause ('illah) for permitting tamlik of both a'yan and manafi'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the author of al-`Inayah argue about the qiyas for usufructs being ownable like physical objects?
A) The qiyas is invalid because definitions cannot be proven by inference
B) The qiyas is valid because it only requires sharing the 'illah (daf' al-hajah)
C) The qiyas is invalid because usufructs are not property
D) The qiyas is valid but only for ariyah, not ijara

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates the ownership of usufructs by analogy to physical objects based on the shared 'illah of need (daf' al-hajah), after refuting objections that definitions resist inference and that usufructs lack parallelism.

Using Ibahah for Tamlik in 'Aariyah
Explains why ibahah can be used for tamlik in 'Aariyah, answering four objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits using the word ibahah (permission) to effect tamlik (transfer of ownership) in 'Aariyah contracts.

Core Idea
In 'Aariyah, ibahah is a valid metaphor for tamlik because the contract is non-binding and ignorance does not cause dispute.

When someone says 'I permit you to use my pen for a day,' is that a valid loan? The Hanafi school says yes, even though 'ibahah' literally means permission, not transfer of ownership. This lesson explores why ibahah can legally transfer benefits, and how the school answers objections about ignorance, prohibition, and leasing. By understanding this reasoning, you will see how Hanafi fiqh uses legal metaphors and the non-binding nature of 'Aariyah to uphold its validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and its basis
The act is 'Aariyah (loan) expressed with the word ibahah. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) because ibahah is used metaphorically for tamlik, as in ijarah. This is the foundational premise.
Legal metaphors (majaz) are recognized in Hanafi usul.
2
Address the objection of ignorance (jahalah)
Objection: ignorance of duration leads to dispute. Response: 'Aariyah is non-binding (ghayr lazim); the lender can revoke anytime, so duration is not a point of harmful dispute. Ownership transfers only upon possession (qabd), which is utilization, and at that moment there is no ignorance.
Jahalah only nullifies if it likely leads to dispute (mujiba li al-munaza'ah).
3
Address the objection of prohibition (nahy)
Objection: if the lender says 'I do not permit you,' the benefits cannot be acquired. Response: prohibition (nahy) is a revocation of the permission, not a statement that no tamlik occurred. The contract is still valid; the lender simply reclaims the benefit.
Distinguishes between the effect of nahy on the contract and on the transfer.
4
Address the objection of leasing (ijarah)
Objection: the borrower could sublet the item. Response: the borrower cannot lease it because that would bind the lender, increasing harm. The lender's ownership of benefits is revocable; ijarah is binding (lazim), which would prevent the lender from reclaiming.
This is based on the principle of avoiding extra harm (ziyadat al-darar).
5
Synthesize the Hanafi position and authority
The Hanafi position, based on Zahir al-Riwayah, is that 'Aariyah with ibahah is valid. The four objections are answered by metaphorical usage, non-bindingness, possession, and harm prevention.
This ruling is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَفْظَةُ الْإِبَاحَةِ أَسْتَعِيرَتْ لِلتَّمْلِيْكِ كَمَا فِي الْإِجَارَةِ فَإِنَّهَا تَنْعَقِدُ بِلَفْظِةِ الْإِبَاحَةِ وَهِيَ تَمْلِيْكَ وَالْجَهَالَةُ لَا تُفْضِي إِلَى الْمُنَازَعَةِ لِعَدْمِ اللُّزُومِ فَلَا تَكُونُ صَائِرَةً وَ لاَ الْمِلْكَ إِنَّمَا يَثْبُتُ بِالْقَبْضِ وَهُوَ ا لْانْتِفَاعُ وَعِنْدَ ذلِكَ لَا جِهَالَةَ وَالنَّهَى مَنع عَنِ التَّحْصِيلِ فَلَا يَتَحَصَّلَ الْمُنَافِعُ عَلَى مِلْكِهِ وَلَا يَمْلِكُ الْإِجَارَةَ لِدَفْعِ زِيَادَةِ الضَّرَرِ عَلَى مَا نَذْكُرُهُ إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى
translation and commentary: لفظ اباحت سے جواز اعادہ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ لفظ اباحت کو مجاز اتملیک کے معنی میں لیا گیا ہے۔ جیسے اجارہ اباحت کے لفظ سے منعقد ہو جاتا ہے۔ حالانکہ اجارہ میں تملیک منافع کے معنی ہوتے ہیں جس میں کوئی نزاع ہی نہیں ہے۔ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہاں ایسی جہالت نہیں ہے جو جھگڑے تک پہنچائے اس لئے کہ عاریت کوئی لازمی عقد نہیں ہے بلکہ معیر جب چاہے صبح کر سکتا ہے لہذ امدت کا مجہول ہونا کچھ مضر نہیں ہے۔ علاوہ ازیں عاریت میں ملک اسی وقت ثابت ہوتی ہے جب قبضہ ہو جائے اور عاریت ں قبضہ کا مطلب یہی ہے کہ اس سے انتفاع حاصل کرلے اور انتفاع کے وقت کوئی جہالت نہیں ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ منع مغیر کا مؤثر ہونا اس اعتبار سے نہیں ہے کہ عاریت میں تملیک نہیں ہوتی بلکہ اس اعتبار سے ہے کہ معیر نے مال مستعار نفع لینے کی ممانعت کردی۔ تو اب منافع اس کی ملک پر حاصل نہ ہوں گے۔ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مستعیر دوسرے شخص کو اجارہ پر اس لئے نہیں دے سکتا تا کہ اس سے معیر پر زیادہ ضر لاحق نہ ہو اسلئے کہ معیر ۔ منافع کا مالک اس طور پر بنایا ہے کہ جب چاہے گا واپس لے گا اور اجارہ پر دینے کی صورت میں معیر واپس نہیں لے سکتا۔ کیونکہ عقد اجارہ شرعاً لازمی ہوتا ہے۔
The word ibahah is used metaphorically for tamlik, as in ijarah, for it is concluded with the word ibahah while it is tamlik. Ignorance does not lead to dispute due to lack of bindingness, so it is not harmful. And ownership is established only by possession, which is the utilization, and at that time there is no ignorance. Prohibition prevents acquisition, so the benefits are not acquired in his ownership, and he does not own the ijarah to avoid increased harm, as we will mention if Allah wills.
Commentary: The word ibahah is used metaphorically for tamlik, as ijarah is concluded with the word ibahah while it is tamlik, in which there is no dispute. The answer to the objection about ignorance is that there is no ignorance leading to dispute because 'Aariyah is not a binding contract; the lender can take it back anytime, so ignorance of duration is not harmful. Moreover, ownership in 'Aariyah is established only upon possession, which is utilization, and at that time there is no ignorance. The answer about prohibition is that the prohibition's effect is not that there is no tamlik in 'Aariyah, but that the lender prohibited the borrower from taking benefit, so the benefits are not acquired in his ownership. The answer about ijarah is that the borrower cannot give it on ijarah to prevent extra harm to the lender, because the lender is made owner of benefits in a way that he can take them back anytime, but ijarah is a binding contract, so the lender could not reclaim.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with its supporting proofs, explaining that the word ibahah (permission) can be used to effect tamlik (transfer of ownership of benefits) in 'Aariyah, drawing analogy from ijarah. It then addresses four potential objections: (1) ibahah is not tamlik – the response is that it is used metaphorically; (2) ignorance (jahalah) of duration leads to dispute – the response is that 'Aariyah is non-binding (ghayr lazim), so such ignorance does not cause harmful dispute; (3) the lender's prohibition (nahy) prevents acquisition – the response is that prohibition simply revokes permission, not the contract itself; (4) the borrower could lease the item – the response is that the borrower cannot lease it because that would bind the lender, harming him. This shows how Hanafi fiqh uses legal reasoning and istihsan to uphold the validity of 'Aariyah contracts.

Key Terms
اباحت (ibāḥah): Permission, here used metaphorically to mean transfer of ownership of benefits.
تمليك (tamlīk): Transfer of ownership, specifically of benefits in 'Aariyah.
جهالت (jahālah): Ignorance regarding a contractual term (e.g., duration), which is tolerated in non-binding contracts.
لزوم (luzūm): Bindingness, the quality of a contract that prevents unilateral revocation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the contract is a gift, so ignorance is always permitted.
D) Because the Quran allows ignorance in loan contracts.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the word ibahah is a valid metaphor for tamlik in 'Aariyah, and the non-binding nature allows answering objections about ignorance, prohibition, and leasing.

Valid Verbal Formulas for 'Aariyah and the Lender's Right to Reclaim
Lists valid verbal formulas for 'Aariyah and confirms lender's right of revocation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the valid verbal formulas for creating a valid 'Aariyah contract and explain the lender's right to reclaim the loaned item.

Core Idea
A loan ('Aariyah) is valid with several phrases, not just 'a'irtuka; and the lender may revoke at any time because future benefits are not yet owned.

This passage from al-Hidayah lists the acceptable verbal formulas for initiating a loan of usufruct ('Aariyah). It also clarifies that the lender retains the right to take back the item at any time, a ruling supported by both prophetic hadith and rational reasoning. Understanding these formulas is essential for correctly executing a loan contract in daily transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The passage states that 'Aariyah is valid (sahih) when expressed with specific phrases. Note that the contract is valid even if not using the literal word 'a'irtuka.
2
List the valid phrases
Enumerate each phrase: a'irtuka (I loan you), at'amtu (I feed you) for land, manah'tuka (I grant you), hamaltuka (I mount you) for riding animals, akhdamtuka (I make serve), dāri laka suknā (my house for you to dwell in), and dāri laka 'umrā suknā (my house for your lifetime).
The condition for manah'tuka and hamaltuka is that the lender does not intend a gift of the substance.
3
Understand the legal reasoning for each phrase
Some phrases are literal (haqiqah) like a'irtuka; others are metaphorical (majaz) but conventionally used (musta'mal) for loan of benefits, so they are considered explicit (sarih) according to Hanafi usul.
The Urdu commentary clarifies that conventional metaphor is explicit.
4
Analyze the lender's right to revoke
The passage gives two proofs: (1) the hadith 'al-minhatu mardudah wa al-‘ariyatu mu’addah' – the grant is to be returned and the loan is to be given back; (2) rational reasoning: benefits are owned gradually as they occur, so future benefits not yet possessed can be reclaimed.
This means the lender can demand the item back at any time, even before the agreed period.
5
Distinguish between haqiqah and majaz in valid phrases
The author uses 'sarih' for a'irtuka (literal) and 'musta'mal' for at'amtu (metaphorical). Both are valid because the meaning is clear.
This is a key Hanafi principle: explicit includes common metaphorical usage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَتَصِحُ بِقَوْلِهِ آعَرْتُكَ لأَنَّهُ صَرِيحٌ فِيهِ وَأَطْعَمْتُكَ هَذِهِ الْأَرْضَ لِأَنَّهُ مُسْتَعْمَلْ فِيهِ وَمَنَحْتُكَ لِهَذَا الْقَوْبَ وَحَمَلْتُكَ عَلَى هَذِهِ الدَّابَّةِ إِذَا لَمْ يُرِدْ بِهِ الْهِبَةَ لِأَنَّهُمَا لِتَمْلِيكِ الْعَيْنِ وَعِنْدَ عَدْمٍ إِرَادَتِهِ الْهِبَةِ يُحْمَلُ عَلَى تَمْلِيكَ الْمَنَافِعِ تَجَوُّزًا. قَالَ وَاَحْدَمْتُكَ هذَا الْعَبْدَ لِاَنَّهُ إِذْنٌ لَهُ فِي إِسْتِخْدَامِهِ وَدَارِي لَكَ سُكْنَى لِأَنَّ مَعْنَاهُ سُكْنَاهَا لَكَ وَدَارِى لَكَ عُمْراى سُكْنى لِأَنَّهُ جَعَلَ سُكْنَاهَا لَهُ مُدَّةَ عُمُرِهِ وَجَعَلَ قَوْلِهِ سُكْنَى تَفْسِيرًا لِقَوْلِهِ لَكَ لِأَنَّهُ يَحْتَمِلُ تَمْلِيْكَ الْمَنَافِعِ فَجُمَل عَلَيْهِ بِدَلَالَةِ آخِرِهِ. قَالَ وَلِلْمُعِيرِ أَنْ يَرْجِعَ فِي الْعَارِيَةِ مَتَى شَاءَ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ الْمِنْحَةُ مُرْدُودَة وَالْعَارِيَةِ مُؤَدَّاةٌ) وَلاَنَّ الْمُنَافِعَ تَمَلَكَ شَيْئًا فَشَيْئًا عَلَى حَسْبِ حُدُوثِهَا فَالتَّمْلُكُ في الَمْ يُوْجَدْ لَمْ يَتَّصِلْ بِهِ القَبْضُ فَصَ فَصَحَ )
Urdu commentary: تشریح قوله و تصح بقوله اعرتك ..... عاریت مذکورہ ذیل الفاظ سے صحیح ہو جاتی ہے۔ اعر تك کیونکہ یہ لفظ عاریت کیلئے صریح اور حقیقت ہے۔ اطعمتک ارضی کیونکہ یہ الفاظ اسی معنی میں مستعمل ہیں اس لئے کہ جب الفاظ اطعام کی اضافت غیر ماکول العین کی طرف ہو تو اس سے مجاز أحال پر محل کا اطلاق کرتے ہوئے اس کی پیداوار مراد ہوتی ہے۔ سوال .... یہ استعمال مجاز متعارف ہوا اور مجاز متعارف بھی صریح ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ اصول میں مذکور ہے۔ پس دونوں عبارتوں میں کوئی فرق نہ ہوا۔ جواب ... مذکورہ دونوں لفظ صریح ہیں مگر ایک حقیقت ہے اور دوسرا مجاز ہے اس لئے کہ علماء اصول کے یہاں صریح وہ ہے جس کی مراد فی نفسہ واضح ہو۔ پس یہ حقیقت غیر مہجورہ اور مجاز متعارف دونوں کو شامل ہیں۔ پس صاحب ہدایہ نے مستعمل بول کر اشارہ کر دیا کہ پہلا لفظ حقیقت ہے۔ اور دوسرا مجاز ۔ قوله منحتك منحتك ثوبي حملتك على دابتی سے بھی عاریت صحیح ہوگی۔ کیونکہ مختک کے معنیٰ ہیں۔ اعطيتك يـقـال نحر (فض) مخالشئی بمعنی دینا عطاء کرنا۔ اس دودھ والی بکری یا اونٹنی کو کہتے ہیں جو کسی کو دودھ پینے کے لئے دے دی
He said: And it is valid by his saying 'I have given you as a loan' because it is explicit in that, and 'I have fed you this land' because it is used in that meaning, and 'I have granted you this garment' and 'I have mounted you on this riding animal' if he does not intend gift by them, because both are for tamlik of the substance, and when he does not intend gift, it is interpreted metaphorically as tamlik of benefits. He said: And 'I have made this servant serve you' because it is permission for him to use him, and 'my house is for you to dwell in' because its meaning is dwelling in it for you, and 'my house is for you for life to dwell in' because he made dwelling for him for his lifespan, and he made his saying 'suknah' an interpretation of his saying 'laka' because it could bear tamlik of benefits, so it is applied to that by the indication of the latter. He said: And the lender has the right to take back the loan whenever he wishes, due to his saying peace be upon him: 'The grant is to be returned and the loan is to be given back' and because benefits are owned bit by bit as they occur, so what has not yet come into existence has not been possessed by taking possession, so taking back [those future benefits] is valid.
Commentary: Explanation of his saying 'and it is valid by his saying a'irtuka...' The loan is valid by the following phrases: a'irtuka because this word is explicit and real for loan. at'amtu ardi because these words are used in this meaning, because when the word it'am is added to something not edible, it metaphorically means the produce, applying the name of the place to the product. Question: This usage is conventional metaphor, and conventional metaphor is also explicit as mentioned in usul; so there is no difference between the two expressions. Answer: Both words are explicit, but one is real and the other is metaphorical, because according to usul scholars, explicit is that whose meaning is clear in itself. So it includes both the real (non-abandoned) and conventional metaphor. So the author of al-Hidayah used 'musta'mal' to indicate that the first word is real and the second metaphorical. His saying: 'manah'tuka manah'tuka thawbi, hamaltuka 'ala dabati' also makes loan valid, because manah'tu means a'taytuka (I gave). It is said: 'nahara (fadda) makhlishay' meaning giving. The she-goat or she-camel that is given for someone to drink its milk.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of rulings regarding the verbal formulas that create a valid ‘Aariyah contract. It enumerates several key phrases: ‘a‘irtuka (I loan you) is the explicit and literal term; aṭ‘amtuka (I feed you) when used with land means loaning the produce; manaḥtuka (I grant you) and ḥamaltuka (I mount you) when not intended as a gift of the item itself are interpreted as loaning the benefits; akhdamtuka (I made serve) is permission to use the slave; dārī laka suknā (my house is for you to live in) and dārī laka ‘umrā suknā (my house is for your lifetime) establish a loan of dwelling, with the latter specifying lifetime. The passage then confirms the lender’s right to take back the loaned item at any time, citing the hadith ‘al-minḥatu mardūdah wa al-‘āriyatu mu’addāh’ (the grant is to be returned and the loan is to be repaid) and the reasoning that benefits are owned gradually as they occur, so future benefits not yet possessed can be reclaimed. The Urdu commentary clarifies that ‘a‘irtuka is real (ḥaqīqah) while aṭ‘amtuka is metaphorical (majāz), but both are explicit in the context of loans.

Key Terms
صریح (ṣarīḥ): Explicit; a word that clearly indicates its meaning without need for interpretation. Here it applies to both literal (haqiqah) and conventional metaphor (majaz muta'arif).
مستعمل (mustaʿmal): Used; here it specifically denotes a word that is used in a meaning, as opposed to being the literal (haqiqah) word.
منفع (manfaʿah): Benefit; the usufruct of an item, which is the subject of loan in 'Aariyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the evidence for the lender's right to revoke the loan at any time?
A) The Quranic verse on loans.
B) The hadith: 'Al-minhatu mardudah wa al-'ariyatu mu'addah'.
C) Consensus of the scholars.
D) Rational deduction that ownership of benefits is instantaneous.

Key Takeaway
The loan of usufruct is valid with multiple verbal formulas, and the lender retains the right to revoke at any time based on hadith and the gradual ownership of benefits.

The Legal Nature of 'Ariyah: Trust or Guarantee?
Inter-madhhab dispute on liability of borrowed item

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on liability for a borrowed item and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the hadith proofs presented in the text.

Core Idea
'Ariyah is a trust (amanah); the borrower is not liable for loss without transgression.

Imagine borrowing a friend's lawnmower. If it is destroyed in a storm while in your shed without any fault of yours, must you replace it? Your answer depends on which madhhab you follow. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the fundamental nature of 'ariyah: is it a trust (amanah) where the borrower must only compensate if negligent, or is it a guarantee (mamnun) where loss is always compensated? We will examine the textual proofs and the key difference in interpretation.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the matn's claim: 'Ariyah is a trust; if it perishes without transgression, the borrower does not guarantee it. Note that return of the intact item is obligatory (wajib), but liability only arises from ta'addi.
ta'addi means transgression or exceeding the limits of the permission.
2
Identify the opposing school and their position
The Shafi'i school (and Imam Ahmad) hold that the borrower is liable for any loss, even without fault. Their reasoning is that the borrower takes possession for his own benefit, analogous to a buyer who has taken delivery before full payment.
Al-Shafi'i's argument is presented in the commentary: possession of another's property for oneself without right creates liability.
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof (the hadiths)
The Shafi'i school cites three hadiths: 'Return the trust to the one who entrusted you,' 'The hand is responsible for what it has taken until it returns it,' and 'The borrowed item is to be returned.' These appear to impose an absolute duty to return the item or its value.
The exact Arabic of these hadiths is provided in the source.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response argues that these hadiths only oblige the return of the item itself (the 'ayn) if it still exists. They do not address compensation after loss. The dispute is about post-loss compensation, not about returning an intact item.
Hanafis agree that returning the item is obligatory, but liability for loss is a separate matter.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
In a real case where a borrowed item perishes without the borrower's fault: Hanafi rules no compensation; Shafi'i rules the borrower must pay the value. This affects everyday transactions like borrowing tools, books, or vehicles.
Also note intra-madhhab variation: Imam Malik distinguished between animals and valuables.

عاریت امانت ہے یا مضمون؟
قَالَ وَالْعَارِيَةُ أَمَانَةٌ إِنْ هَلَكَتْ مِنْ غَيْرِ تَعَدَّ لَمْ يَضْمَنْ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يَضْمَنُ لِأَنَّهُ قَبَضَ مَالَ غَيْرِهِ لِنَفْسِهِ لَا عَنْ إِسْتِحْقَاقِ فَيَضْمَنُهُ وَالْإِذْهُ ثَبَتَ ضَرُورَةَ الْاِنْتِفَاعِ فَلَا يَظْهَرُ فِيمَا وَرَانَهُ وَلِهَذَا كَانَ وَاجِبَ الرَّةِ وَصَارَ كَالْمَقْبُوضِ عَلَى سَوْمِ الشَّرَاءِ
ترجمہ اور عاریت امانت ہے اگر تلف ہو جائے تعدی کے بغیر تو ضامن نہ ہوگا امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ ضامن ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس نے مال غیر کو بلا استحقاق اپنے قبضہ میں لیا ہے تو ضامن ہوگا اور ضرورت ثابت ہوئی ہے۔ انتفاع کی ضرورت سے تو مقام ضرورت کے ماسوا میں ظاہر نہ ہوگی ۔ اسی لئے اس کا واپس کرنا واجب ہے اور وہ ایسی ہوگئی جیسے خرید میں پکا کر اپنے قبضہ میں لی ہوئی چیز ۔
تشریح قوله والعاريته امانته الخ ہمارے نزدیک عاریت کی چیز امانت ہوتی ہے اب اگر وہ علی حالہ قائم ہو تو اس کو بلا خلاف واپس کرنا ضروری ہے اور اگر وہ ضائع ہوگی ہوتو دیکھا جائے گا کہ مستعیر کی تعدی اور زیادتی سے ضائع ہوئی ہے یا بلا تعدی۔ اگر متعمیر کی تعدی کے بغیر ضائع ہوئی تو اس پر ضمان لازم نہ ہوگا ۔ قاضی ابن شبرمہ قضاء کوفہ کے زمانہ میں متوارتر تمیں سال تک اسی پر عمل پیرا رہے ہیں ۔ امام مالک ، سفیان ثوری، اوزاعی اسی کے قائل ہیں اور یہی حضرت علی ، ابن مسعود، عمر، جابر، حسن، ابراهیم حتی شعمی ، عمر بن عبد العزیز سے مروی ہے ۔ امام مالک سے یہ بھی منقول ہے کہ عاریت اگر جانور ہو تو ضامن نہ ہوگا اور اس زیورات اور کپڑے وغیرہ ہوں تو ضامن ہو گا۔
قوله و قال الشافعی امام شافعی اور امام احمد کے نزدیک اگر عاریت تلف ہو جائے تو مستغیر ضامن ہوگا۔ یہی عطاء اور اسحاق کا قول ہے۔ اور یہ حضرت ابن عباس و حضرت ابو ہریرہ سے بھی مروی ہے ( امام شافعی کا ایک قول یہ بھی منقول ہے کہ اگر وہ استعمال معتاد سے ہلاک ہوئی تو ضامن نہ ہوگا ورنہ ضامن ہوگا۔ مگر یہ قول ان کے یہاں ضعیف ہے) ربیعہ کے نزدیک تمام عاریتیں مضمون ہیں روضہ میں ہے کہ عاریت کی چیز مستغیر کے قبضہ میں تلف ہو گئی تو وہ ضامن ہوگا۔ خواہ اس کا تلف ہونا آفت سادیہ سے ہو یا مستغیر کے فعل سے ہو۔ نیز اس کی کوتاہی سے ہو یا بلا ء کو تا ہی حاوی حنابلہ میں ہے ان شرط نفی ضما نها سقط الضمان عثمان ہی کا قول کہ مستیعر حیوان اور عقل کے علاوہ کا ضامن ہے اوراگران میں ضمان کی شرط کر لی گئی تو ان کا بھی ضامن ہو گا۔ اختلاف کی اصل بنیاد یہ ہے کہ عاریت ہمارے نزدیک علی الاطلاق امانت ہے نہ کہ بوقت استعمال جیسا کہ امام شافعی و امام احمد قرماتے ہیں۔ ان کے روایتی ادلہ حسب ذیل ہیں۔
ا۔ حدیث ابوہریرہ اس کی تخریج امام ترندی نے کی ہے۔
قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ادالامانته الى من اتمنك ولاتخن من خانك
حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا۔ کہ جس نے تیرے پاس کوئی امانت رکھی تو اس کی امانت ادا کر اور جس نے تیری خیانت کی ہو تو اس کی خیانت مت کر۔ ۲۔ حدیث سمرہ اس کی تخریج امام نسائی کے علاوہ اصحاب خمسہ نے کی ہے
"عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: على اليد ما اخدت حتى تودى "
حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا کہ ہاتھ پر واجب رہے گی جو اس نے لے لی ہے جب تک کہ ادانہ کر دے۔
۳۔ حدیث ابوامامہ اس کی تخریج امام ابوداؤ تر نمدی اور ابن حبان نے کی ہے اور طبرانی نے اس کو مسند شامیین میں حضرت انس سے اور حافظ بزار نے حضرت عمر سے روایت کیا ہے۔
انه سمع النبي يقول في حجته الوداع : العاريته مؤداة
حضرت ابوامامہ فرماتے ہیں کہ میں نے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کو الوداعی حج کے خطبہ میں یہ فرماتے سنا کہ غاریت لی ہوئی چیز ادا ہو کر رہے گی۔
جواب یہ ہے کہ ان احادیث میں عاریت کے مضمون ہونے پر کوئی دلالت نہیں ہے ان کا مقتضی تو صرف وجوب رد عین ہے جس میں کوئی کلام نہیں۔ ہم بھی کہتے ہیں کہ عاریت اگر بعینہ موجود ہو تو اس کو واپس کرنا ضروری ہے۔ گفتگو تو ہلاک عین کے بعد منمان قیمت کے وجوب میں ہے۔
Is 'ariyah a trust or guarantee? He said: 'Ariyah is a trust; if it perishes without transgression, he does not guarantee it. Al-Shafi'i said: He guarantees it, because he took possession of another's property for himself without right, so he guarantees it. The permission is established by necessity of use, so it does not appear beyond that. For this reason, its return is obligatory, and it becomes like what is taken on the basis of purchase.
Translation: And 'ariyah is a trust; if it perishes without transgression, he does not guarantee it. Imam al-Shafi'i says he does guarantee it, because he took possession of another's property without right, so he guarantees it. The necessity is established by the need for use, so it does not appear beyond the scope of necessity. Therefore, its return is obligatory, and it becomes like an item taken in hand on the condition of purchase.
Commentary on his saying 'and 'ariyah is a trust' etc.: According to us, the borrowed item is a trust. Now if it remains intact, it must be returned without disagreement. If it is lost, it is considered: did it perish due to the borrower's transgression and excess or without transgression? If it perished without the borrower's transgression, he is not liable for compensation. Qadi Ibn Shubrumah, during his tenure as judge of Kufa, continued to act upon this for many years. Imam Malik, Sufyan al-Thawri, and al-Awza'i also hold this view, and it is reported from 'Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, 'Umar, Jabir, Hasan, Ibrahim, Hisham? [Hisham?], 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz. Another narration from Imam Malik: If the borrowed item is an animal, he does not guarantee it; if it is jewelry or clothing, he guarantees it.
His saying: 'and al-Shafi'i said' — According to Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad, if the borrowed item perishes, the borrower guarantees it. This is also the saying of 'Ata' and Ishaq. It is also reported from Ibn 'Abbas and Abu Hurayrah. (Another narration from al-Shafi'i: if it perishes by normal use, he does not guarantee; otherwise he guarantees. But this saying is weak according to them.) According to Rabi'ah, all borrowed items are guaranteed. In Rawdah, it is said: if the borrowed item perishes in the borrower's possession, he guarantees it, whether by a natural calamity or by the borrower's act, whether due to his negligence or not. In Hanabilah (the Hanbali school), if they stipulate the negation of liability, liability falls. Another saying: The borrower is liable for animals and rational beings? And if they stipulate liability for them, he is also liable. The basis of the disagreement is that according to us, 'ariyah is absolutely a trust, not during use as Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad say. Their transmitted proofs are as follows:
1. Hadith of Abu Hurayrah, narrated by al-Tirmidhi: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Return the trust to the one who entrusted you, and do not betray the one who betrayed you.'
2. Hadith of Samurah, narrated by the five except al-Nasa'i: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The hand is responsible for what it has taken until it returns it.'
3. Hadith of Abu Umamah, narrated by Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Hibban, and al-Tabarani in Musnad al-Shamiyyin from Anas, and al-Bazzar from 'Umar: He heard the Prophet say in the Farewell Pilgrimage: 'The borrowed item is to be returned.'
The response is that these hadiths do not indicate that the borrowed item is guaranteed. They only necessitate the obligation to return the item itself, about which there is no disagreement. We also say that if the item is still in existence, its return is obligatory. The dispute is about the obligation to pay compensation after the item perishes.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the legal nature of 'ariyah (loan for use). The Hanafi school, represented by the text, holds that 'ariyah is a trust (amanah), meaning the borrower is not liable for loss or damage unless it occurs due to his transgression (ta'addi) or negligence. The Shafi'i school, and also Imam Ahmad, hold that the borrowed item is guaranteed (mamnun), so the borrower is liable for any loss even without his fault. The passage first presents the Hanafi position from the matn, then the Shafi'i argument: the borrower takes possession of another's property for his own benefit without any right, so he should be liable; the permission is only to the extent of necessity, so beyond that the item is like something taken for purchase. The commentary elaborates that according to Hanafis, if the item remains intact, it must be returned; if lost, liability only arises from transgression. It supports this with the practice of Qadi Ibn Shubrumah and reports from many Companions and early jurists. It notes that Imam Malik has a different opinion distinguishing animals from valuables. Then it presents the Shafi'i and Ahmad's position, along with some variant narrations from Shafi'i and the views of Rabi'ah and the Hanbalis. The core of the dispute is whether 'ariyah is a trust absolutely (as Hanafis hold) or only during use (as Shafi'is claim). The passage then provides three hadith proofs from the Shafi'i side: the hadith of returning trusts under all circumstances?; the hadith 'the hand is responsible'; and the hadith 'the borrowed item is to be returned'. The Hanafi response is that these hadiths only oblige returning the item itself if it still exists; they do not impose liability for compensation if the item is lost without negligence. The dispute is solely about compensation after loss, not about returning the existing item.

Key Terms
عاریة ('ariyah): A contract granting temporary use of an item without compensation.
أمانة (amanah): A property held in trust, where the holder is not liable for loss without negligence.
مضمون (mamnun): A property for which the holder is liable for compensation if lost or damaged.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage.
تعدی (ta'addi): Transgression or exceeding limits; acting in a way not authorized.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a borrowed item is lost without any transgression (ta'addi) by the borrower, the borrower:
A) Must compensate the owner.
B) Does not have to compensate.
C) Must return the item if found later.
D) Is considered a usurper (ghasib).

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, 'ariyah is a trust (amanah); the borrower is not liable for loss or damage unless it occurs due to transgression (ta'addi).

Ariyah: Trust or Guarantee? Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Presents and defends Hanafi position that borrowed item is a trust.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that a borrowed item is a trust (amanah) and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on textual and rational proofs.

Core Idea
A borrowed item is a trust, not a guarantee—permission negates liability unless stipulated.

When you borrow an item and it is accidentally lost, who bears the loss? The Hanafi school distinguishes based on the nature of possession: if taken with permission, it is a trust; if without, it is guaranteed. This lesson dives into the classical dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on this precise question, analyzing the proofs from both sides.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling that a borrowed item (ariyah) is a trust (amanah); the borrower is not liable for loss without transgression.
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i (and Ahmad) hold the borrower liable for any loss of the borrowed item.
Also note that Imam Malik has a qualified view.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i proofs: three hadiths (on returning trusts and borrowed items) and a rational argument that possession of another's property without right creates liability.
The hadiths are quoted in the text.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand how the Hanafi school rebuts each proof: the hadiths only require return of the item if it exists, not compensation after loss; the rational argument fails because the possession is with permission, and permission negates the transgression that would trigger liability.
Also note the distinction from the item taken on purchase discussion (maqbud 'ala sawm al-shira'), which is guaranteed by contract.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Note the practical difference: in the Hanafi school, if a borrowed item is lost accidentally, the borrower pays nothing; in the Shafi'i school, he must pay the value.
This affects real-world lending transactions.
