قوله و قال الشافعی امام شافعی اور امام احمد کے نزدیک اگر عاریت تلف ہو جائے تو مستغیر ضامن ہوگا۔ یہی عطاء اور اسحاق کا قول ہے۔ اور یہ حضرت ابن عباس و حضرت ابو ہریرہ سے بھی مروی ہے ( امام شافعی کا ایک قول یہ بھی منقول ہے کہ اگر وہ استعمال معتاد سے ہلاک ہوئی تو ضامن نہ ہوگا ورنہ ضامن ہوگا۔ مگر یہ قول ان کے یہاں ضعیف ہے) ربیعہ کے نزدیک تمام عاریتیں مضمون ہیں روضہ میں ہے کہ عاریت کی چیز مستغیر کے قبضہ میں تلف ہو گئی تو وہ ضامن ہوگا۔ خواہ اس کا تلف ہونا آفت سادیہ سے ہو یا مستغیر کے فعل سے ہو۔ نیز اس کی کوتاہی سے ہو یا بلا ء کو تا ہی حاوی حنابلہ میں ہے ان شرط نفي ضما نها سقط الضمان عثمان ہی کا قول کہ مستیعر حیوان اور عقل کے علاوہ کا ضامن ہے اوراگران میں ضمان کی شرط کر لی گئی تو ان کا بھی ضامن ہو گا۔ اختلاف کی اصل بنیاد یہ ہے کہ عاریت ہمارے نزدیک علی الاطلاق امانت ہے نہ کہ بوقت استعمال جیسا کہ امام شافعی و امام احمد قرماتے ہیں۔ ان کے روایتی ادلہ حسب ذیل ہیں۔
ا۔ حدیث ابوہریرہ اس کی تخریج امام ترندی نے کی ہے۔
قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ادالامانته الى من اتمنك ولاتخن من خانك
حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا۔ کہ جس نے تیرے پاس کوئی امانت رکھی تو اس کی امانت ادا کر اور جس نے تیری خیانت کی ہو تو اس کی خیانت مت کر۔ ۲۔ حدیث سمرہ اس کی تخریج امام نسائی کے علاوہ اصحاب خمسہ نے کی ہے
"عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: على اليد ما اخدت حتى تودى "
حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا کہ ہاتھ پر واجب رہے گی جو اس نے لے لی ہے جب تک کہ ادانہ کر دے۔
۳۔ حدیث ابوامامہ اس کی تخریج امام ابوداؤ تر نمدی اور ابن حبان نے کی ہے اور طبرانی نے اس کو مسند شامیین میں حضرت انس سے اور حافظ
بزار نے حضرت عمر سے روایت کیا ہے۔
انه سمع النبي يقول في حجته الوداع : العاريته مؤداة
حضرت ابوامامہ فرماتے ہیں کہ میں نے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کو الوداعی حج کے خطبہ میں یہ فرماتے سنا کہ غاریت لی ہوئی چیز ادا ہو کر رہے گی۔
جواب یہ ہے کہ ان احادیث میں عاریت کے مضمون ہونے پر کوئی دلالت نہیں ہے ان کا مقتضی تو صرف وجوب رد عین ہے جس میں کوئی کلام نہیں۔ ہم بھی کہتے ہیں کہ عاریت اگر بعینہ موجود ہو تو اس کو واپس کرنا ضروری ہے۔ گفتگو تو ہلاک عین کے بعد منمان قیمت کے وجوب میں ہے۔

اشرف البدایہ جلد - یازدهم
كتاب العارية
قوله ولانه قبض مال غيره .... الخ یه امام شافعی کی معقلی دلیل ہے کہ مستعیر نے غیر کے مال واپنے قbesturdubo
والادء غير الضمان في اللغة ولا لحكم
کے لئے لیا ہے لہذا ضامن ہوگا۔ ممکن ہے اس پر کوئی یہ کہے کہ اس نے جو عاریت پر قبضہ کیا ہے وہ مالک کی اجازت سے کیا ہے اور جو قبضہ باجازت ہو وہ موجب ضمان نہیں ہوتا والا ذن ثبت ضرورة الانتفاع “ سے اس کا جواب ہے کہ مالک کی طرف سے اجازت صرف اس ضرورت کے پیش نظر ہے کہ مستعیر اس سے فائدہ ٹھائے۔ اور جو چیز ثابت بالضرورۃ ہوٹل ضرورت تک ہی رہتی ہے اور ضرورت صرف استعمال کی حالت میں ہے تو اس کے علاوہ میں اجازت کا اثر ظاہر نہ ہوگا۔ اور اسی وجہ سے ( کہ اس نے مال غیر پر اپنے لئے بلا استحقاق قبضہ کیا ہے ) عاریت کو واپس کرنا واجب ہوا۔ اور عاریت ایسی چیز کی ماند ہوگئی جوخرید میں چکا کر بالغ کی اجازت سے اپنے قبضہ میں لی ہو وہ اگر چہ مقبوض باجازت مالک ہے لیکن اگر ہلاک ہو جائے تو ملک غیر پر بلا استحقاق قبضہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ضامن ہوتا ہے ایسے ہی یہاں بھی ضامن ہو گا۔
قوله ولهذا كان .... الخ صاحب عنایہ اور صاحب بنایہ نے ھذا کا مشار الیہ الاذن ضرور یا قرار دیا ہے۔ صاحب نتائج کہتے ہیں کہ میرے نزدیک حق یہ ہے کہ یہ لانہ قبض مال غيره لنفسه لا عن استحقاق " کی طرف اشارہ ہے اور اس کے حق ہونے کی دوہ نہیں ہیں ۔ ایک یہ کہ وصار کا لمقبوض على سوم الشراء" کا عطف "كان واجب الردّ پر ہے اور معطوف معطوف علیہ کے حکم میں ہوتا ہے(ای بالنظر الی ما قبله ) اب اگر ہذا کا مشار الیہ کون الاذن ضرور یا قرار دیا جائے تو معنی یہ ہوں گے۔ ولكون الاذن ضرورياً صار كا لمقبوض على سوم الشراء حالانکہ ظاہر یہی ہے کہ مقبوص علی سوم الشراء میں اذان بوجہ ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ والاذان ثبت ضرورة الانتفاع “كلام ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب ہونے کی بنا پر استدلال کا عمدہ جز نہیں ہے۔ بخلاف لانه قبض مال غیرہ اٹھ کے کہ یہ استدلال کا ٹھوس اور عمدہ جزء ہے يس ولهذا كان واجب الردّ اور وصار كا لمقبوض على سوم اشراء کو استدلال کے عمدہ جزء پر متفرع کرنا احق ہو گا اس کی تائید صاحب کافی کے اس صنیع سے بھی ہوتی ہے کہ موصوف نے کون الاذن ضروریاً والی بات کو مذکورہ دونوں تعریفوں سے مؤخر کیا ہے۔

احناف کی دلیل
وَلَنَا أَنَّ اللَّفْظَ لَا يُنْبِئُءُ عَنْ الْتَزَامِ الصَّمَانِ لِاَنَّهُ لِتَمْلِيكِ الْمَنَافِعِ بِغَيْرِ عِوَضٍ أَوْ لِإِبَاحَتِهَا وَالْقَبْضُ لَمْ يَقَعُ تَعَـدِيَّا لِكُوْنِهِ مَادُونَا فِيْهِ وَالْإِذْهُ وَإِنْ ثَبَتَ لِاَجَلِ الْاِنْتِفَاعِ فَهُوَ مَا قَبَضَهُ إِلَّا لِلْانْتِفَاعِ فَلَمْ يَقَعَ تَعَدِيًا وَإِنَّمَا وَجَبَ الرَّدُّ مُؤنَةً كَنَفَقَةِ الْمُسْتَعَارِ فَإِنَّهَا عَلَى الْمُسْتَعِيرِ لَا لِنَقْضِ الْقَبْضِ وَالْمَقْبُوضِ عَلَى سَوْمِ الشَّرَاءِ مَضْمُونَ بالْعَقْدِ لأَنَّ الْأَخْذَ فِي الْعَقْدِ لَهُ حُكْمُ الْعَقْدِ عَلَى مَا عُرِفَ فِي مَوْضِعِهِ

ترجمہ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ لفظ عاربیت خود پر ضمان لازم کرنے کو نہیں بتا تا۔ کیونکہ عاریت بلا عوض منافع کا مالک کرنے یا ان کی اباحت کے لئے ہے اور قبضہ کرنا تعدی واقع نہیں ہوا۔ کیونکہ قبضہ کرنے میں وہ اجازت دیا گیا ہے اور اجازت اگر چہ نفع اٹھانے کے لئے ثابت ہوئی ہے مگر اس نے قبضہ نفع اٹھانے کے لئے ہی کیا ہے تو وہ تعدی واقع نہ ہوا ۔ اور لوٹانے کا واجب ہونا خرچہ کی وجہ سے ہے جیسے مستعار کا نفقہ کہ وہ مستعیر پر واجب ہوتا ہے۔ قبضہ توڑنے کے لئے نہیں ہے اور خرید کے طور پر لی ہوئی چیز عقد کی وجہ سے مضمون ہوتی ہے اس لئے کہ عقد میں لینے کے لئے عقد ہی کا حکم ہے۔ جیسا کہ اپنی جگہ پر معلوم ہے۔
تشریح قوله لنا ان اللفظ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مستغیر کی جانب سے وجوب ضمان کا کوئی سبب نہیں پایا گیا۔ اس لئے کہ آدمی پر ضمان اس کے فعل کے بغیر واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ اور مستغیر کی جانب سے ظاہر جو فعل پایا گیا ہے۔ وہ عقد عاریت اور قبضہ ہے جن میں سے کوئی ایک بھی منمان
Book of Al-Ariyah: Like the item taken on the basis of a purchase discussion. Translation: And ariyah is a trust; if it perishes without transgression, the borrower is not liable. Imam Shafi'i says he will be liable because he has taken possession of another's property without right, so he is liable, and necessity is established; the necessity of benefit, so it will not be apparent beyond the scope of necessity. Therefore, returning it is obligatory, and it becomes like an item taken with a firm intention to purchase. Commentary: The author's statement 'and his ariyah is a trust, etc.' According to us, a borrowed item is a trust. If it remains intact, it must be returned without dispute; if it perishes, it is examined whether the borrower's transgression or excess caused it or not. If it perished without his transgression, no guarantee is required. Qadi Ibn Shubrumah during his time as judge of Kufa acted upon this for forty years. Imam Malik, Sufyan al-Thawri, al-Awza'i held this view, and it is narrated from Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, Umar, Jabir, Hasan, Ibrahim, […], and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz. From Imam Malik, it is also transmitted that if the borrowed item is an animal, he is not liable, but if it is jewelry and clothes, he will be liable. The author's statement: 'And al-Shafi'i said' – According to Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad, if the borrowed item perishes, the borrower is liable. This is also the view of Ata' and Ishaq, and it is narrated from Ibn Abbas and Abu Hurayra. (Another narration from al-Shafi'i states that if it perishes through customary use, he is not liable; otherwise he is liable, but this narration is weak in his school). According to Rabi'ah, all borrowings are guaranteed. In Rawdah: if the borrowed item perishes in the borrower's possession, he is liable, whether through a natural disaster or his own act, whether due to his negligence or not. In Hanabila: if a condition of non-liability is stipulated, liability drops; al-Uthmani's view: the borrower is liable for animals and other than cash, and if guarantee is stipulated for these, he will also be liable. The basis of disagreement is that, according to us, ariyah is absolutely a trust, not only at the time of use, as Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad say. Their transmitted proofs are as follows: 1. Hadith of Abu Hurayra (recorded by al-Tirmidhi): The Prophet ﷺ said, 'Return the trust to the one who entrusted you, and do not betray the one who betrayed you.' 2. Hadith of Samurah (recorded by the five except al-Nasa'i): The Prophet ﷺ said, 'The hand must return what it took until it returns it.' 3. Hadith of Abu Umamah (recorded by Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and Ibn Hibban; al-Tabarani narrated it from Anas; al-Bazzar from Umar): He heard the Prophet ﷺ in his Farewell Pilgrimage say, 'The borrowed item must be returned.' The response is that these hadiths do not indicate that the borrowed item is guaranteed; they only necessitate the return of the item itself, which is undisputed – we also say that if the item still exists, it must be returned. The discussion is about the obligation of compensation after the item has perished. The author's statement: 'And because he took possession of another's property...' – this is Imam Shafi'i's rational argument: the borrower took another's property for himself, so he is liable. Someone might say that he took possession with the owner's permission, and a possession with permission does not cause liability. But the response is that the owner's permission is only for the necessity of benefiting, and whatever is established by necessity remains only to the extent of necessity. Necessity is only during use, so beyond that, the permission's effect does not appear. Therefore, returning it is obligatory, and it becomes like an item taken with a firm intention to purchase by a baligh (mature person) – even though it is taken with the owner's permission, if it perishes, the taker is liable because he took possession without right. Similarly here, the borrower will be liable. The author's statement: 'And therefore it was...' – The author of Inayah and Binayah consider the reference of 'this' to be 'the permission is necessitated'. The author of Nata'ij says that, in my view, the correct thing is that it refers to 'because he took possession of another's property for himself without right', and there are two reasons for its correctness: first, the conjunction 'and it became like the item taken on purchase discussion' is connected to 'returning it was obligatory', and the conjoined follows the rule of the conjoined; if the reference is to 'the permission is necessitated', the meaning would be 'and because the permission is necessitated, it became like the item taken on purchase discussion', but it is evident that the item taken on purchase discussion does not have permission due to necessity. Second, the statement 'the permission is established due to necessity of benefit' is not a solid part of the argument, being a response to an implicit question, unlike 'because he took possession of another's property...' which is a strong part, and it is more appropriate that 'therefore returning it was obligatory' and 'and it became like the item taken on purchase discussion' branch from that strong part. This is supported by the author of Kafi's arrangement, who deferred the matter of 'the permission is necessitated' after the two mentioned definitions. 

Proof of the Hanafis: 'And we argue that the word does not indicate the assumption of guarantee, because it [ariyah] is for granting ownership of benefits without compensation or for permitting them; and the possession did not occur as transgression because it is with permission; and although permission is established for the sake of benefit, he only took possession for benefit, so it was not transgression; and the obligation to return is due to expense, like the expense of the borrowed item, which is upon the borrower, not to break the possession; and the item taken on purchase discussion is guaranteed by contract because the taking in the contract has the ruling of the contract, as known in its place.' Translation of the above: Our proof is that the term ariyah does not indicate the imposition of guarantee, because it is for granting ownership of benefits without compensation or for permitting them; and the possession did not occur as transgression because he is permitted to do so; and though permission is established for benefiting, he only took possession for benefit, so it was not transgression; and the obligation to return is due to expense, like the expense of the borrowed item, which is on the borrower – not to break the possession; and the item taken on the basis of purchase discussion is guaranteed by contract, because the taking in a contract has the ruling of the contract, as is known in its place. Commentary on 'our proof is that the word': Our reasoning is that no cause for liability is found on the part of the borrower, because liability is not obligatory without an act, and the apparent acts on the borrower's part are the contract of ariyah and possession, none of which are [liability-inducing].
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute on the ruling of a borrowed item (ariyah). The passage begins by stating the Hanafi position: a borrowed item is a trust (amanah). If it perishes without the borrower's transgression (ta'addi), the borrower is not liable (daman). The author immediately contrasts with Imam al-Shafi'i's view that the borrower is liable. The Hanafi ruling is supported by many early authorities, including Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, Umar, and others. Imam Malik has a qualified view: if the borrowed item is an animal, no liability; if it is jewelry or clothing, liability applies. Then the Shafi'i position is explained: the borrower is liable because he took possession of another's property without a right. The Shafi'i argument is that the owner's permission is only for the necessity of use; beyond that, the possession is without right, so liability attaches, analogous to a purchase discussion where a person takes an item to consider buying it. The Hanafi response is that the Shafi'i hadith proofs (three hadiths about returning trusts and borrowed items) only require return of the item itself, not compensation after loss. The Hanafi's own proof is given in Arabic: the word 'ariyah' does not imply guarantee; it is a contract for free benefit; the borrower's possession is with permission, so no transgression; the obligation to return is a separate duty, not a sign of liability; the item taken on purchase discussion is guaranteed because the contract itself (the discussion) creates liability, unlike ariyah. Finally, the commentary discusses a grammatical point about the phrase 'kal-maqbud 'ala sawm al-shira'', clarifying that the reference is to the fact that the borrower's possession is with permission, but that permission is limited to the time of use, not to loss. The overall lesson: the Hanafi school upholds ariyah as a trust; this is the mufta bihi position. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah, as this is a standard Hidayah ruling.

Key Terms
عاریت (āriyah): A contract whereby a person gives another permission to use a specific item without compensation, retaining ownership; the borrowed item is a trust.
امانت (amānah): Something held in trust; the holder is not liable for loss except in case of transgression or negligence.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability to compensate for loss or damage, typically by paying the value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of a borrowed item (ariyah) that perishes without any transgression (ta'addi) by the borrower?
A) The borrower must pay the value of the item because he took possession of another's property.
B) The borrower is not liable because the item is a trust (amanah) and he had permission to use it.
C) The borrower is liable only if the item is an animal, but not for other items.
D) The borrower must return a similar item or its price, because the hadith says 'the borrowed item must be returned'.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a borrowed item is a trust (amanah); the borrower is not liable for accidental loss without transgression.

intermediate
6 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Guarantee Condition in Loan (Ariyah)
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on effect of daman condition in ariyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the famous Hanafi position on a loan with a guarantee condition and explain the response to the counter-evidence using the non-Muslim status of Safwan.

Core Idea
A condition of guarantee in a loan is void among Muslims; the hadith of Safwan applies only because he was non-Muslim.

This lesson examines a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding whether a borrower becomes liable for loss if they agree to a condition of guarantee when taking a loan. One narration, supported by Sahib al-Jawharah, considers the condition valid and makes the borrowed item guaranteed. However, the famous (mashhur) narration treats the condition as void, keeping the loan as a trust. The apparent conflict with the hadith of Safwan is resolved by noting that Safwan was not a Muslim at the time, and special rules apply between Muslims and non-Muslims.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi default position
Without any condition, a borrowed item is a trust (amanah). The borrower is only liable for loss due to negligence or transgression, not for accidental loss. This is the baseline ruling.
2
Identify the disputed condition
The dispute arises when the lender includes a condition that the borrower must guarantee the item (i.e., be liable for any loss, even without negligence). Some Hanafis argue this condition makes the item guaranteed (madhmun).
The condition is contrary to the nature of ariyah as a gratuitous contract.
3
Present the two opinions
1) Famous (mashhur) narration: The condition is void (laghw), and the loan remains a trust. 2) Narration from Sahib al-Jawharah (and a minority): The condition is valid and the item becomes guaranteed.
The text states the famous narration is the relied-upon position.
4
Analyse the evidence for the minority view
The minority cites the hadith of Safwan ibn Umayyah, who lent his armor to the Prophet (PBUH) with a condition of return. They interpret this as a valid guarantee condition in a loan.
The hadith is proven, but its application is contested.
5
Examine the Hanafi response to the hadith
The famous narration responds that Safwan was a non-Muslim (harbi) at the time. Conditions between a Muslim and a non-Muslim combatant are permissible even if they would be void between two Muslims. Thus, the hadith does not establish a rule for Muslim borrowers.
This is the key tarjih (preference) mechanism.

ای آن هممت بهاوار تھا تیرے یہ کہ بقول حافظ قتادہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت صفوان [؟] سے جوزرہم یہ [؟] بشرط ضمان تھیں جیسا کہ مسند احمد کی روایت صفوان اور مسردک حاکم کی روایت جابر بن عبد اللہ نے کے الفاظ حتى نؤ ديها اليك "اس پر دال ہیں اور مستعغیر اگر عاریت بشرط ضمان لے تو احناف کے یہاں بھی ایک روایت کے مطابق مضمون ہوتی ہے۔ چنانچہ صاحب جو ہرہ نے اس پر جزم کیا ہے۔ حيث قال ان شرط فيها الضمان كانت مضمونته بالشرط الھ البتہ مذہب میں مشہور روایت یہی ہے کہ عاریت بشرط ضماں کی صورت میں شرط لغو ہوگی اور ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اس روایت کے پیش نظر جواب یہ ہوگا۔ حضرت صفوان اس وقت تک مسلمان نہیں تھے بعد میں با سلام ہو گئے تھے۔ جیسا کہ روایت مسند احمد کے الفاظ انا اليوم يارسول الله في الاسلام راغب اور روایت ابوداؤد کے الفاظ لأنَّ فی قلبي اليوم مالم یکن یو مند ہیں اس کی صراحت موجود ہے اور مسلم و حربی کے درمیان وہ شرائط جائز ہیں۔ جو بین المسلمین جائز نہیں۔
It is said that according to Hafiz Qatadah, the Prophet (peace be upon him) borrowed the armor of Safwan with a condition of guarantee, as narrated by Ahmad from Safwan and by Hakim from Jabir ibn Abdullah with the words 'until we return it to you.' This indicates. And if the borrower takes the loan with a condition of guarantee, then according to a narration among the Hanafis, it becomes guaranteed. Thus, Sahib al-Jawharah asserted this, saying: 'If he stipulated guarantee in it, it becomes guaranteed by the condition.' However, the famous narration in the school is that in the case of a loan with a condition of guarantee, the condition is void and guarantee is not obligatory. According to this narration, the answer is: Safwan was not a Muslim at that time; he later became Muslim, as indicated by the words in Musnad Ahmad: 'Today, O Messenger of Allah, I am desirous of Islam' and in Abu Dawud: 'Because in my heart there is today that which was not yesterday.' And conditions between a Muslim and a combatant are permissible which are not permissible between Muslims.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on a borrowed item when the borrower agrees to a condition of guarantee. The issue arises from the hadith of Safwan ibn Umayyah, who lent the Prophet (peace be upon him) armor with a condition of guarantee. Some Hanafi scholars, such as Sahib al-Jawharah, hold that the condition is valid and the borrowed item becomes guaranteed (i.e., the borrower is liable for loss). However, the famous (mashhur) narration in the Hanafi school states that the condition is void and the loan remains a trust (amanah), meaning no guarantee arises from the condition alone. The response to the apparent contradiction with the hadith is that Safwan was not a Muslim at the time of the loan; conditions between a Muslim and a non-Muslim (harbi) are valid even if they are invalid between two Muslims. Thus, the hadith is not a precedent for loans among Muslims. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the condition of guarantee in a loan is void, and the borrower is not liable for loss unless there is negligence.

Key Terms
عارية (ariyah): A loan of a benefit for free, temporary use.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or destruction of the borrowed item.
شرط لغو (shart laghw): A void condition that has no legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the famous (mashhur) Hanafi narration, what is the ruling if a borrower agrees to a condition of guarantee in a loan?
A) The borrowed item becomes guaranteed (madhmun) and the borrower is liable.
B) The condition is void and the borrower is not liable unless negligent.
C) The loan contract becomes invalid.
D) The condition is valid only if the lender is non-Muslim.

Key Takeaway
A condition of guarantee in a loan (ariyah) is void among Muslims; the borrowed item remains a trust, and liability only arises from negligence, not from a stipulation.

Borrower Lending the Borrowed Item: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute on whether musta'ir may lend the borrowed item

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that the borrower may lend the borrowed item if the use does not vary with the user, and contrast it with the Shafi'i prohibition, citing the respective proofs.

Core Idea
ʿĀriyah is tamlīk (ownership transfer) of benefits, not just ibāḥah (permission), so the borrower can transfer those benefits.

This lesson examines a classical dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over whether a borrower (musta'ir) may lend the borrowed item to a third party. The answer hinges on the legal nature of 'ariyah: is it a mere permission to benefit (ibāḥah al-manāfiʿ) or a transfer of ownership of benefits (tamlīk al-manāfiʿ)? The Hanafi school adopts the latter view, permitting sub-lending under a key condition. We will unpack the arguments on both sides and understand the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from the matn: the borrower may lend the item if it does not vary with different users. Note the condition.
This is the muftā bihī position.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imām al-Shāfiʿī holds that sub-lending is impermissible. Understand his reasoning: 'ariyah is ibāḥah, so the permit-holder cannot permit another.
Imām Aḥmad in one narration also holds this view.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Trace the Shāfiʿī argument: benefits are non-existent and cannot be owned; they are treated as existent in ijārah only by necessity; here necessity is already met by the original permission.
The key point: benefits are 'ma'dūmah' (non-existent) so not susceptible to ownership.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafīs counter that 'ariyah is tamlīk, as established. The borrower owns the benefits and can transfer them, analogous to a bequest of service. Benefits are considered ownable in ijārah and similarly in 'ariyah to fulfill a need. The condition prevents additional harm to the lender.
This is a qiyās (analogy) to ijārah and to wasiyyah bil-khidmah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: If the borrower lends the item and it is damaged, under Hanafi the borrower remains liable as guarantor; under Shāfiʿī the sub-lending is invalid and the borrower is a usurper (ghāṣib).
This affects liability and recourse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَهُ أَنْ يُعِيْرَهُ إِذَا كَانَ لَا يَخْتَلِفُ بِاِخْتِلَافِ الْمُسْتَعْمَلِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ لَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يُعِيْرَهُ لِأَنَّهُ إِبَاحَةُ الْمَنَافِعِ عَلَى مَا بَيَّنَّاهُ مِنْ قَبْلُ وَالْمُبَاحُ لَهُ لَا يَمْلِكُ الْإِبَاحَةَ وَهذَا لِاَنَّ الْمُنَافِعَ غَيْرُ قَابِلَةٍ لِلْمِلْكِ لِكَوْنِهَا مَعْدُومَةً وَإِنَّمَا جَعَلْنَاهَا مَوْجُوْدَةً فِى الْإِجَارَةِ لِلضَّرُورَةِ وَقَدْ انْدَفَعَتْ بِالْإِبَاحَةِ هَهُنَا وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ هُوَ تَمْلِيْكُ الْمَنَافِعِ عَلَى مَا ذَكَرْنَا فَيَمْلِكُ الْإِعَارَةَ كَالْمُؤْعِى لَهُ بِالْخِدْمَةِ وَالْمَنَافِعُ اعْتَبِرَتْ قَابِلَةً لِلْمِلْكِ فِي الْإِجَارَةِ فَتَجْعَلُ كَذلِكَ فِي الْإِعَارَةِ دَفْعًا لِلْحَاجَةِ وَإِنَّمَا لَا يَجُوزُ فِيمَا يَخْتَلِفُ بِاخْتِلَافِ الْمُسْتَعْمِلِ دَفْعًا لِمَزِيدِ الضَّرَرِ عَنِ الْمُعِيرِ لِأَنَّهُ رَضِيَ بِاسْتِعْمَالِهِ لَا بِإِسْتِعْمَالِ خَيْرِهِ
And he may lend it if it does not vary with variation of the user. Al-Shafi'i said: He may not lend it because it is an ibahah (permission) of benefits as we explained earlier, and the one to whom something is made permissible does not own the permission. And this is because benefits are not susceptible to ownership due to their non-existence, and we only consider them existent in ijarah out of necessity, and that necessity is removed here by ibahah. And we say: It is tamlik (ownership transfer) of benefits as we stated, so he owns the right to lend, like the one for whom service is bequeathed. And benefits are considered susceptible to ownership in ijarah, so they are similarly considered in ijarah to fulfill a need. And it is not permitted in what varies with variation of the user, to prevent additional harm to the lender, because he consented to the borrower's use, not to the use of another.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether the borrower (musta'ir) of an item can lend that item to a third party. The Hanafi position, stated in the matn, is that he may, provided the item's utility does not change with different users (e.g., riding a horse, using a tool). Imam al-Shafi'i opposes this, arguing that 'ariyah is merely a permission (ibahah) of benefits, and the one who receives permission cannot pass it on. Shafi'i also argues that benefits are non-existent and thus cannot be owned; they are considered owned in ijarah only due to necessity, and that necessity is met by the original permission. The Hanafi response affirms that 'ariyah is a transfer of ownership (tamlik) of benefits, as established at the beginning of the book. Therefore, the borrower, having become owner of the benefits, can transfer that ownership to another. This is analogous to a person for whom the service of a slave is bequeathed; he can authorize another to receive that service. The Hanafis further argue that benefits are considered susceptible to ownership in ijarah, and the same consideration applies in 'ariyah to fulfill a need. However, the permission is restricted: if the item's use varies significantly with the user (e.g., a skilled vs. unskilled rider), then lending is not allowed to prevent additional harm to the lender, who only consented to the borrower's specific use.

Key Terms
إِبَاحَةُ الْمَنَافِعِ (ibāḥatu al-manāfiʿ): The view that 'ariyah is merely a permission to benefit from an item, not a transfer of ownership of benefits.
تَمْلِيكُ الْمَنَافِعِ (tamlīku al-manāfiʿ): The Hanafi position that the borrower is given ownership of the benefits, allowing him to lend or even hire out the item within limits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why may the borrower lend the borrowed item to another person?
A) Because 'ariyah is a permission (ibahah) that can be passed on.
B) Because 'ariyah is an ownership transfer (tamlik) of benefits, so the borrower owns them and can transfer them.
C) Because Imam al-Shafi'i also allows it.
D) Because the item is owned by the borrower during the loan period.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits the borrower to lend the borrowed item when the use does not vary, based on 'ariyah being a transfer of ownership of benefits, not mere permission.

The Four Types of Ariyah (Loan) by Time and Use
Classification of loans by restrictions on time and use

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify an 'ariyah agreement into one of four types based on restrictions on time and use, and determine the borrower's rights and limits in each type.

Core Idea
A loan can be absolute or restricted in time and use; the borrower must follow restrictions but may switch to similar or better use.

The Hanafi jurists have classified the lawful loan (ariyah) into four categories based on whether the lender specifies a particular time or manner of use. Understanding these types helps both lender and borrower know their rights and obligations. This lesson unpacks the classification and the rules that apply when the borrower wishes to deviate from the specified terms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four possible combinations
Time and use can each be either unrestricted (mutlaq) or restricted (muqayyad). That gives four types: (1) unrestricted time and unrestricted use, (2) restricted both, (3) restricted time only, (4) restricted use only.
The source text lists three types; the fourth is implied by the binary logic.
2
Apply the rule for each type
For each type, state the borrower's flexibility: in type 1 he can use any time any way; type 2 he must adhere; type 3 he can use any way within the time; type 4 he can use any time but only in the specified way.
The exception for type 2: he may switch to a similar or better use.
3
Interpret the exception
If the borrower changes to something similar (e.g., wheat for wheat) or better (less harmful), it is permitted even if not explicitly allowed, because the underlying benefit is preserved without harming the lender.
This exception is based on preventing loss and adhering to the spirit of the loan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ وَهَذَا إِذَا صَدَرَتِ الْإِعَارَةُ مُطْلَقَةٌ وَهِيَ عَلَى أَرْبَعَةِ أَوْجُهِ أَحَدُهَا أَنْ يَكُونَ مُطْلَقَةً فِي الْوَقْتِ وَالْانْتِفَاعِ فَلِلْمُسْتَعِيْرِ فِيْهِ أَنْ يَنْتَفِعَ بِهِ أَيَّ نَوْعِ شَاءَ فِي اَتِ وَقْتٍ شَاءَ عَمَلًا بِالْإِطْلَاقِ وَالثَّانِي اَنْ تَكُونَ مُقَيَّدَةً فِيهِمَا فَلَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يُجَاوِزَ فِيهِ مَا سَمَّاهُ عَمَلًا بِالتَّقْدِ إِلَّا إِذَا كَانَ خِلَافًا إِلَى مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ أوْ خَيْرَ مِنْهُ وَالْحِنْطَةِ مِثْلُ الْحِنْطَةِ وَالثَّالِثُ اَنْ تَكُونَ مُقَيَّدَةً فِى حَقَّ الْوَقْتِ مُطْلَقَةٌ فِي حَقِّ الْانْتِفَاعِ
He (the author), may Allah be pleased with him, said: And this applies when the loan is absolute. And it is of four types: First: that it is absolute in time and use, so the borrower may benefit with it in any way he wishes and at any time he wishes, acting on the absoluteness. Second: that it is restricted in both, so he may not exceed what was specified, acting on the restriction, unless he changes to something similar or better, and wheat is like wheat. Third: that it is restricted in time but absolute in use.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage defines the four types of 'ariyah based on whether the lender imposes restrictions on the time of use and the type of use. The classification is rational: time can be absolute or restricted, and use can be absolute or restricted, yielding four combinations. The first type is unrestricted in both, giving the borrower full freedom in time and manner of benefit. The second is restricted in both, so the borrower must adhere to the specified time and use; however, he may switch to a use that is similar or better (e.g., using a horse for riding instead of carrying goods, if riding is similar or less harmful). The third is restricted in time but unrestricted in use, so the borrower can use the item in any way within the given time. The fourth (mentioned in the following lines) is unrestricted in time but restricted in use. These classifications guide the rights and limits of the borrower.

Key Terms
مُطْلَقَة (muṭlaqah): Unrestricted, i.e., the loan agreement does not specify a particular time or particular manner of use.
مُقَيَّدَة (muqayyadah): Restricted, i.e., the loan agreement specifies a particular time or particular use (or both).
أَرْبَعَة أَوْجُه (arba‘ah awjuh): Four types (of ariyah) based on the binary of time and use restrictions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the second type of 'ariyah (restricted in both time and use), what can the borrower do if he wants to use the item in a way different from the specified use?
A) He may use it in any way because the loan is absolute.
B) He may only use it in the exact way specified, no exception.
C) He may use it in a way that is similar or better (i.e., less harmful or equally beneficial).
D) He must return the item immediately.

Key Takeaway
The four types of ariyah are defined by whether time and use are restricted, and the borrower may only deviate from a restriction if the change is to something similar or better.

Ruling on Sub-Lending the Borrowed Item to Another
Dispute on borrower lending borrowed item to third party

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on sub-lending a borrowed item and explain the legal reasoning behind it.

Core Idea
The borrower owns the benefits and can transfer them; the opposition sees only permission, not ownership.

This passage presents a key dispute between the Hanafi school and others over whether a borrower can lend a borrowed item to a third party. The Hanafis argue that 'ariyah is an ownership of benefits, not mere permission, thus the borrower can transfer that ownership. However, the Shafi'i and Hanbali schools consider it only a permission, prohibiting sub-lending. Let's examine the arguments.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Clearly state what the Hanafi school holds regarding sub-lending a borrowed item. What is the condition for permissibility?
The condition is that the benefit (manfa'ah) must not be altered harmfully.
2
Identify the opposing schools and their views
Which schools disagree with the Hanafi position? What is their ruling and why?
Imam Shafi'i (in one narration) and Imam Ahmad prohibit; Imam Malik and another narration of Shafi'i allow.
3
Follow the opposing proof
What is the evidence that the opponents use to argue their case?
They argue that 'ariyah is ibaha (permission), and permission cannot be extended to others.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How do the Hanafis refute the opponent's proof? What is their alternative interpretation of 'ariyah?
Hanafis counter that 'ariyah is tamlik (ownership) of benefits, as established in the text, and ownership allows transfer.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference between the two positions in a real-life scenario?
Hanafis allow sub-lending if no harm; others disallow it entirely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لئے جائز نہیں تا کہ معیر سے ضرر زائد دور ہو۔ کیونکہ وہ مستغیر کے استعمال سے راضی ہوا ہے نہ کہ اس کے غیر کے استعمال سے ۔ تشریح قوله وله ان يعيره .. الخ جو چیزیں اختلاف مستعمل سے مختلف نہیں ہوتیں۔ یعنی ان میں کوئی فرق نہیں آتا۔ جیسے جانور پر بوجھ لادنا، غلام سے خدمت لینا، زمین میں کاشت کرنا ، مکان میں سکونت و ر ہائش کرنا وغیرہ تو ایسی چیزیں مستعیر دوسرے کو عاریت دے سکتا ہے امام مالک اور ایک قول میں امام شافعی بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ امام شافعی کے دوسرے قول میں اس کی اجازت نہیں امام احمد بھی اس کے قائل ہیں۔ کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک امارہ میں منافع کی اباحت ہوتی ہے اور جس شخص کے لئے کوئی چیز مباح کی جائے وہ اس کو دوسرے کے لئے مباح کرنے کا مجاز نہیں اس لئے کہ منافع بالفعل موجود نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے قابل ملک نہیں ہیں اور اجارہ میں جو ان کو موجود مانا گیا ہے وہ ضرورت کی وجہ سے ہے اور عاریت میں یہ ضرورت مباح کرنے کے ذریعہ سے مندفع ہو جاتی ہے۔ فلا يصار الى التمليك
قوله ونحن نقول ... الخ ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ عقد عاریت تو تملیک منافع کا نام ہے نہ کہ ان کی اباحت کا ۔ جیسا کہ ہم نے کتاب العاریہ کے شروع میں ذکر کیا ہے اور جب معیر نے مستعغیر کو عاریت کے منافع کا مالک بنادیا تو وہ دوسرے کو مالک بنا سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ ٹی اپنے مثل کو تضمن ہوتی ہے جیسے اگر کسی نے اپنے غلام کی خدمت کی وصیت کی تو وہ خدمت کے کئے دوسرے کو دے سکتا ہے۔ رہا امام شافعی کا یہ کہنا کہ منافع بالفعل
قابل ملک نہیں ہیں۔ سواس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ منافع اجارہ میں بھی قابل ملک نہیں ہیں۔ لیکن جیسے ان کو بوجہ ضرورت اجارہ میں قابلِ ملک قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ ایسے ہی اعادہ میں بھی قابل ملک ٹھرایا جائے گا۔ لیکن اس جواب کا حاصل اجارہ پر قیاس ہے۔ حالانکہ ایام شافعی " وقد اندفعت بالا باحتہ کہہ کر اس کا تدارک پہلے ہی کر چکے۔ پس جواب تام نہ ہوا۔ الا یہ کہ یوں کہا جائے کہ جیسے لوگوں کو اشیاء سے خود نفع اٹھانے کی احتیاج ہے۔ ایسی ہی ان سے دوسروں کو نفع پہنچانے کی بھی احتیاج ہے اور اعادہ کی اباحت ہونے کی صورت میں ان کا یہ دوسری ضرورت پوری نہیں ہوتی۔ اس لئے عاریت میں بھی منافع کو قابل ملک ٹھرایا گیا۔
قوله وانما لا يجوز..... الخ سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔
سوال یہ ہے کہ جب عاریت تملیک منافع کا نام ہے تو پھر مستعمل کے اختلاف وعدم اختلاف سے حکم مختلف نہیں ہونا چاہئے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ حکم کا اختلاف اس لئے ہے تا کہ معیر کوز اند ضر ر لاحق نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ وہ مستغیر کے استعمال سے راضی ہوا ہے نہ کہ اس کے استعمال سے۔ مثلاً زید نے بکر کو اپنا گھوڑا عاریت اس لئے دیا کہ اس کو سوار ہونا اچھی طرح آتا ہے اور بکر نے وہ خالد کو عاربیت دے دیا۔ پس اگر خالد بھی اچھی طرح سواری جانتا ہو تو جائز ہوگا۔ کیونکہ دونوں کے استعمال سے کوئی ضرر نہیں ورنہ جائز نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنی نادانی سے گھوڑے کو نقصان پہنچائے گا۔
Not allowed so that extra harm from the lender is removed. Because he consented to the borrower's use, not to another's use. Commentary on His statement: 'And he has the right to lend it to another...' etc. Items that do not differ with different users — meaning no difference arises. Like loading an animal, taking service from a slave, cultivating land, residing in a house, etc. — such things the borrower can lend to another. Imam Malik and in one narration Imam Shafi'i also hold this view. In another narration of Imam Shafi'i, it is not allowed; Imam Ahmad also holds it not allowed. Because according to them, in a loan (ariyah) there is permission (ibaha) of benefits, and a person for whom something is made permissible cannot make it permissible for another, because benefits are not ownable due to not actually existing, and in hire (ijara) they are considered existing due to necessity, and in ariyah this necessity is fulfilled by making permissible, so ownership is not resorted to. "And we say..." etc. We say that the contract of ariyah is ownership of benefits, not their permissibility, as we mentioned at the beginning of the Book of Ariyah. And when the lender made the borrower owner of the benefits of the loan, he can make another owner. Because each thing implies its like, just as if someone bequeathed the service of his slave, he can give that service to another. As for Imam Shafi'i's saying that benefits are not actually ownable, its answer is that benefits are also not ownable in ijara, but just as they are considered ownable in ijara due to necessity, similarly in ariyah they are deemed ownable. But the gist of this answer is analogy on ijara, whereas Imam Shafi'i already preempted this by saying "it was removed by permissibility." So the answer is not complete. Unless it is said that just as people need to benefit from things themselves, similarly they need to benefit others from them, and if ariyah is permissibility, this second need is not fulfilled. Therefore, in ariyah benefits are deemed ownable. "And why it is not permissible..." etc. This is the answer to an implied question. The question is: When ariyah is ownership of benefits, then the ruling should not differ based on whether the user is the same or different. The gist of the answer is that the ruling differs so that no harm befalls the lender, because he consented to the borrower's use, not to someone else's use. For example, Zayd gave his horse on loan to Bakr because he knows how to ride well, and Bakr gave it on loan to Khalid. If Khalid also knows how to ride well, it is permissible, because there is no harm from either's use; otherwise it is not permissible, because he will damage the horse through his ignorance.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether a borrower (musta'ir) can lend the borrowed item to a third party without the lender's permission. The Hanafi position permits such sub-lending when the benefit (manfa'ah) is not affected by the difference in users — for example, loading an animal, employing a slave for service, cultivating land, or residing in a house. Imam Malik and one narration of Imam Shafi'i agree with this ruling. However, another narration of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad prohibit it. The basis of the opposing view is that 'ariyah is merely a permission (ibaha) of benefits, not ownership (tamlik). Since benefits are not actual existing things, they cannot be owned; the owner only permits the borrower to use them, and one who has mere permission cannot transfer that permission to someone else. The Hanafis respond that 'ariyah is indeed ownership of benefits, as established at the beginning of the Book of 'Ariyah. Once the lender (mu'ir) makes the borrower owner of the benefits, the borrower can transfer that ownership to another, because ownership implies the right to transfer. This is supported by analogy with ijara (hire), where benefits are considered ownable due to necessity. The same necessity exists in 'ariyah: people need both to benefit personally and to benefit others. If 'ariyah were mere ibaha, this secondary need would not be fulfilled. The passage then addresses a hidden question: since 'ariyah is ownership, why does the permissibility of sub-lending depend on the identity of the sub-borrower? The answer is to avoid harm to the lender. For instance, if a lender lends his horse specifically to a skilled rider, the borrower cannot sub-lend it to an unskilled rider who might damage it. If the sub-borrower is similarly skilled, it is permissible.

Key Terms
عارية ('āriyah): A contract where the lender (mu'ir) permits the borrower (musta'ir) to use something without compensation.
تمليك المنافع (tamlik al-manāfi'): Transfer of ownership of benefits, as opposed to mere permission to use.
إباحة (ibāḥah): Permission without transfer of ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when can a borrower (musta'ir) lend the borrowed item to another person?
A) Only with the lender's explicit permission
B) Whenever the item is not consumable
C) When the mode of use does not differ harmfully between users
D) Never, because 'ariyah is only permission

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits sub-lending a borrowed item provided the benefit remains unchanged and no harm results to the lender.

The Four Types of 'Ariyah: Time and Use Restrictions
Classification of 'Ariyah into four categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four types of 'Ariyah based on time and mode of use, and state the borrower's rights and limits in each type.

Core Idea
Absolute permission does not allow unlimited change after use begins; restrictions bind unless switching to an equivalent.

The Hanafi school classifies the gratuitous loan (ʿĀriyah) into four logical types depending on whether the time and the mode of use are specified or left unrestricted. This classification determines how much freedom the borrower has and when liability arises. The following passage from al-Hidayah introduces these four types with a practical example involving a borrowed animal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Four Logical Combinations
Note that the contract can be either absolute or restricted in two dimensions: time (waqt) and mode of use (intifāʿ). The four combinations are: both absolute; both restricted; time restricted but use absolute; time absolute but use restricted.
2
Understand the Ruling for Each Type
For each type, the borrower must act according to the specification. Absolute gives maximum freedom; restricted binds him to the stated limits. An exception: he may switch to something similar or better (mithl or khayr).
The example of wheat (al-ḥinṭah) illustrates that replacing wheat with wheat is permissible because it is equivalent.
3
Apply the Principle to the Animal Example
When the loan is absolute and no specific use is mentioned, the borrower may load or ride, and may even let others use the animal. However, once he personally performs a specific use (e.g., rides himself), that use becomes fixed for him, and he cannot then let another ride without becoming liable.
This shows that absolute permission allows specification by action.
4
Note the Consequence of Overstepping
If the borrower exceeds the restrictions or changes the specified use after it has been fixed, he becomes liable (ḍāmin) for any damage or loss.
Liability arises because the borrower has violated the terms of the trust (amānah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عاریت کے اقسام اربعہ کی تشریح
قَالَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ وَهَذَا إِذَا صَدَرَتِ الْإِعَارَةُ مُطْلَقَةٌ وَهِيَ عَلَى أَرْبَعَةِ أَوْجُهِ أَحَدُهَا أَنْ يَكُونَ مُطْلَقَةٌ فِي الْوَقْتِ وَالْانْتِفَاعِ فَلِلْمُسْتَعِيْرِ فِيْهِ أَنْ يَنْتَفِعَ بِهِ أَيَّ نَوْعِ شَاءَ فِي اَتِ وَقْتٍ شَاءَ عَمَلًا بِالْإِطْلَاقِ وَالثَّانِي اَنْ تَكُونَ مُقَيَّدَةً فِيهِمَا فَلَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يُجَاوَزَ فِيهِ مَا سَمَّاهُ عَمَلًا بِالتَّقْدِ إِلَّا إِذَا كَانَ خِلَافًا إِلَى مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ أوْ خَيْرَ مِنْهُ وَالْحِنْطَةِ مِثْلُ الْحِنْطَةِ وَالثَّالِثُ اَنْ تَكُونَ مُقَيَّدَةً فِى حَقَّ الْوَقْتِ مُطْلَقَةٌ فِي حَقِّ الْانْتِفَاع
وَالرَّابِعُ عَكْسُهُ لَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يَتَعَدَّى مَا سَمَّاهُ فَلَوِ اسْتَعَارَ دَابَّةٌ وَلَمْ يُسَمِّ شَيْئًا لَهُ أَنْ يَحْمِلَ وَيُعِيرَ غَيْرَهُ لِلْحِمْلِ لَاتَ الْحِمْلَ لَا يَتَفَاوَتُ وَلَهُ اَنْ يَرْكَبَ وَيُرْكِبَ غَيْرَهُ وَإِنْ كَانَ الرُّكُوبُ مُخْتَلِفًا لِأَنَّهُ لَمَّا أَطْلَقَ فِيهِ فَلَهُ أَنْ يُعَيِّنَ حَتَّى لَوْ رَكِبَ بِنَفْسِهِ لَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يُرْكِبَ غَيْرَهُ لِأَنَّهُ تَعَيَّنَ رُكُوبُهُ وَلَوْ أَرْكَبَ غَيْرَهُ لَيْسَ لَهُ أَنْ يَرْكَبَهُ حَتْ ــلَهُ ضَمِنَ لأَنَّهُ تَعَيَّنَ الْأَرْكَابَ
ترجمہ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ اس وقت ہے جب اعادہ مطلقہ واقع ہوا ہو اور یہ چار تم پر ہے۔ ایک یہ کہ اعادہ مطلق ہو وقت اور انفاع میں اس صورت میں مستغیر کو اختیار ہے کہ اس سے نفع اٹھائے جس قسم کا چاہے اور جس وقت چاہے اطلاق پر عمل کرتے ہوئے ۔ دوم یہ کہ وقت اور انتفاع دونوں میں موید ہو۔ پس اس میں بیان کردہ سے تجاوز کرنے کا اختیار نہیں تقیید پر عمل کرتے ہوئے مگر جب کہ مخالف اس کے مثل یا اس سے بہتر کی طرف ہو۔ اور گیہوں مثل گیہوں کے ہے۔ سوم یہ کہ وقت کے حق میں مقید اور انفاع کے حق میں مطلق ہو ۔ چہارم اس کا عکس ہے اور اس کو اختیار نہیں کہ اس کے بیان کردہ سے تجاوز کرے۔ پس اگر چوپایہ مستعار لیا اور کوئی چیز بیان نہیں کی تو اس کو اختیار ہے کہ اپنی چیز لادے یا دوسرے کولادنے کے لئے عاریت دے دے۔ کیونکہ لادنا متفاوت نہیں ہوتا اور اختیار ہے کہ خود سوار ہو یا دوسرے کو سوار کرے اگر رکزب مختلف ہوتا ہے اس لئے کہ جب اس نے مطلق اجازت دے دی تو اس کو معین کرنے کا اختیار ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر خود سوار ہو گیا۔ تو دوسرے کو سوار نہیں کرسکتا۔ کیو نکہ اس کی سواری متعین ہوگئی اور دوسرے کو سوار کیا تو خود سوار نہیں ہو سکتا۔ اگر ایسا کیا تو ضامن ہوگا۔ کیونکہ سوار کر نا متعین ہو گیا۔
Explanation of the four divisions of 'Ariyah.
He (may Allah be pleased with him) said: This is when the loan is given absolutely, and it is of four types. First: it is absolute in time and mode of use; then the borrower may use it in any manner and at any time he wishes, acting upon the absolute nature. Second: it is restricted in both; then he may not exceed what was specified, acting upon the restriction, except if he changes to something similar or better. Wheat is like wheat. Third: it is restricted in time but absolute in mode of use. Fourth: the opposite (absolute in time, restricted in mode); he may not exceed what was specified. So if he borrows an animal and does not specify anything, he may load it and lend it to another for loading, because loading does not vary. And he may ride it and let another ride it, even though riding may differ; because when he gave absolute permission, he has the right to specify. Consequently, if he rides himself, he may not let another ride, because his riding has become specified. And if he lets another ride, he may not ride himself; if he does, he is liable, because the riding of another has become specified.
Translation: The author of Hidayah states that this is when the loan is absolute, and it is of four types: First, the loan is absolute in time and use; in this case, the borrower may benefit in any way and at any time, acting upon the absolute nature. Second, it is restricted in both; so he may not exceed what was stated, acting upon the restriction, unless he changes to something similar or better. Wheat is like wheat. Third, it is restricted in time but absolute in use. Fourth, the opposite (absolute in time, restricted in use); he may not exceed what was specified. So if he borrows an animal and does not specify anything, he may load his own item or lend it to another for loading, because loading does not differ. And he may ride himself or let another ride, even though riding differs, because when absolute permission was given, he has the right to specify. Thus, if he rides himself, he cannot let another ride, because his riding has become specified. And if he lets another ride, he cannot ride himself; if he does, he is liable, because riding by another has become specified.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage defines the four logical types of the 'Ariyah (gratuitous loan) contract based on whether the time (waqt) and mode of use (intifa') are specified or left unrestricted. The classification is inherent to the nature of the contract, giving four categories. First type: both time and use are absolute. The borrower may use the object in any lawful way at any time. Second type: both are restricted. The borrower must adhere to the specified time and use and cannot exceed them, unless he switches to something equivalent or better (e.g., replacing wheat with wheat or with a less harmful grain). Third type: time restricted, use absolute. The borrower must use it within the specified time but can choose any mode of use. Fourth type: time absolute, use restricted. The borrower can use it at any time but only in the specified manner. The passage also illustrates with an example of borrowing an animal without specifying anything: the borrower may load it or lend it for loading (since loading does not vary in harm), and may ride it or let another ride (though riding quality varies, absolute permission allows the borrower to choose). However, once the borrower specifies his own use (e.g., rides himself), that specific use becomes fixed, and he cannot then change to another user. If he does, he becomes liable (damin) for damage.

Key Terms
مطلقة (muṭlaqah): Absolute loan without restriction on time or mode of use.
مقيدة (muqayyadah): Loan with restrictions on time, use, or both.
الحنطة (al-ḥinṭah): Wheat; used as example of a commodity that is uniform in quality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which type of ʿĀriyah may the borrower use the object in any manner and at any time?
A) Restricted in both time and use
B) Absolute in both time and use
C) Restricted in time, absolute in use
D) Absolute in time, restricted in use

Key Takeaway
The borrower's rights in ʿĀriyah depend on the type of restrictions; absolute permission does not allow unlimited change once a specific use is actualized.

intermediate

Borrower's Right to Lend the Borrowed Item
Critical refinement of Al-Hidayah on borrower's right to lend

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a borrower's right to sub-lend and distinguish between absolute and restricted loans when determining permissibility.

Core Idea
Whether a borrower may lend the borrowed item depends on the terms — absolute gives broad authority, restricted limits it.

This passage refines a key principle from Al-Hidayah about the borrower's authority to lend. The commentator resolves an apparent inconsistency by clarifying the distinction between absolute and restricted loans, and the relevance of whether the benefit varies among users.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two loan types
Distinguish between an absolute loan (i'ārah muṭlaqah) — no restriction on user or use — and a restricted loan (i'ārah muqayyadah) — limited to the borrower's personal use.
The restriction can be explicit or implicit from context.
2
Apply the rule for absolute loans
If the loan is absolute, the borrower may lend to anyone for any purpose, regardless of whether the benefit varies among users. The general wording of the contract grants this authority.
This is based on the literal meaning and custom.
3
Apply the rule for restricted loans
If the loan is restricted to personal use, the borrower may only lend items where the benefit does not vary (e.g., loading). For variable-benefit items (e.g., wearing, riding), sub-lending is not allowed.
The reason: the owner's intention was for personal benefit, and sub-lending a variable-benefit item violates that intention.
4
Understand the Shafi'i opposition
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the borrower cannot sub-lend without explicit permission, as the borrowed item is a trust (amānah) that cannot be transferred.
The Hanafi response: absolute loan implies permission to sub-lend because the owner's trust extends to the borrower's judgment.
5
Apply to scenarios
Test your understanding: if a friend gives you his car with 'use it as you wish' (absolute), you may lend it. If he says 'for your own trip' (restricted), you cannot lend it for another's trip, but you can lend it for loading cargo if the benefit does not vary.
The key is whether the benefit (manfa'ah) varies among users.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیہ صاحب ہدایہ کے قول و هذا اذا صدرت اھ میں غذا کا مشار الیہ کیا ہے؟ عام شراح نے کہا ہے ۔ ای ما ذكر من ولايته الاعارة للمستعير ۔ اس پر یہ اشکال ہوتا ہے کہ سابق میں جو مذکور ہے وہ یہ ہے وله ان يعيرهه اذن كان ممالا يختلف با اختلاف المستعمل " پس مطلب یہ ہوا کہ جو چیزیں اختلاف مستعمل سے مختلف نہیں ہوتیں۔ ان میں مستعغیر کو عاریت پر دینے کا اختیار اس وقت ہے جب اعارہ مطلقہ ہو ۔ حالانکہ عام کتب فقہ میں حتیٰ کہ متون میں بھی یہ بات صریح ثابت ہے ۔ کہ اختلاف مستعمل سے مختلف نہ ہونے والی چیزوں میں عاریت پر دینے کا اختیار اس وقت ہے جب اعارہ اس قید کے ساتھ مقید ہو کہ اس سے خود مستعغیر فائدہ اٹھائے گا۔ اگر یہ قید نہ ہو بلکہ مطلق ہو تو مستغیر کو علی الاطلاق عاریت پر دینے کا اختیار ہے۔ خواہ وہ چیز اختلاف مستعمل سے مختلف ہوتی ہو یا نہ ہوتی ہو ۔ خود صاحب ہدایہ نے بھی مسئلہ کے اخیر میں اس کی تصریح کی ہے۔ حیث قال : فلو استعار دابته ولم يسم شيئاله ان يحمل ويعير غيره للحمل لان الحمل لا يتفاوت وله ان يركب ويُركب غيره وان كان الركوب مختلفاً پس ہذا کا مشار الیہ جو عام شراح نے ذکر کیا ہے اسی وقت صحیح ہوسکتا تھا جب کلام سابق ۔ ’اذان كـان مـمـالا يـخـتـلـف بـا ختلاف المستعمل “ کے ساتھ مقید نہ ہوتا اس لئے انصاف کی بات یہ ہے کہ اگر صاحب ہدایہ اپنے قول وهذا اذا صدرت الاعارة مطلقت “ کو حذف کر کے یوں کہتے ۔ والاعارة على اربعة اوجه اھ تو بہتر ہوتا۔
اس مقام پر صاحب کافی کا طر زتحریر بہت عمدہ ہے کہ موصوف نے اوّلاً وله ان یعیر “ کہہ کر امام شافعی کا اختلاف ذکر کر کے جانبین کی دلیل بیان کرنے کے بعد کہا ہے۔
ثم هذه المسئله على وجهين اما ان حصلت الا عادة مطلقة في حق المنتفع بان اعا ثوباً للبس ولم يبين اللابس او دابة للركوب ولم يبين الراكب اودابة للحمل ولم يبين الحامل وفي هذا لوجه له ان يعير سواء كان المستعار شيئًا يتفاوت الناس فى الانتفاع به كاللبس في الثوب والركوب في الدابة اولا يتفاوتون فى الاتنفاوع كالحمل على الدابة عملا با طلاق اللفظ وان حصلت الاعارة مقيدة بان استعار ليلبس بنفسه او ليحمل بنفسه فله ان يعير فيما لا يتفاوت الناس في الانتفاع به كما في الحمل وليس له ان يعير فيما يتفاوت الناس فى الانتفاع به كا للبس والركوب ثم قال : وهذا اهو الكلام فى اعارة المستعير واما الكلام في انتفاعه فى المستعار فهو اربة اوجه اهـ
Admonition: What does the author of Al-Hidayah refer to by his statement 'and this is when the loan is absolute'? The general commentators said: it refers to what was mentioned regarding his authority to lend out to the borrower. An objection arises: what was mentioned earlier is 'he has the right to lend it if it is something that does not vary with the difference of users.' So the meaning is that in things that do not vary with different users, the borrower has the authority to lend it out only when the loan was absolute. Whereas in the general books of fiqh, even the texts, it is explicitly established that in things that do not vary with different users, the borrower has the authority to lend it out only when the loan was restricted to the condition that the borrower himself will benefit. If there is no such restriction but it is absolute, then the borrower has absolute authority to lend it out, whether the item varies with users or not. The author of Al-Hidayah himself clarified this at the end of the issue where he said: 'If he borrows his riding animal and does not specify anything, he may load and lend it to others for loading because loading does not differ; and he may ride and let others ride even though riding differs.' So the referent of 'this' that the general commentators mentioned could only be correct if the earlier statement was not restricted by 'when it is something that does not vary with the difference of users.' Therefore, the fair thing is that if the author of Al-Hidayah had omitted his statement 'and this is when the loan is absolute' and said 'the loan is of four types', it would have been better. At this point, the style of the author of Al-Kafi is excellent. He first said 'he has the right to lend it' and mentioned the difference with Imam al-Shafi'i, giving proofs from both sides, then said: 'This issue has two aspects: either the loan is absolute in terms of the beneficiary, such as giving a garment for wearing without specifying the wearer, or a riding animal for riding without specifying the rider, or an animal for loading without specifying the loader. In this aspect, he has the right to lend it, whether the borrowed thing varies among people in benefiting from it, like wearing a garment or riding an animal, or does not vary, like loading on an animal, acting on the generality of the wording. If the loan is restricted, such as borrowing to wear oneself or to load oneself, then he has the right to lend in things where people do not vary in benefiting, as in loading, but not in things where people vary, like wearing and riding.' Then he said: 'This is the discussion on the borrower's lending. As for the discussion on his own benefit from the borrowed item, it is of four aspects.'
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hāshiya-style) on Al-Hidayah. The commentator identifies an inconsistency in the wording of Al-Hidayah regarding the borrower's right to lend the borrowed item. The earlier part of Al-Hidayah (not fully shown here) states that the borrower may lend the item to another if the item does not vary with different users, apparently conditioned on the loan being absolute (unrestricted). However, the consensus in Hanafi texts is different: if the loan is absolute (muṭlaqah), the borrower may lend to anyone regardless of whether the item varies; if the loan is restricted to the borrower's personal use (muqayyadah), then he may only lend items where the benefit does not vary (e.g., loading vs. riding). The commentator praises Al-Kāfī for its clear exposition: it divides the issue into two scenarios (absolute vs. restricted loan) and explains the rulings clearly. Important: The Hanafi position is that the borrower's authority to lend depends on the terms of the original loan, not just the nature of the item. This is a nuance that earlier commentators missed.

Key Terms
اعارہ مطلقہ (i'ārah muṭlaqah): A loan contract without any restriction on the borrower's usage or identity of user.
اعارہ مقیدہ (i'ārah muqayyadah): A loan restricted to a specific use or user, e.g., 'for your own wearing'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under Hanafi fiqh, when can a borrower lend a borrowed riding animal to another person for riding?
A) Always, because riding is a common benefit.
B) Only if the loan was absolute, because riding varies among people.
C) Never, because riding requires explicit permission.
D) Only if the animal is not needed by the owner.

Key Takeaway
The borrower's authority to sub-lend hinges on whether the loan was absolute or restricted, and whether the item's benefit varies among users.

Borrowing Fungibles is a Loan (Qard)
Ruling with proof and exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on borrowing consumable fungibles, explain the legal reasoning, and identify the exception for specified non-consumptive use.

Core Idea
Borrowing something you must consume makes it a loan, not a bailment.

When you borrow something like a book, you return the same book. But what if you borrow food or coins? You cannot return the same ones. The Hanafi school clarifies that such a borrowing is legally a loan (qard), not a loan for use (i'arah). This lesson unpacks the reasoning and an important exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the first sentence: the borrowing of dirhams, dinars, and similar fungibles is qard.
2
Understand the first proof
The author argues that i'arah transfers benefits, but these items can only be used by consuming them, so the substance must be transferred. That happens through hibah or qard, and qard is the lesser obligation.
This is a qiyas based on the nature of the contracts.
3
Understand the second proof
Another angle: The essence of i'arah requires returning the specific item. Since that's impossible, returning an equivalent is substituted, which is qard.
This reinforcement shows the legal necessity.
4
Note the exception
If the borrower specifies a non-consumptive purpose (e.g., using coins for decoration), it remains a true i'arah. The borrower may only use the item for that purpose and must return the same item.
This exception is crucial for fatwa application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَعَارِيَّةُ الدَّرَاهِمِ وَالدَّنَانِيرِ وَالْمَكِيْلِ وَالْمَوْزُونِ وَالْمَعْدُودِ قَرْضٌ لِأَنَّ الْإِعَارَةَ تَمْلِيْكُ الْمَنَافِعِ وَلَا يُمْكِنُ الْانْتِفَاعُ بِهَا إِلَّا بِاسْتِهْلَاكِ عَيْنِهَا فَاقْتَضَى تَمْلِيْكَ الْعَيْنِ ضَرُورَةً وَذَالِكَ بِالْهِبَةِ أَوِ الْقَرْضِ وَالْقَرْضُ أَدْنَاهُمَا فَيَقْتُ اَوْ لَاَنَّ مِنْ قَضِيَّةِ الْإِعَارَةِ الْانْتِفَاعِ وَرَدَّ الْعَيْنِ فَأَقِيمَ رَدَّ الْمِثْلَ مَقَامَهُ قَالُوا هَذَا إِذَا أَطْلَقَ الْإِعَارَةَ أَمَّا إِذَا عَيَّنَ الْجِهَةَ بِاَنِ اسْتَعَارَ الدَّرَاهِمَ لِيُعِيرَ بِهَا مِيزَانَا اَوْ يُزَيِّنُ بِهَا دُكَانًا لَمْ تَكُنْ قَرْضًا وَلَا يَكُونُ لَهُ إِلَّا الْمَنْفَعَةُ الْمُسَمَّاهُ فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا اسْتَعَارَ آنِيَةً يَتَجَمَّلُ بِهَا أَوْ سَيْفًا مُحَلَّى يَتَقَلَّدُهَا
He said: And the loan of dirhams, dinars, measured (makīl), weighed (mawzūn), and counted (maʻdūd) items is a loan (qarḍ). Because the loan contract (iʻārah) is a transfer of ownership of benefits, and it is not possible to benefit from these except by consuming their substance. So necessity requires the transfer of ownership of the substance, and that is through gift (hibah) or loan (qarḍ). And the loan is the lesser of the two, so it is established. Or because from the requirements of the loan contract are benefiting and returning the substance. So returning the equivalent (miṯl) is placed in its stead. They said: This is when the loan is absolute. However, if the purpose is specified, like borrowing dirhams to adjust a scale with them or to decorate a shop with them, then it is not a loan, and he only has the named benefit. It becomes like borrowing a vessel for adornment or a decorated sword to wear it.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This is a ruling statement with proof. The passage establishes that when someone borrows consumable fungible items (dirhams, dinars, grain weighed or measured, eggs, nuts, etc.), the contract is legally considered a qarḍ (loan) rather than a true ʻāriyah (loan for use). The reason given is twofold: First, ʻāriyah transfers ownership of benefits (manāfiʻ), but these items cannot be used without consuming them (istihlāk al-ʻayn), so the substance must be transferred; this can be via gift or loan, and the loan is the lesser obligation. Second, the nature of ʻāriyah requires returning the very item, but since that's impossible, returning an equivalent (miṯl) is substituted, which is the essence of qarḍ. However, this ruling applies only when the loan is absolute (muṭlaqah). If the borrower specifies a purpose that does not consume the item (e.g., using dirhams as weights or decoration), then it remains a true ʻāriyah and is not qarḍ. The commentary from Ashraf al-Hidāyah adds that the scholars are nearly unanimous; only some Shafi'is consider it a fāsid (invalid) loan. The author of al-Natāʼij noted that the second reason (returning equivalent) seems empty because both the reality of ʻāriyah and its ruling are negated; the reality is negated because the condition of ʻāriyah (benefit with preservation of substance) is absent, so it is metaphorically called qarḍ; the ruling is negated because the qabīḍ (possessor) is not guilty of taʻaddī (transgression) as he is certain of the ruling due to the lesser harm (qarḍ being less harmful than hibah).

Key Terms
عارية (ʻāriyah): A loan of an item for use, with the obligation to return the specific item.
قرض (qarḍ): A loan of consumable items where the borrower returns the equivalent (miṯl) in quality and quantity.
مثلى (mithliy): Fungible items that have equivalents in the market, like grains, oils, eggs, and currencies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone borrows a kilogram of wheat without specifying a purpose, what is the legal status of the contract?
A) It is a valid i'arah (loan for use).
B) It is a qard (loan) and the borrower must return an equivalent weight of wheat.
C) It is a hibah (gift) if the wheat is consumed.
D) It is a void contract because wheat cannot be borrowed.

Key Takeaway
Borrowing consumable fungibles is qard, not i'arah, unless a non-consumptive purpose is specified.

Loan of Consumable Items: When 'Ariyah Becomes Qard
States ruling and two proofs for consumable items' loan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that an absolute loan of consumable items is treated as a qard, and identify the two proofs (dalil) and the exception when a specific non-consumptive use is specified.

Core Idea
If the use of a borrowed item necessarily consumes it, the contract becomes a qard, not 'ariyah.

When someone borrows dirhams or food items, most people assume it's a simple loan ('ariyah) — you borrow and return the same item. But Hanafi fiqh looks deeper: if the item's substance is consumed in use, the contract legally becomes a qard (loan of fungibles). This lesson unpacks the ruling and its two proofs, and explores the important exception when a specific non-consumptive purpose is stated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Identify what transaction is being discussed (loan of dirhams, dinars, measured/weighed/counted items) and the ruling: it is considered a qard, not an 'ariyah.
The ruling is categorical for such items when the loan is absolute (mutlaq).
2
Locate the first proof (dalil aqli)
The first proof is based on the definition of 'ariyah: it is a transfer of usufruct (tamlik al-manafi'). Since benefiting from a consumable item requires consuming its substance, the contract necessarily implies transfer of ownership of the substance. That can only happen through hibah or qard; qard is the lesser, so it is the default.
This is a qiyas/khiyali reasoning: the essence of the contract shifts.
3
Locate the second proof (dalil aqli)
The second proof focuses on the purpose of 'ariyah: benefit and return of the same item. Since the substance cannot be returned, the return of a similar item (mithl) is substituted, which is exactly the obligation in a qard.
This reinforces the first proof from a different angle.
4
Note the exception: specified non-consumptive use
If the borrower specifies a use that does not consume the substance (e.g., using dirhams to adjust a scale or for decoration), it remains a valid 'ariyah, not qard. The borrower may only use it for that specific purpose.
The analogy is given: like borrowing a vessel for adornment or a bejeweled sword to wear.
5
Evaluate the authority and cross-madhhab dispute
This ruling is from the zahir al-riwayah and is the mufta bihi position. Some Shafi'is consider such a transaction a fasid 'ariyah (invalid loan) rather than qard. The Hanafi view prevails due to the strength of the analogy and practical necessity.
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Hanafi law, the borrower must return the mithl; under Shafi'i, the contract is invalid and the item must be returned if still intact.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَعَارِيَّةُ الدَّرَاهِمِ وَالدَّنَانِيرِ وَالْمَكِيْلِ وَالْمَوْزُونِ وَالْمَعْدُودِ قَرْضٌ لِأَنَّ الْإِعَارَةَ تَمْلِيْكُ الْمَنَافِعِ وَلَا يُمْكِنُ الْانْتِفَاعُ بِهَا إِلَّا بِاسْتِهْلَاكِ عَيْنِهَا فَاقْتَضَى تَمْلِيْكَ الْعَيْنِ ضَرُورَةً وَذَالِكَ بِالْهِبَةِ أَوِ الْقَرْضِ وَالْقَرْضُ أَدْنَاهُمَا فَيَقْتُ [؟] أَوْ لَاَنَّ مِنْ قَضِيَّةِ الْإِعَارَةِ الْانْتِفَاعِ وَرَدَّ الْعَيْنِ فَأَقِيمَ رَدَّ الْمِثْلَ مَقَامَهُ قَالُوا هَذَا إِذَا أَطْلَقَ الْإِعَارَةَ أَمَّا إِذَا عَيَّنَ الْجِهَةَ بِاَنِ اسْتَعَارَ الدَّرَاهِمَ لِيُعِيرَ بِهَا مِيزَانَا اَوْ يُزَيِّنُ بِهَا دُكَانًا لَمْ تَكُنْ قَرْضًا وَلَا يَكُونُ لَهُ إِلَّا الْمَنْفَعَةُ الْمُسَمَّاهُ فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا اسْتَعَارَ آنِيَةً يَتَجَمَّلُ بِهَا أَوْ سَيْفًا مُحَلَّى يَتَقَلَّدُهَا
He said: The loan of dirhams, dinars, measured items, weighed items, and counted items is a qard (loan) because 'ariyah (gratuitous loan) is the ownership of usufructs, and it is not possible to benefit from them except by consuming their substance. So necessarily, this requires ownership of the substance, and that is through gift (hibah) or qard, and qard is the lesser of the two, so it is restricted to that? Or because from the requirements of 'ariyah is benefit and return of the substance, so returning a similar item is put in its place. They said: This is when the 'ariyah is absolute. As for when the purpose is specified—like he borrows dirhams to adjust a scale with them or to adorn his shop—then it is not qard, and he has only the specified usufruct, so it becomes like when one borrows a vessel for decoration or a bejeweled sword to wear as a necklace.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the loan (ariyah) of consumable items such as dirhams, dinars, and other measured, weighed, or counted items. The author states that such an 'ariyah is legally considered a qard (loan of fungible items) rather than a true 'ariyah, because the essence of 'ariyah is the transfer of usufruct (manafi'), not the substance ('ayn). However, using these items inevitably consumes their substance, so the contract effectively transfers ownership of the substance itself. This can only be achieved through hibah (gift) or qard; qard is the lesser of the two, so it is the default. A second proof is that the purpose of 'ariyah is benefit and return, but since the original substance cannot be returned, the return of a similar item (mithl) is substituted, which is exactly qard. The scholars then add a condition: this ruling applies when the 'ariyah is absolute (mutlaq). If the borrower specifies a use that does not require consumption—e.g., borrowing dirhams to use as weights or for decoration—then it remains a valid 'ariyah and not qard, and the borrower may only use it for that specified purpose. The analogy is provided: like borrowing a vessel to adorn one's home or a sword to wear as an ornament. The passage does not explicitly note the authority weight, but the base ruling (zahir al-riwayah) is standard in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الْإِعَارَة (al-‘āriyah): A gratuitous loan of a non-consumable item for its usufruct, with the obligation to return the same item.
قَرْض (qarḍ): A loan of fungible items (mithliyyat) where the borrower consumes the substance and returns a similar item (mithl).
استهلاك العين (istihlāk al-‘ayn): Consumption of the very substance of the item, such that it cannot be returned in kind.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the loan of dirhams remain a valid 'ariyah (and not become qard)?
A) When the borrower specifies a non-consumptive use, such as using them for decoration.
B) When the loan is for a short period only.
C) When the borrower promises to return the exact same dirhams.
D) It never remains 'ariyah; dirhams are always qard.

Key Takeaway
An absolute loan of any consumable fungible item is automatically reclassified as a qard contract in Hanafi law, unless a specific non-consumptive purpose is declared.
